Farewell To The Fairground

by bitchywitchyboo

Summary

“Why did you do it?” Rio had asked her, tight-lipped.

Agatha chewed on her words.

“You wanted a platform to tell the truth, now you’ve got it.”

“You could have consulted me before blowing up my entire career.”

“Darling,” she had said with a mewl. “I’ve just changed your life. Act a little more grateful.”

-- OR --

Two rival journalists, forced together as the new co-hosts of UBA's The Morning Show. What the hell could go wrong?

Chapter 1: Midnight Caller

Chapter Notes

CAN'T BELIEVE YOU'RE FINALLY READING

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness loathed falsity. 

And there was nothing worse than attending a full evening of it. 

False grins, false news, false people. 

It was the worst part of her job, having to constantly put on a smile that left her cheeks aching at the end of each day. But to have to do it of an evening too? 

She hated it. 

After fifteen years of attending the National Journalism Awards, it was not hard for her to navigate her way through the ceremony, nor the hundreds of people she was professionally obliged to converse with, no matter how dull said conversing actually was. 

But knowing and enjoying were two very different things, and Agatha certainly did not get any of the latter out of these constant awards, galas and networking events that were forced upon her. 

She could think of much, much better ways to spend her time. 

It was a night, mid-autumn, for journalists, politicians, donors and spearhead figures to come together and offer their falsest smiles to one another under the guise of celebrating those best able to uncover their lies. 

To add to the horrors, there were old, sweating men in abundance who drooled at the sight of her navy, satin dress and bared chest that unveiled the delicate lines forming violets, azaleas and roses beneath her collarbone. 

There were old colleagues at every corner who she wished she could spit into their drinks. 

There were young, bidding reporters desperate to get the scoop on her which only left her laughing in their face. “Number one rule to journalism, honey. Don’t take down your own, which is exactly what you’re trying to do right now,” she would tell them before sending them on her way.

Held in the ballroom of The Plaza Hotel, it was so grand its guests would not believe they were still amidst Manhattan. She had been there an hour and already had endured several unpleasant conversations, drank two negronis and lost one bet with her assistant about which of them would get hit on first. 

It was, unfortunately, Agatha who had gotten hit on first. 

It was only to be expected of an heir to such a powerful media dynasty. 

UBA - the United Broadcast Association - had their own table, of course. She had Wanda on her left being far too sweet, and far too accommodating to one of their ancient board members but Agatha was too focused on her mother, standing in the corner of the room speaking to none other than up-and-coming Republican, Tony Stark. 

The man had always left her unnerved. His father had been a respected politician and governor of Nevada, and she had grown up watching his son propel his father’s ideals into extremism. 

There had been rumours, in the wake of their current president’s impending cease in power, that Stark would try to run himself. 

The thought alone left a chill running up her spine. Agatha could only think of her son, and the implications on him if he were to grow up in a future dictated to him by somebody so out of touch with reality. 

Still, her job was to inform people of the truth; personal narratives were not allowed. 

The sight of her mother - CEO of UBA - fraternising with the enemy, sickened her to her stomach no less. Agatha had twenty minutes until she was due to present an award; that was enough time for two more drinks at least.. 

The bar was busy and she found herself offering crude, flat smiles to people she’d rather see behind bars than right in front of her, but when another negroni was placed in front of her, she sighed with a deep exhale. 

If only she had known, walking back, that she would come face-to-face with one of many women she would happily drop a building on. 

Pushed up against the wall of the corridor in an annoyingly-well-tailored brown, pin-striped suit, with dimpled cheeks and dark, hazel eyes that flashed up at her briefly, was Rio Vidal. 

Agatha did not like Rio Vidal. 

Agatha loathed Rio Vidal. 

An up-and-coming journalist, employed by their biggest competitors at Your Day America, more commonly known as YDA, she was nothing but a nasty piece of work. 

Rio Vidal had no problem getting dirty, just like she had no problem sinking her fellow journalists down to the ground. Most importantly of all, she had published nothing short of a smear campaign on Agatha only the month before, deep-diving into the story behind Agatha’s marriage and the wrought, legal going-on’s that occurred in her divorce. 

Agatha all but stormed over to Rio, her heel only inches from the foot of the blonde sulked up against the younger journalist. 

“Leave,” she hissed to the woman. 

She quickly realised that Rio had been flirting with a waitress. 

Once she stood face to face with Rio, blue eyes stabbed into hazel. 

“Did you think that was funny?” 

“I haven’t done anything.” 

Agatha scoffed. “Apart from deep-dive into my non-existent relationship with someone that has nothing to do with me anymore?” 

Rio tried to refrain from rolling her eyes. “You’re the one calling it a relationship.” 

“Isn’t it your whole,” Agatha imitated with her hands, “… thing, to be a transparent reporter?  Not to gossip into people’s private lives…” 

“I want to tell the truth,” Rio’s eyes hardened, aligned with her tight posture. “I’d say there is some truth to be sought after ten years of rumours about you sleeping with women, whilst having a husband that you only divorced six years ago.”

Agatha composed herself quickly, her jaw tight as she offered a flat smile. 

“Wouldn’t you like to know.” 

With that, she turned away and returned to UBA’s table. 

Fifteen minutes later, she was being prised from her seat and forced backstage to present the next award.

“Awarded for her broadcasting by the White House Correspondents Association, owner of two Pulitzer Prizes, winner of the John Chancellor Award for Excellence in Journalism, and many more, you know her as the face of UBA’s The Morning Show for the last fifteen years, please welcome to the stage… Agatha Harkness!” 

With the bronzed-statue and envelope in-hand, Agatha rolled her shoulders back and fought her inebriation as she walked onto the stage. She scoffed at the generosity of the announcement. Perhaps she should remind her employers of her many accolades; perhaps it would offer her some actual say over her career. 

The applause for her was wild and she couldn't help but soak it up as she walked out. It wasn’t like she received it in many other places in her life. 

“Good evening,” Agatha began. 

“I have lived and breathed this craft for nearly two decades - and no, that is not an invitation to call me old.” The audience laughed; she didn’t know why. It was hardly a joke. 

“Upon graduating, after final exams, journalists sign an oath. It is an oath to uphold the truth, and maintain an honest, non-biased seeking of that truth in order to bring the most transparent forms of journalism to the public that we can. With that in mind, I am here to celebrate those individuals who are paving the way for the future of investigative journalism.” 

She did not celebrate them. Each and every one of them were a pain in her ass, not to mention they would most likely be after her job in several years. Well, perhaps only one or two of them. She couldn’t offer them that much credit. 

“Here are the nominees for the Breakthrough Investigative Reporter Award.”

There was more applause as she fumbled with the envelope. 

All she could think about was, please, please don’t let it be her. 

The words laughed cruelly back at her on the card. 

Presenting Rio Vidal with the award was something she should have expected. YDA would have paid the voting body off; everyone knew it would have made spectacular press to watch Agatha Harkness present an award to somebody who had made a mockery of her. 

Still, Agatha smiled and took Rio off-stage with a gentle arm. She posed for photos with her and held her award whilst a board official offered Rio their congratulations. 

“You owe me a drink,” Agatha said in between flashes and shouts from photographers. 

Rio looked up, as if she had been startled. “Why?” 

“You’ve just won an award because you poked your nose into my private life. The least you could do is take the edge off the embarrassment you have just shoved upon me.” 

That was when she first saw Rio’s smirk. It was deep and intense and blocked any other thoughts from her mind. 

“Your private life did not get me this win,” Rio said, shaking her head. “That story just got people talking about me enough to watch my piece on the transphobia within the girl scouts.” 

“My case in point. Every person in this room is more interested in me than they are in the politics of children’s clubs, Vidal,” Agatha muttered. 

“You think everyone is more interested in you?” 

Agatha’s lips curled. “I know they are.” 

“Prove it.” 

“Tell me, what would you rather be doing right now than being here?” 

Rio thought about her answer after offering a questioning look, having no idea where Agatha was going with this conversation. “A quiet bar… Or my bed.” 

“I can’t take you to your bed,” Agatha began, her body leaning ever-so-slightly closer into Rio’s chest. “Yet,” she smirked, her hand briefly grazing Rio’s shoulder. “But there’s a nice bar across the street, if you’re interested.” 

Of course Rio was interested, and of course Agatha was proven right. 

A few hours into their bar-hop over to the Pierre Hotel, Agatha and Rio had gotten drunk to an unprofessional level. Rio was desperate for Agatha to tell her if she was straight or not, whilst Agatha spent every moment trying to keep her lips from crashing into Rio’s in such a public space. 

“Darling, I’m still waiting for you to explain exactly why you thought it was ok to bury up old skeletons of mine. Care to share? After all, I’m sure that bottle I’ve just ordered would cover half of your monthly rent.” 

Rio offered her a look that Agatha didn’t think she was capable of. Her amber eyes turned darker, wider, imploring into her own. Her cheeks drooped, her lips too as they formed into a pout. She had never taken Rio Vidal to be the type to pout. 

“So this was a ploy to get inside information, rather than inside my clothes?” 

Agatha’s lips curled. 

They sat in a secluded corner of the bar after a generous tip was offered to their waiter. It allowed the perfect anonymity for Agatha to shift closer to Rio, both of their knees touching. Her fingers found Rio’s thigh as she watched the woman shudder at the touch. Rio’s breathing became unsteady the further Agatha’s fingers trailed along her thigh. 

“You don’t think I’m capable of multi-tasking?” 

“I think you’re capable of a lot of things, but I also happen to be a visual learner.”

Agatha smirked, raising her glass. 

Her hand never left Rio’s thigh.

It took one finished bottle of wine between them before Agatha had booked them a room and Rio finally received her answer in the form of slicken skin and whimpered moans.  

Agatha left the sheets cold for Rio to wake up next to. 

They were two of the same kind, but polar opposite in every way. They didn’t need to be anything more than a shared night together.

Chapter 2: Jump Into The Fire

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Three weeks after the awards ceremony, Agatha’s alarm rang out at 3.30am.

After fifteen years, her body had gotten used to the unnatural hour being the start of her day; it didn’t mean she despised it any less. 

What she despised even more was the nine missed calls from Jen on her phone. 

Jennifer Kale: Call me. It’s bad. 

When Jen meant bad, she meant that Agatha’s favourite make-up artist had called out of work, or perhaps that ratings had slumped slightly that week. Bad didn’t indicate the life-altering, this-show-is-going-to-be-dragged-through-the-mud-now kind of bad. 

So, coffee demanded more from her at this hour than her assistant ever could. 

She switched her phone off, counted down to five and tore the sheets from her body. She showered, picked out a pair of slacks and a sleeveless black turtle neck and put on her heels before walking to the kitchen. 

She had learned the art of silence at this hour; Nicky would sleep until Sharon got him up for school at seven. He was too old now for the mornings she would go into his room and cuddle him before leaving for work. She missed those times, and missed him. 

At least she got to be there each afternoon to collect him from school.

Still, once she had spent ten minutes watching the West Village wake up with her mug in hand, she couldn’t help but poke her head into the darkness of his room and whisper her goodbyes before getting the elevator down to the foyer to meet her driver, George. 

It was only when she turned her phone back on in the car that she realised Jen’s idea of bad may have taken on a new meaning, because why on god’s green earth had her mother ordered her to see her in her office immediately over text? 

She didn’t want to know. 

She called Jen anyway. 

“You’re alive. Thank god,” Jen exhaled the moment she picked up the phone. “No, it’s ok. I’ve got her… Um, I don’t know. Wait, you’re coming in right?” 

“No Jen, I just called you at four in the morning for the fun of it. Who are you talking to?”  

“Lilia.” 

That was never good. 

“And why is my mother telling me to see her immediately?” 

“How far out are you? When you get here, I’ll meet you. I have copy ready, we need to go over the facts, go over what you’re going to say-” 

“Jen, spit it out.” 

There was silence on the line.

“Maximoff’s out.” 

“Funny.” 

“I’m being serious. She’s gone.”

“Why didn’t I know about this sooner? You’re supposed to be my assistant-” 

“I’m your producer, Agatha.” 

“Same difference,” she ignored Jen’s sigh. “I’m ten minutes out. Do not call me again.”

Those last ten minutes were spent mentally preparing herself for whatever fresh hell she was about to walk into. There had been no texts or calls from Wanda, and she certainly wasn’t going to be the one to reach out first. UBA wasn’t trending on the internet nor was anyone talking about them in the news outlets. Whatever it was, she wanted out of it already. 

When she reached UBA headquarters, the doorman was as gracious with her as ever but she wasn’t met by the usual chorus of colleagues demanding her arms and her legs and that she break her back for them whilst she was at it. Only Jen, waiting in the lobby with a grim expression and copious amounts of paperwork in her arms. 

“Walk and talk,” Agatha demanded to the woman as she scanned her badge and walked straight past her towards the elevators. Jen trotted at her heel, catching her breath as the elevator chimed its arrival. “What’s the plan?”

“It’s not been released yet and as far as we know, no one has gotten a hold of it. Including us. We only know that she’s resigned, no further explanations. Even her team turned up this morning,” Jen said during their venture to the sixth floor. “You’ll make the announcement at seven. Jimmy is happy to cover her segments alongside you today.” 

“I’m not working alongside him. The show is mine, I’ll handle it.” 

“Lilia’s already signed off on the copy-” 

“I am not working with him so unless you want to lose another anchor today, I suggest you do your damned job and keep that smug bastard and his tiny prick away from me.” 

“Noted,” they both stepped out of the elevator as Jen passed over a document. “Read this.” 

There was barely much to read. It was just a memo addressed to Lilia, signed off by HR. 

Wanda Maximoff has chosen to step down to focus on her family during this election cycle. 

“Bullshit,” Agatha spat out a laugh. “She wouldn’t do that.” 

Jen shrugged her shoulders, both arms up in question. “Perhaps your Mom can tell us more. No one can get through to her - Maximoff, I mean.” 

Agatha frowned as they turned the corner of the hallway towards her dressing room. 

“I’ll try later,” she said before shutting the door firmly in Jen’s face. 

By 4.45am, she was finished with hair and make-up and was onto her third coffee when someone knocked at her door. 

“If it’s Jen, I’m not here,” she called out before groaning to herself. 

It wasn’t Jen. 

It was a young man with dark, curling hair in pants that showed too much ankle and several fingers coated in black nail polish. 

Her mother’s assistant; she had no hope in remembering his name. 

It made her laugh to consider that her own mother had no sense in who she was actually hiring, considering her disapproval towards anything outside the heteronormative. 

“What?”

There was no question in her voice. 

The man - boy, she didn’t know - seemed to jump back at her words. 

He clutched his notebook so hard she could see his skin turn white. 

“Um, er… Ms. Harkness wants to see you. Like, right now.” 

“Well, you can tell her I am busy,” Agatha retorted, “like right now.” 

“She said it was an urgent matter.” 

“No shit,” she rolled her eyes. “She’s aware I have to be on-air in two hours?” 

Billy nodded. 

“That I have just lost my co-anchor and am having to pick up this mess myself?”

He nodded again, lips trembling. 

“I’ll head up there soon,” she replied, already focused back on her script until she noticed the boy stood there still. “What, are you waiting around for a tip or something? Leave.” 

“She…” his hands were hidden in his sleeves now, his words mumbled. “... She said not to return back without you.” 

Of course she did. 

“In that case, you’ll have to wait for me then,” she offered him a smile that sunk her neck into her shoulders, so forced it almost hurt. “Come along, pet.” 

This day was quickly becoming a hell within hell itself. 

It only continued to get worse. 

The story was leaked at 5am, just as Agatha pushed her way past William in an effort to find her Executive Producer. 

 

‘THE MORNING SHOW’ BELOVED ANCHOR CHOOSES TO WAKE UP WITH RUSSIA, NOT AMERICA, FBI INVESTIGATION SUGGESTS 

After Wanda Maximoff announced her resignation from America’s oldest television network earlier this morning, the nation is shocked to discover that she is being investigated by the FBI for suspected ties with Russia. 

Just how long has UBA been harbouring a spy in their newsroom? 

The headline could have been about anyone, if it weren’t for the super-imposed image of Wanda sitting beside her on the set of The Morning Show. 

“Fuck,” she swore under her breath. 

The Wanda they were trying to paint was not the same Wanda that she knew. Then again, considering the article was from an anonymous leak and published by Page Six, she didn’t know what to believe. 

When Agatha looked up to see Lilia already preoccupied in her office, she nearly threw her phone against the wall. When she saw who was preoccupying Lilia’s office, she actually had to hold back her scream. 

What the fuck was Rio Vidal doing in there? 

It had been weeks since she had laid eyes on the petulant, immature, infantile excuse for a journalist. In those weeks, she had somehow managed to get herself taken off-air at YDA after an aggravated altercation with a member of the public that was caught on film and uploaded to social media - just like all good things nowadays. 

That was when she remembered that - yes - she was supposed to be interviewing Vidal that morning. UBA had offered her the platform to speak her truth, and she was clearly pissed off enough at her own employer to agree to it. 

But Vidal was looking a little too friendly with Lilia to just be there for on-air damage control. 

She sauntered from the room with a cockiness that had Agatha wondering how her morning could become any worse. It was only when Rio headed straight in her direction that she realised it could definitely, and was about to, get a lot worse. 

“Harkness.” 

Her eyes narrowed. “Vidal.” 

Rio looked her up and down; Agatha couldn’t help but step back slightly under the scrutiny. 

It had only been three weeks since she had those eyes staring up at her from the apex of her own thighs. It had only been three weeks since she had let a woman dominate her in a way she had never let anyone do before and it only left her despising Rio Vidal more. 

“Fancy seeing you here,” Rio said, her lips curled. 

“I work here. But last time I checked, you don’t so what do we owe this pleasure?” She asked through gritted teeth. “Finding someone for your next assault?” 

“Funny,” Rio said with a humourless laugh. “That guy deserved it.” 

“And you clearly deserved your suspension.” 

“Big of you to be talking about my professional problems when you’ve been harbouring a spy around here for god knows how many years,” she said. “Excited to see how that one plays out for you guys!”

Agatha merely imitated back her words in a childish voice. 

“I’d love to pick your brain on Wanda-gate sometime,” Rio’s hands were in the pockets of her slacks, her foot tapping against the floor. She looked up at Agatha, curling her lips. “Got any scoop for me? Perhaps we could finish where we left off? I seem to remember you begging for more-” 

Rio’s words were cut off by a hiss escaping her mouth, thanks to the point of Agatha’s heel kicking into her shin. 

“Yeah, why not,” Agatha smiled sweetly. “Here.” 

She offered Rio her middle finger. 

Rio laughed again, under her breath, shaking her head before meeting Agatha with those annoyingly dark eyes. “And they call you America’s Sweetheart. Anyway, break a leg today. You know where I am if you want more.” 

Agatha snarled at Rio before she watched her strut down the hallway like she actually had a right to be there. She nearly kicked her heel through the nearest-available wall. 

When Agatha turned back around, she saw Lilia standing in the doorway to her office, watching the exchange with raised brows. 

“Don’t,” Agatha deadpanned. 

Lilia held her hands up in defence, though she was clearly refraining from letting a laugh escape. “Not my business. What is my business, however, is the fact that your mother’s office is calling me every damn minute asking where you are. For the love of god woman, go and see her.” 

“So she can shout at me for not knowing enough about my co-anchor? We need to re-draft, we need to-” Agatha huffed before taking a deep breath. “This show is going to be a wreck and I’m the one that has to look like the fool on national television!”

“Copy has been re-drafted,” Lilia tutted. “If you don’t go up there now, I’ll just have to get Jimmy to do the show with you.” 

Agatha’s eyes narrowed, her mouth parted in a disbelieving smile. “You wouldn’t dare.” 

“Try me.” 

Agatha’s body squirmed as she tried to keep her feet planted to the floor rather than lashing out to damage the nearest item available. If that morning had shown her anything, it was that she should not be trusted around any fragile items. 

There weren’t many of her colleagues that would stand up to her like Lilia would, but then again, Lilia had known the version of Agatha Harkness that wore purple ribbons in her braided hair that ran around the studio with a stolen hairbrush as her microphone. For all intents and purposes, Lilia was more of a mother to Agatha than her own mother was. 

When she saw William standing at the end of the corridor, waiting expectantly, Agatha’s hands flailed at her sides as she let out an exasperated sound before turning on her heel and carrying herself down the hallway with a pointed jaw and pounding chest. 

“Be back down here by six-thirty!” 

She stood outside the CEO’s office, clenching her fists and evening her breath out. 

The entire executive floor was as ostentatious as the people it housed yet it managed to simultaneously suck the life from anyone unfortunate enough to visit it. 

She remembered the hours she had been forced to do her homework under the watchful eye of the receptionist. She remembered the countless men that would flow in and out of that room with wicked laughter and sickening smiles directed towards her despite her not even being in high school yet. 

She hadn’t been a child for a very long time, but this floor had a way of transporting her back to a time where she lacked experience and lacked any real ability to stand her ground.  

There weren't many people on the planet that could make Agatha nervous, but Evanora Harkness firmly maintained the number one spot. Work meant their relationship was smiles and curt nods, but outside of that, it meant thirty-nine years of disdain between a mother and her daughter. 

William knocked at the door, waiting for Evanora’s approval before opening it. Agatha straightened the moment she heard the cold tones of her mother’s voice. 

Evanora sat at the overly grand desk that looked out onto the skyline above 6th Avenue with her phone pressed to her ear and jaw set tight. She was a cold woman, old and haggard and always wearing a perfectly tailored blazer and matching skirt that aged her distastefully. 

“Mother.” 

Evanora barely looked up. “I’ll call you back, Stark. She’s here.” 

Agatha’s ears pricked up. 

Stark. 

Evanora Harkness, CEO of America's largest television network and news division that prided itself on journalistic integrity and transparency, getting friendly with philanthropist-turned-politician Tony Stark, known for his far-right opinions and intent to run for state. 

It was an interesting realisation, to say the least. 

“Agatha, sit down. Much to discuss.” 

“I’ll sit down once you tell me why my co-anchor is being done for espionage.” 

Evanora’s shoulders were stone, her movements calculated and cold. 

“Nothing is confirmed but we cannot risk that becoming a reflection of our standards here at UBA. We let the investigation take its course, far, far away from here.” 

Agatha offered a bitter laugh. “You have no proof she did it, yet you forced her out.” 

“She resigned." 

Agatha raised her eyebrows. “I’m sure.” 

“Don’t be difficult with me,” Evanora’s eyes narrowed. “There’s no time for you to be emotional. We need to discuss today’s broadcast, and going forward, your new co-host.” 

“Yes. Lets.” Agatha perched herself up against the back of the couch, arms folded across her chest as she watched her mother type away on her laptop. “Perhaps you can tell me why Rio Vidal was sniffing around our studio this morning?” 

“You’re interviewing her, are you not?” 

“That doesn’t explain why she was in Lilia’s office from 5am.”

Evanora sighed, pushing her glasses to the brow of her nose before finally looking at her daughter. “Optics, Agatha.” 

“You’re considering her? She’s just been taken off-air for assaulting a man in the street.” 

“Not for anchor, you fool. She’s too unpredictable. Right now we need stability.” 

“That doesn’t answer why she was here. One of my biggest competitors in the industry has practically moved into my dressing room on the day the network is falling to the ground, and you’re telling me it's for optics?” 

“You’ve always been too dramatic,” Evanora said as she scrolled on her laptop. The stare she offered when she looked back up had Agatha believing she was back to being lectured about not scoring full marks on a middle school paper. “So weak. Think more of yourself, girl. You think that substitute anchor on YDA is competition?”

Agatha remained silent.  

“I made you what you are. And you insult me by comparing yourself to that?” she continued, each word spat instead of spoken. “No network is falling to the ground whilst I run it, but it also won’t have a lesbian leading it. The only thing you have to worry about is making UBA look good.” 

Agatha stilled. 

She took a deep breath. 

Her nails dug into the oak boardroom table she leaned against. 

“I let Calderu bring in a few of her own selections for protocol’s sake. It's time that TMS had some changes around here, and the first being, your co-host will be male. Respectable, charming, able to offer this country stability.” 

If she wasn’t already seething from her mother’s previous comment, she was sure her skin had turned red at its successor. Hell, it had probably turned green with the way her stomach was churning at what she was hearing from her own flesh and blood. 

It was clear that her mother had known about the allegations against Wanda long before that morning. 

And worse, she was adopting Tony Stark’s anti-human rights rhetoric, ironically just after getting off the phone from him. 

She knew her mother was an awful human being, but she had never seen Evanora dare to show it so overtly. If only she could say she was surprised. 

“You best be ready for screen tests tomorrow afternoon.”

“Mom, I have Nicky to-” 

“That boy is old enough to look after himself.” 

“He’s seven.” 

But why would Evanora know that? She barely acknowledged his existence. 

“I pay you enough to afford a Nanny.” 

“Yes, who he is with now. But I get him after school, that’s always been the deal.” 

Evanora’s chin was pointed and her shoulders tight as she turned away from Agatha. 

“I have Ralph coming in at four.” 

Agatha suspected getting shot would have been more painful than to hear those words leave her mother’s mouth. She could barely process them, let alone react to them. 

“Do I need to remind you how hard it is to secure that man? Be thankful Eagle News are still negotiating his renewal because this is our one and only chance at poaching him back.” 

It was the way Evanora refused to look at her as she delivered a blow lower than Agatha expected her to go. It was the way that she made no attempt to conceal her obvious disregard for her own daughter’s feelings in the name of money and status. 

Agatha was simply lost for words. 

“You will be there. And you will be nice. We need him to pull through this mess Maximoff has thrown us in. Now go back downstairs, put on a smile and do not screw this up for me.” 

She allowed herself a few breaths, processing what her mother had said, trying everything in her power not to react like she had been taught by the years of therapy endured as an adult. 

She turned to her mother, let her hands unclench and offered a singular nod and smile that didn’t quite reach her eyes as she let the door slam behind her. 

There was not a single planet that existed where Agatha Harkness would agree to host The Morning Show with her ex-husband again. 

There hadn’t been many broadcasts that had been difficult for Agatha; she could count them on one hand for certain. 

“And we’re live in six…” 

There had been the broadcast when her son decided - in utero - that he was fed up in his mother’s stomach and that Agatha should have to endure contractions for over two hours whilst on-air. 

“... Five.” 

There had been that morning that Agatha had spent thirty minutes more than usual in her dressing room as her make-up artist tried to conceal the blackening bruise forming at her cheekbone, just to go and sit beside the man who had given her it. 

“...Four.” 

There had been her last time on air with her then-husband, with fake smiles plastered in front of the camera whilst she knew, that evening, that Ralph would be served their divorce papers and The Morning Show would never be the same again. 

The Assistant Director quietened, instead counting down on her final three fingers. 

Three.

“Breathe,” Jen whispered into her ear-piece. “You’ve got this.” 

She’d kill the woman if she weren't about to address the nation. 

Two. 

Her eyes flickered over to the corner of the room. Rio stood against the wall looking directly back at her with her arms crossed and tongue poking against her cheek. She looked to be enjoying seeing Agatha sweat with far too much satisfaction. 

One.

Agatha smiled softly at the camera, hands held out in front of her. 

“Good morning. It is Friday, 2nd December, 2020. I am Agatha Harkness. Before we begin today’s show, on behalf of UBA, I want to address the news that we have all woken up to this morning.”

She cleared her throat. 

Everyone in the studio watched her intensely. 

“It has come as a shock to us all but we will continue to remain transparent with you as we receive further updates,” she continued. “For the past six years, Wanda Maximoff has been a trusted presence in homes across the country - mine included.” 

“Her reporting has taken her from war-zones to Capitol Hill. She has held power to account. She has asked difficult questions.” 

None as difficult as the ones they were about to face from the rest of the world. 

“As many of you now know, questions have been raised regarding Wanda’s past international affiliations,“ she straightened her back slightly. “In order to allow that review to proceed without becoming a distraction to this broadcast, Wanda has decided to step away from her role here at UBA.” 

She paused at the next sentence on the teleprompter. 

Her mouth twitched. She could feel her jaw tighten. 

“We respect her decision,” she finally managed to say. 

“UBA remains committed to independent journalism and to the principles that have guided this network for generations,” Agatha continued. 

She tried to ignore whatever Lilia was saying into her ear-piece about keeping it together. 

She always kept it together.

“We believe in due process. We believe in facts,” she looked directly into the camera. “And we believe that fairness must extend to everyone.” 

Ironic, she thought. 

UBA was anything but. 

Wanda’s dismissal was certainly anything but. 

She had taken an oath to remain transparent; to serve journalism with dignity. Right now, she was doing the complete opposite. She sat on information that she knew would make the network look bad, but it was the truth. 

She wondered when they had started caring about appearance more than integrity, and why she was so readily being used as their puppet to portray their innocence. 

She couldn’t accuse them now; she didn’t have the evidence. 

But she could piss her mother off and that was always a brilliant place to start. 

“Which is why we believe in giving people second chances when the situation demands it.” 

Jen was in her ear. 

Lilia was also in her ear. 

Every person on set looked at her as if she had grown an extra head. 

Agatha Harkness never went off script. 

Then again, Agatha Harkness hadn’t gotten that far in her career by sitting around and letting people make decisions for her, no matter what other people thought. 

“You, our viewers, have been loyal to us. You are kept stable by sharing your morning coffee with us, or your commute to work. In return, we owe you stability back. We owe you progress in a world that is sure it shouldn’t be a priority. We owe you real.” 

“Agatha, what are you doing?” Jen hissed into her earpiece. 

Agatha simply smiled harder at the camera and removed her earpiece from her ear. 

“Which is why I am thrilled,” her eyes shone in a way that only those close to Agatha could know was false, “to announce my new co-host.” 

Her colleagues stood, dumbfounded. 

Some held their palms to their mouths, others whispered to one another. 

Lilia had stormed in, as close as she could possibly get to Agatha without moving in front of the camera. Agatha noticed she didn’t look angry, she just looked unimpressed, her arms crossed and eyebrows raised. 

“As of next week, joining us here at The Morning Show,” she could practically hear her mother screaming from the thirty-fourth floor, “is Rio Vidal.”



Chapter End Notes

if you've seen the morning show (apple tv) then you know exactly the moment that was in reference to

Chapter 3: Supermassive Black Hole

Chapter Summary

TW - Implied/Referenced Domestic Violence

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“You haven’t changed, have you? Still as stupid, still as spineless.”  

It was not the first time she had been sat down, fingers digging into the skin of her knuckles, as her mother cowered over her with words meant only to hurt. 

The only difference was that her private school uniform had been swapped for a tailored number straight out of Bergdorf Goodman, her childhood bedroom was now a boardroom and her once fresh face had been marred with the lines of nearly forty years on this earth. But her mother would never see her as the adult she was, only the insolent child she still claimed her to be. 

“Do you have any idea what you have just done?” 

Agatha held a palm against her mouth to hide her scoff. 

“Saved our network from public humiliation, brought in new viewers and sorted out the minor issue of us missing a primetime anchor? You should be thanking me.” 

It was true; the fallout from Agatha’s little stunt had not been much of a fallout but more so a revolution in how their network had been received. In the few hours it had been since their morning show aired, the clip of her unexpected announcement had gone viral and their fellow media outlets were hailing it an impeccable, necessary decision that honoured UBA’s commitment to be current, and give current back. 

Her mother didn’t see it that way; she only saw that her daughter had defied her. 

“You have jeopardised the integrity of everything that we stand for.” 

Agatha looked up at her, at those blue eyes that held more ice than her own ever could, and slowly shook her head. “What we stand for, mother? Or what you stand for?” 

There had been a time where Agatha would crumble under that hard stare. She would lose all ability to speak, would simply nod her head and hope to god that it was one more argument she had managed to get away from with only mental pain as a consequence. 

Now she had a life to fight for in the form of a small boy who still made her friendship bracelets, and thirty-nine years of learning that her mother’s ideals were not those shared by the average person, and that Agatha was able to form her own judgments on the world. 

The first judgement she had allowed herself to make was that her mother was an absolute bitch. 

Evanora, who had been pacing to the side of the table, stopped still. She turned to Agatha, chin pointed and fist clenched before slamming it down against the oak. 

“Don’t you dare,” she hissed. “We are going to have YDA breathing down our necks for breaching a contract that never even belonged to us. We are going to lose all credibility. Our viewers are going to think we want to surround ourselves with those kinds of people.” 

Agatha couldn’t control her instinct to recoil as far into the back of her chair as possible, nor could she calm the quickening pace of her heart against her chest. 

“Those people?” 

“People like her, Agatha.” 

She really shouldn’t have been shocked. 

“I see what you’re doing,” Agatha said in an unnaturally measured tone. 

Her mother looked at her once more before snarling in her face and abruptly turning away to face the city beyond the windows. “We were supposed to have Ralph here tomorrow. He would have solidified us that top spot for the foreseeable, unlike the flight-risk you have just decided to put on the top band of the payroll.” 

It was the mention of that man’s name, for the second time that morning, that caused her to falter, even if just for a fraction of a second as the reminder of him sent her into fight or flight mode. For all her mothers’ shouts and slaps, Ralph’s had always been louder and harder. It was probably why the pair of them had always gotten on so well together. 

Agatha’s laugh was a bitter ghost of a laugh. “You thought that would make good television?”

“It would bring the viewers to us, yes.” 

Evanora knew what he had done to her. She knew and she still turned a blind eye. 

“We’re not a goddamn soap opera!” 

“You two can be amicable with each other. You’re both adults.” 

No, they couldn’t be. He was lucky he still had a career after what he had done to her; it had been the only guarantee he had agreed to for him to give up his rights to their son. 

“You can’t be serious.” 

“Agatha, it doesn’t matter what you want. It only matters what keeps this network alive and paying your salaries, and that is Bohner. Not this Vidal thing.” 

“She is young, she is involved in things that matter. She may not have the most appropriate ways of going about it, but she stands up for what is right. That is what people want. That is what our audience wants. Especially after the shit-storm you have caused with Wanda.” 

“Be careful what accusations you go throwing around, Agatha,” Evanora said. “The world is changing, despite what your generation thinks. We either stay on the right side of politics, or we are left to hang dry when it moves on without us.” 

Of course it always came back to politics. The irony, that politics was the one thing that had enforced journalistic practices and protected their right to find out and tell the truth, whilst it inhibited who was actually allowed to tell it. 

“You will prepare her for her first show on Monday. You will sit through every minute with her on-air and when she fails, Bohner will replace her. Am I clear?” 

Agatha had heard enough. She stood up from her chair, the legs screeching against the hard wood floor. Her knuckles found the ledge of the table as she leant over it, staring directly at her mother with narrow eyes. 

“If you bring him here, I will walk.” 

“At least I know that he won’t.” 

The irony in her mother’s belief wasn’t lost on her. 

Rio Vidal had better take to that screen like butter takes to toast, or so help her god. 

They had three days until Rio would take to the air. In the first of their prep sessions, Rio had been uncooperative at best. Granted, it was the same day that Agatha had made her announcement on a whim and ever since, Rio had been shoved into Lilia’s office and told she could not leave until the necessary people had been contacted. 

Whilst Agatha had been berated by her mother, Rio had sat through calls to legal, calls with YDA representatives, contract negotiations and other logistical issues that were far too above Agatha’s pay grade for her to care. 

Rio did not say a word to Agatha when they had been reunited later that morning to prepare alongside the production team; she continued her silence for the remainder of the day and only offered her an occasional, hard stare that Agatha couldn’t help but roll her eyes at. 

On their second day of preparing their new anchor, Agatha was already not in the mood.

It was a Saturday and weekends had always been strictly for time with her son. Instead, Nicky had been shipped off to a friend’s house whilst Agatha endured what she assumed was her punishment for ensuring the longevity of their network as they knew it. 

It was during their first screen test that Rio decided to actually acknowledge her presence. She had turned around in her chair, her smile from their practice segment replaced with a scowl. 

“Why did you do it?” Rio had asked her, tight-lipped. 

Agatha chewed on her words. 

“You wanted a platform to tell the truth, now you’ve got it.” 

Her answer was not received well. 

“You could have consulted me before blowing up my entire career.” 

She hadn’t been able to hide her laugh. Little did Rio know that it wasn’t just her career that would go under if they couldn’t pull off a good show; Agatha could lose her and Nicky’s safety and, as his mother, that was everything to her. 

“Darling,” she had said with a mewl. “I’ve just changed your life. Act a little more grateful.” 

By Sunday, Rio had become slightly more cooperative. They had been with production all morning, endured an arduous meeting with Lilia and been introduced to Rio’s producer, Alice. Agatha had overheard from Jen that Rio had demanded they employ Alice as her producer, and that she would accept no one else. They had previously worked at YDA together, and Rio had threatened to not show up on Monday until Lilia agreed to it. 

There was something about Alice that irked Agatha; she was preppy, she was too self-involving and she kept touching and fawning over Rio in a way that left Agatha seething. 

They couldn’t just be colleagues; Agatha found herself close to her final straw with her new co-host at just the thought of it. 

The team had been let go in the early afternoon but Agatha wasn’t finished, even if she did have a little boy at home waiting for a movie and takeout like she had promised. 

The hallways were quiet; their usual inhabitants all enjoying the remainder of their weekend before another week commenced, much to Agatha’s displeasure. She reached Wanda’s - no, Rio’s - dressing room and gave one sharp, rapt knock before forcing the door open. 

Rio was sitting in her chair, Alice on the couch behind her. The room was different to how Agatha remembered it - less stuff, less personal. The two women inside it looked up at her with wide, expectant eyes; Alice began to stutter out words that made no sense. 

“Out,” Agatha demanded to the producer, her hand pointing through the doorway. 

“Agatha-” 

She ignored Rio. “Out,” she repeated with more force. 

Alice looked torn. She offered Rio an apologetic smile before turning to Agatha, eyes narrowed. It didn’t get lost on her that the woman with spiky, highlighted hair brushed past her shoulder a little too forcefully. 

When the door slammed behind Alice, Agatha was met by an equally-angry face. 

“What?” 

“You need to learn to pretend to like me.” 

Rio huffed. “Apologies for not getting a degree in acting.” 

Agatha moved further into the room, leaning the back of her legs against the dressing table to face her un-willing co-star. “Rio…” she sighed. “I’m being serious. If this doesn’t work tomorrow, it’s not just you in the firing line.” 

“Ah, there’s the self-preservation I was waiting for you to admit to. Well done, it’s been an honourable attempt at convincing me that you did this for me.” Rio clapped several times whilst her smile remained flat. “I don’t know what you think will happen to you. It’s your network, Agatha. Nepotism at its fucking finest.” 

Agatha’s inhale was sharp. 

“My mother wanted to re-employ my abusive ex-husband.” 

Rio wasn’t prepared for those words to come out from her mouth; Agatha wasn’t either. 

“She wanted him to sit beside me every morning, even though I had to get a restraining order against him, and get him to waive his rights to my - our - son. So yes, there was an element of self-preservation. Because I can’t fucking look at him, let alone work with him.” 

Agatha watched as Rio processed her words. 

She wondered if Rio pitied her. She wondered if Rio despised her. She wondered if Rio even believed her. 

“Hell, you want the full truth?” Agatha couldn’t stop herself. “That job would never have been yours if it weren’t for me. You were here so Lilia felt like her opinions had been heard. My mother hates you; she hates anyone like you,” Agatha paused and took a deep breath before continuing. “Including me. Do you understand what I am trying to tell you? I wanted to piss her off, and you were the perfect means of doing so.” 

Agatha didn’t expect for Rio’s doe-eyes to hurt her. 

She hadn’t realised Rio was capable of softening, which had always been a large part as to why she’d ever bothered wasting breath on her, or her body-count for that matter. 

“Agatha… I didn’t know that. Jesus, how does no one know about that? Wait, no that’s not important. I…” Rio’s voice quietened, her eyes trailing to the floor. “I’m sorry. That you went through that.” 

Agatha shrugged her shoulders. “Just don’t fuck this up for me.” 

Rio’s usual smirk and glint of excitement in her eye had disappeared, replaced instead by straight lips and a solemn stare. 

“Oh, and that is completely off-the-record,” Agatha said as she stopped in the doorway, “otherwise I will ruin your career before it has even started.” 

Monday arrived and with it, nausea sank deep into her every muscle and bone. She had barely slept, barely eaten and barely spent any time with her son. To say she was off-kilter and marginally pissed off would be an understatement. 

They had to get this right. 

If they didn’t, Rio Vidal would quickly take the third spot on her hit list of people she absolutely would hit if and when the opportunity arose without legal implications. 

“What the hell are you wearing?” 

Rio had walked onto set, Alice in tow, wearing a maroon shift dress and low kitten heels. Agatha didn’t think she had ever seen Rio in a dress, nor could she ever imagine her in one. 

If she was to imagine it, it certainly would never have been that. 

“They wanted to make me look less gay.” 

Agatha bit the inside of her cheek. “They told you that?” 

“With their eyes.” 

“You look awful.” 

“Thank you.” 

“We have got to do something about that before tomorrow,” Agatha resisted the temptation to laugh. “In the meantime, don’t-” 

“Don’t fuck this up. Yes, I know.” 

Rio Vidal, in fact, did not fuck it up. 

By some miracle of a god that Agatha would hunt down and kiss at their feet, the show was a success. There wasn’t a moment that Rio stumbled. She was collected, she was invigorating and she bounced off Agatha like she had never worked alongside anyone else. 

There were times during the show that Rio’s eyes would darken and lips spread into a grin as she watched Agatha, captivated. The first time Agatha had felt that stare, she misread a line on the teleprompter. Each other time left her unnerved as something in her throat tightened. 

The response was overwhelming post-wrap of the show. They had trended on social media for two hours afterwards. Several media outlets branded them an iconic duo that every household needed to tune into each morning. Someone on X had already made a fan account for the both of them. 

Agatha stopped at Rio’s dressing room on her way out of the building. 

“What are you doing this evening?” Agatha asked, pretending to be entranced by her nails. 

Rio looked around the room before her wide-eyes found Agatha again. “Me?” 

“I don’t see anyone else here.” 

“Oh,” Rio said, shaking back her shoulders and fixing her hair in her mirror. “Nothing.” 

“Good. We’re going for a drink,” Agatha said. “Say 6pm? The St. Regis.” 

As Rio’s tongue licked her teeth, a disbelieving smile on her face, Agatha couldn’t help but be captivated by her. For all of Rio’s bravado, she was still putty in Agatha’s hands. 

Agatha was enjoying it too much. 

“And I don’t get to decline?” 

“No, you don’t.”

Rio simply rolled her eyes, muttering something under her breath as she swivelled her chair away from Agatha. 

“Oh, and Rio?” Agatha called before leaving the room. “Good show today.” 

In her haste to leave, Agatha missed the first small, genuine smile on Rio’s face that she had been the reason behind. 

The King Cole Bar was a brief pause to life amidst the city that never sleeps. It allowed Agatha’s shoulders to ease as soft jazz sounded and a waiter brought her usual drink over before she had time to put her bag down. 

She sipped her negroni like it was water; the burn wasn’t enough to quell her nerves. Agatha Harkness did not get nervous when meeting a co-worker for a drink. Then again, it wasn’t often that she slept with her co-workers; she at least tried to go further afield. 

She downed her drink quickly. She felt idiotic. She had spent twenty minutes looking in the mirror before she had left, sorting out stray locks of hair and swapping her shoes seven times. She chose wide leg black pants with a sleeveless black cow-neck underneath her jacket, an ordinary outfit for an ordinary, casual drink. 

She knew she was overthinking it, she just didn't know why Rio Vidal was having that effect on her. 

When she saw Rio walk in, eyes bright and movements skittish as she took in the surrounding extravagance, Agatha felt her jaw clench. She wore pants similar to Agatha’s, only they cuffed at the bottom. It was her top that left Agatha’s heart breathing just slightly too fast for her liking; it was a white shirt, with the sleeves rolled up and too many buttons undone at her chest. 

Agatha quickly downed the rest of her cocktail. 

It was as if every time Agatha saw the face of Rio Vidal, she wanted to inflict something against it. Each time, the sight of that woman caused a visceral reaction that left her fingers bent in a rage of need to sink into her skin. To cause her pain, to hear her pain, to feel her pain. Anything to dull the rage within her. 

If only Agatha could have seen it clearer. She didn’t want to inflict pain on Rio Vidal, she was only angry that she couldn’t inflict anything other than pain onto her. 

“A negroni,” Agatha said to the waiter. She watched as Rio surveyed the menu, those hazel eyes scanning back and forth far too quickly for somebody who felt comfortable in a place like this. “Make it two.” 

When he left their table, she placed a hand on Rio’s knee, causing the woman to break her stand-off with the list of drinks and look up, eyes wide. 

“Breathe,” Agatha reminded her. “Not your usual haunt?” 

Rio kept glancing to the hand against her knee; Agatha noticed and did nothing about it. 

“I’m more of a lager in a dive bar kind-of-gal.” 

“And yet,” Agatha’s hand flexed against the material against her leg before trailing a finger up higher along the wool-blend fabric of her thigh, “these are perfectly tailored.” 

“My paycheque doesn’t change my choice of where I get drunk.” 

“People will start noticing you more.” Agatha removed her hand, each movement slow as she breathed in the sweet burn of liquor against her throat. “Are you ready for that?” 

The woman before her found the floor rather than her face as she exhaled deeply and offered a shrug of her shoulders. Rio sipped her drink and Agatha couldn’t take her eyes away. She watched as Rio’s expression turned from tepid to an impressed smirk. 

“That’s good,” Rio said. 

A slow smile crept into Agatha’s lips. “Good.” 

One drink quickly turned into two and their conversation, to Agatha’s surprise, had run smooth. 

Rio had explained how she had managed to reach so far up the career ladder despite being a nobody from Delaware that got through her undergraduate and postgraduate on scholarships alone. Agatha learned more about Rio’s time at BBC News as a US correspondent, fascinated and feeling slightly put-out that Rio definitely held more life experience than she could ever have hoped for. 

“When did you first decide you hated me?” 

She hadn’t expected the abruptness of Rio’s question, but she was impressed by her abrasive nature no less. 

“Oh, that’s a hard one,” Agatha said as the corner of her lips began to curl. “I’d love to say that it was that piece you so kindly published on my behalf, without my say so-” 

“But?” Rio asked.

“But,” Agatha continued, narrowing her eyes at Rio. “It would have to be when you won the IWMF over me.” 

Rio’s lips cracked into a wry smile. 

“I’ve been in your head for a long time then, that was a couple of years ago” Rio sat up a little straighter. “...Do you still hate me?” 

Agatha considered her response. “I’m learning not to.” 

The silence that fell between them wasn’t uncomfortable. It was an affront between hazel and blue - both working each other out, both surprised at themselves and each other. 

“I wanted to ask you something else,” Rio began. “About you.” 

“Great,” Agatha said through gritted teeth. 

“There’s been rumours about you for years. You’re clearly not straight, but you had a husband-” 

“Rio,” Agatha’s tone was clipped, her eyes lacking any warmth. “Not here.” 

Were she not three negroni’s deep, she would have left the bar altogether.

Rio ducked - Agatha had no idea who from. “You said your mother doesn’t like people like me. Like you. Why stay hidden? If you were telling me what I think you were telling me…” 

The air grew thick. Agatha gulped; Rio watched carefully. 

“I want to believe you,” Rio added. “But I don’t trust you.” 

“Good, that’s something we can mutually agree on then.” 

“You still haven’t answered my question.” 

“You just told me you don’t trust me. How can I then trust you with the truth?” 

“I can give you something in exchange.” 

Agatha stopped. It was a sobering suggestion although it caused her stomach to swirl with anticipation. Was it odd to be turned on by someone so willing to play at her game?

“And how does that something concern me?” 

“It’s about your mother.” 

Now Rio was truly speaking her language. 

“Go on,” Agatha said, her hand motioning for her to continue. 

“I got a tip-off that UBA is receiving sponsors from a PAC known to be aligned with Tony Stark’s campaign.” 

“What?” 

“There’s a group who support Stark funneling money into your precious network-” 

“I know what a PAC is, Rio. And it’s not my network.” 

Rio ignored her. “It kind of goes against UBA’s whole ‘political transparency’ narrative.” 

Agatha thought back to Wanda’s dismissal; to finding her on the phone with Stark that same day; of her mother reminding her they needed to stay on the ‘right’ side of politics. 

It all ran deeper than she had suspected. It had all been in front of her the entire time. 

“Interesting,” she said in a low drool, trying her best to look entirely uninterested despite the news setting off alarm bells in her mind. 

“Is that enough for you to answer my question?” Rio asked, puffing out her chest as she reached for her drink. “I’ve heard things about you, Agatha Harkness.” 

Agatha couldn’t imagine what. In their line of work, everyone was desperate to sink their teeth into one another’s lives. Anything to get a one-up and reach the top of the food chain. 

“All bad, I hope.” 

She didn’t know if it was that her own gaze had become more sultry by the second, or if Rio was just quick to feel her drink, but the way Rio’s eyes darkened at her words told her that neither of them were immune to the tension in the air around them. 

“Bad enough for me to want to find out the truth behind them,” Rio clicked her tongue. “Did you even want to be with Bohner?” 

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Are you asking as a co-worker, or a friend?” 

“I think we both know that friendship will never be possible,” Rio said, before sitting forward slightly. “I’m asking as someone who is interested. You have an ex-husband, and a son, and years-worth of rumours that lead me to believe you didn’t want a husband in the first place. I’m sure you can see my confusion.” 

Agatha watched Rio, her mouth open slightly as she processed her guest’s brazen intrigue into her personal life. She had to admit that she knew about the rumours, and she knew that a large chunk of her colleagues in the industry did too. And Agatha Harkness, being proclaimed the nation’s sweetheart and heir to America’s largest television network, meant that people were desperate to get their hands on any information that could cause her downfall. 

“Is this for your next hit piece?” Agatha arched her brow. “You think I don’t know you’re probably still working for them on the side? Bet they gave you a real nice deal for the dirt on me, didn’t they?” 

“Believe it or not, Agatha, I wouldn’t do that to you,” Rio had found her cool, collected tone as her shoulders eased into her seat. If Agatha hadn’t gotten so riled up, she would have enjoyed seeing Rio become more accustomed to her unfamiliar surroundings; now, it only angered her more. “Not anymore.” 

“Anymore?” Agatha’s laugh was bitter. “So you would have.” 

Rio answered without missing a beat. “Of course I would have.” 

And how could Agatha blame her? She would have done the same; any journalist would have. But Rio’s honesty was surprising just as much as her confidence was surprising. Most surprisingly of all: Agatha liked her even more for it. 

“What changed?” 

Rio considered her response as Agatha watched her slowly sip at her drink, her eyes never straying too far from Agatha’s stare. “You gave me a job that I never thought I could get my hands on. Why would I ruin that opportunity for myself?” Agatha noticed she gnawed her teeth into the pink of her lips. “...But, I don’t think it’s just the job I want to stay for anymore.” 

Agatha hummed as she tried to keep up her act of nonchalance. Truth be told, it felt like there were several tiny people within her chest who had all screamed in unison at Rio’s words. 

“What are you interested in, Vidal?” 

“What? 

“You said you were someone who is interested. What are you interested in?” 

“You.” 

Agatha’s mouth parted slightly, her shoulders tense. She hadn’t expected Rio to say that. Perhaps there had been some small part of her that hoped, given the way their conversation had turned but that hope had been firmly locked away into a part of her mind she had permanently closed off. 

When she looked at Rio, there was no hesitation in her expression; no regret. 

“... And helping you get to the bottom of whatever fucked up situation you have just forced me to be a part of.” 

Agatha’s lips slowly began to curl. “You’re bold,” she said slowly. 

“It wasn’t just luck that got me to where I am.” 

“I like it,” Agatha said. 

I like you, she could have said if she were one or two more negroni’s deep.

Chapter End Notes

you'll start to notice that agatha really, really likes a drink

Chapter 4: Breath Of Life

Chapter Summary

TW - Themes of homophobia and far-right politics.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

It wasn’t often that Agatha succeeded in shutting her mother up, but Evanora had been forced to eat her words in the wake of the success of Rio and Agatha’s first show together. 

Agatha now had the pleasure of being given the silent treatment; she revelled in it. 

Their ratings had sky-rocketed and Agatha and Rio both were earning their respective PR teams’ bonuses for that year with their growing popularity as co-hosts. Rio had been given brand deals; Agatha had been carted off to every gala, dinner and conference as the face of UBA. 

On screen, their chemistry needed no improvement. 

Behind the scenes, it only continued to grow. 

Agatha hated it. 

It came too naturally between them. Ever since their night at the bar, Agatha found herself smiling at things Rio said that, if said by any other person, she usually would be holding herself back from spitting in their face. Agatha noticed that Rio found her gaze the moment they were in the same room and each time, Agatha would indulge her. 

Worst of all, Agatha found her mind wandering to those dark eyes and tanned skin, usually hidden between too many layers of clothing that left her daydreaming about what was beneath them.

She should be focused on the important things, and the important things were uncovering the details behind her mother’s dirty secrets. The only important thing she needed to uncover about Rio was whether there was any credibility behind her so-called anonymous tip-off. 

And with her mother not currently breathing down her neck, Agatha had decided to take advantage and revert back to one of her favourite pastimes: snooping. 

She had learned quickly as a child that the only way to ever find out the things that adults didn't want to tell you, was to stick your own nose in. She was her mother’s daughter in some ways, no matter how much she hated it.

And what she found indicated that maybe, just maybe, she should start to trust Rio. 

Agatha Harkness: Got something. Come back to the studio at 10pm. 

Rio Vidal: That’s past my bed time, and yours. 

Agatha Harkness: I’ll bring you coffee tomorrow. 

Rio Vidal: And a pastry. 

Agatha Harkness: Whatever. 

The building was quiet, the evening show finished and the team packed up for another day. It was just Agatha and Rio, alone, besides a few cleaners and security lurking about. 

“I managed to pull a few strings and have got my hands on copies of UBA’s finance reports for the last quarter.” 

They were in Agatha’s dressing room, documents spread across the floor and laptops open with sticky-notes littering them like a sorry excuse for art. 

“A few strings?” 

Agatha smirked. “You’re not the only one with investigative roots, darling.” 

Rio’s tongue poked against her cheek, her eyes narrowing in surprise at her colleagues’ zest for rule-breaking. “So, what are we looking at?” 

Agatha passed her laptop over. “This. Page 32. You see that, there?” She pointed to a particular segment of a spreadsheet. 

The way Rio looked up, face breaking into a disbelieving smile. “Jesus Christ. That’s a lot more than just a friendly donation." 

“And it dates back to last year,” Agatha filtered through the documents spread on the floor, picking out three different sheets to show Rio. “See? He’s been doing it for months.”

It was a glorious thing to see Agatha Harkness looking so impressed. Rio had never witnessed this side to the woman before, let alone believed she had it in her. 

“That’s not the only thing I found,” Agatha continued, reaching for another pile of documents. “I managed to get onto Lilia’s computer whilst she was in a meeting. These are programme schedules for the last month. TMS and evening news. All those redacted segments? They’re pulling certain political stories. Immigration welfare, pro-choice marches, even-” 

“That’s why they pulled the piece on Alabama this week,” Rio realised. “That boy was fifteen. Fifteen, Agatha.” 

Agatha knew. She truly did. She thought about her son, half that boy's age. She couldn’t even fathom the horror; the heartbreak. She considered if Nicky would one day tell her that he liked boys. Would she raise a gun to his head? Would she, hell. 

“This is censorship,” Rio hissed. 

“Rein it in, Vidal,” Agatha murmured as she studied the document. She turned, looked at Rio and sighed. “I’m seeing Wanda later this week, to talk about everything.” 

“You think that she can corroborate?” 

“No, but I think she can confirm to us that my mother is not playing by the rules.” 

“And if she does?”

Agatha thought long and hard. She hadn’t really considered the fallout from such a momentous scandal; a scandal she was connected to in more ways than just blood. 

“Then we burn my mother, and anyone else who thinks they can touch this place, to the ground.” 

Agatha didn’t think Rio’s eyes could get any darker, but she was quickly proven wrong. Hazel turned to black, piercing into her own blue. It was a collision so ferocious, she was slightly choked for breath. 

“You’re enjoying this, aren’t you?” Rio asked. 

Rio continued her stare, as if no one else in the world existed apart from Agatha Harkness. 

Agatha gnawed on her lip as she bit back a laugh. “It’s exciting, don't you think?”

“It is attractive,” Rio murmured, her voice lowering as her eyes searched Agatha’s face. Agatha couldn’t help but notice the way Rio’s gaze darted to her own lips several times. “That’s what I think it is.” 

The document in Agatha’s hand stopped swaying as her arm locked in time with every other muscle in her body. Had she heard that right? Rio Vidal found her attractive. 

She couldn’t go there. She couldn’t trust Rio, for starters. The woman was earlier in her career than Agatha, and known to have a stronger bite. Agatha was no fool, and to assume that Rio could be sourcing her own story to sell in light of Agatha throwing her entire career up in arms was not entirely absurd to consider. 

“Your affinity with breaking the rules runs strong, Vidal,” Agatha rolled her shoulders back. “Is that what you get off on? Illegal activity?” 

“No,” Rio corrected. “It’s seeing you, finally getting the chance to do what you trained for.” 

Agatha did not know how to respond and chose to ignore it entirely. Instead, she brought the document closer to her face, lifting her glasses lower to look like she was far more interested in that than whatever Rio’s next advance would be. 

When a hand gently reached for her wrist, forcing it down against the floor, document now discarded nearby, Agatha’s breath hitched in her throat. 

“Rio-” 

“Look at me,” Rio’s nails dug into Agatha’s skin in a way that left her unable to look anywhere else. Her voice was firm; Agatha found herself wondering when this woman that she had plucked from nowhere and thrown into a once-in-a-lifetime career opportunity had thought it was ok to take control. “Explain to me why this matters to you so much.” 

When Rio had finished speaking, Agatha had to admit that it was incredibly attractive. It didn’t feel like judgement; it felt like genuine intrigue, like Rio wanted to understand why she was putting her entire career on the line for a woman who had already tried to ruin it once.  

“I don’t want my son belonging to a family that helped to ruin his future,” Agatha admitted after a long silent battle between their eyes. “And…” she took a deep breath, “...I don’t want him to have to hide… like I did.” 

Rio’s grip on her wrist loosened just as her eyes softened. 

“You’re different to how I expected you to be,” she said with ernest. 

“A good different, or a bad different?” 

“A good different,” Rio was resolute. “You’re different to how people talk about you and there is not a single part of you that is like your mother.” 

How could Agatha tell Rio that her words were the highest compliment anyone could offer? 

Rio’s fingers were now trailing up Agatha’s wrist, reaching under her sleeve to feel her bare skin. Agatha’s breath was caught in her throat at the soft tickles of her touch that were making her feel much more than just like laughing. 

“You’ve come to that conclusion rather quickly.” 

“I’m a good judge of character.” 

Agatha could only gasp when Rio’s fingers gripped her arm again and began to pull her closer. Without consciously deciding so, Agatha found herself shuffling across the floor, her chest now inches from Rio’s. They were so close that she could feel Rio’s breath warming her skin. 

“Rio, what are you-”

“Shh,” Rio whispered, her hand reaching up to brush a loose lock of hair from Agatha’s face.  “I want to kiss you,” she said, causing Agatha to lose any chance at maintaining a rational thought process. “Is that ok with you?” 

She nodded her head, unable to breathe and unable to offer anything more coherent. She watched as she lost the hazel of Rio’s eyes to closed lids. She watched the indent of Rio’s cheekbones appear as her lips pursed together, and her head began to lean in. 

They joined so sweetly, all Agatha could feel was panic. 

She stopped it just as quickly as Rio had started it. 

“Rio-” Agatha breathed heavily. “No, we can’t.” 

Agatha tried to ignore the deep-seated concern etched into Rio’s features, just like she tried to ignore the dizzying feel of her fingers raking through her hair and the guilt inside her at the sight of Rio’s eyes desperately searching her own. 

“Why not?” 

“I’m not-” Agatha’s movements were muddled as bad as her thoughts as she began to collect the paperwork up from the floor. “I can’t do this.” 

“Agatha…” 

She closed her laptop, picked up her handbag and coat and stormed to the doorway. 

“Good night,” she said, barely turning around. 

The first thing Agatha did after opening the front door to her apartment was pour a glass of wine and proceed to pout at how little wine the glass could be filled with. She considered scrapping the glass altogether and downing the contents from the bottle itself. Anything to quell her raging heart and clammy skin. 

Her thoughts argued against each other as she scraped her hands through her hair. She questioned what she was doing, fooling around in a way that felt far from fooling. Perhaps, if anything, she was the fool in question. 

One moment, she would convince herself that this was wrong, and she was just seeking out a release in a stressful situation. On the other hand, she couldn’t get those damn hazel eyes out of her mind. Or her smirk. Or the way she fluttered her lashes before she leant in. 

There was too much riding on this 

Then again, it felt incredible to be actually investigating something again. With someone else, equally as invested and equally as at stake as she. It was the first time in years - perhaps even her entire career - where that buzz of reaching the truth had returned. 

“Mama?” 

Agatha was taken from her thoughts by that small, innocent voice that caused her heart to flip without fail. She looked up to find Nicky stood in the shadows, his foot tapping on the floor and hands clutching at the sleeve of his dinosaur-printed pyjamas. 

“Hey baby,” she said with a soft smile. “What you doing up?” 

His head tucked into his neck sheepishly. “I… I had a-” 

“Bad dream?” 

He nodded quickly, cheeks reddening. 

Agatha’s chest ached at the sight. She shifted her position on the couch before opening her arms out. That was all the boy needed before he swept across the room and collapsed into her waiting embrace. 

“You were out late,” Nicky mumbled against her chest. 

She tightened her hold on him, placing a kiss to his hair. “I had to go back to work. You remember me telling you about Rio?” She felt Nicky nod against her chin. “She’s helping me work on a new story, and it's a hard one. So there might be more late nights soon, ok?”

Nicky nodded again, curling tighter into his mother. “My friends at school said she’s really good. And funny.” 

Agatha smiled, not that Nicky could see it. “Yeah,” she agreed softly. “She is.” 

As she sat there, her son’s breath evening out against her chest, Agatha couldn’t help but replay that moment - that horrific almost-kiss which she now realised she never wanted to be an ‘almost’ - and her mind started to convince herself that she was an idiot. That she was wimpish. That she was the fool. Rio couldn’t know she was like that; Agatha Harkness did not, and could not, hold that reputation. 

It was a double-edged sword. She wanted to prove to Rio that she was not one to chicken out of any self-gratification they could manage, but she also didn’t want Rio thinking she threw herself at any stranger. 

What left her most on edge was that, usually when sleeping with women, it was no more than a one-night-thing where she would forget their name by her second coffee of the morning. 

She couldn’t forget Rio’s name; Rio’s voice; Rio’s eyes. 

She didn’t want it to be a one time thing. 

She visited Wanda a few days later, after work. Nicky was at theatre club after-school and Agatha watched streets of people pass her in her car, wondering if they too were experiencing such an astronomical shift in everything they had known for the past half a decade. 

It took thirty minutes to reach Wanda’s apartment in the East Village. She couldn’t help but wonder how long Wanda could upkeep such a place like that, with two young boys and a husband desperate to make his move to Silicon Valley. She doubted they would last in the city long, given what had happened. 

Another friend gone, thanks to the incredulous machine that was broadcasting. 

When Wanda opened the door, Agatha noticed the dark circles beneath her eyes and her paler complexion. She noticed the clothes on her that looked like they hadn’t been changed since the night before, and the piles of toys and books strewn across the floor. 

Their pleasantries didn’t last long until Wanda’s eyes were glassing over under the weight of everything that she was dealing with. Agatha could only sigh, extend her arm around Wanda’s back and guide her to sit on the couch. 

“I didn’t do it, Agatha. I didn’t do any of what they’re accusing me of.” 

Agatha had quickly learned the art of not trusting another soul. It had been integral to her studies; one of the first lessons they had been taught on her first day at Columbia. She knew to question everybody, including her own sources. She knew not to trust her closest allies. 

But she had also perfected the art of context clues. Including the obtuse, glaringly-obvious one that was pitting Wanda against her mother. If she put the two together in a room and was forced to pick one to trust, it would always be Wanda. 

She trusted Wanda. She had trusted Wanda. And she would continue to trust her over her own mother, any day of the week. If Wanda said she didn’t do it then she didn’t do it. 

“They called me in at the beginning of the week; told me they had a tip-off about an old relation I had from back home, but I don’t even know who this person is that they’re claiming is my insider. They claimed they had no choice but to involve the authorities. I didn’t even get a chance to explain myself. They told me to pack my bags, or my whole family would be dragged through the mud.” 

“They?” 

Wanda’s hand came to her mouth, eyes wide. “I-...”

“It’s ok, you can say it.” 

“Your mother.” 

Agatha couldn’t even pretend to be shocked. She just inhaled, deeply, and offered Wanda a flat smile. “I thought you would say that.” 

“It’s the truth, Agatha. I swear it,” Wanda began. “I wouldn’t make this up. We’re going to lose everything; we can’t stay here anymore. Vis has been desperate to leave the city as it is, and his company has wanted him in San Francisco for years. The boys’ lives are going to be completely uprooted.” 

Listening to those harsh truths was hard for Agatha. Sure, she felt guilty knowing that her ex-collague, and friend’s entire life was being turned upside down through no fault of her own. Sure, she hated knowing that she was a direct relation of the person who had no qualms in executing this obliteration of a family. Most of all, she could only think about the very real possibility that Evanora would have no issue with doing that to her and Nicky. 

“Look, Wanda,” Agatha sighed. “My hands are tied at the moment, but we’re investigating this, off the record. I can’t say anymore. Ok? You know how these things work-”

Wanda’s brows furrowed. “You’re investigating UBA?” 

Agatha’s lips pursed together. “...Maybe.” 

“Who the hell got you to agree to that?” 

“It was my idea.” 

“Wow, Vidal is really rubbing off on you.” 

Agatha choked on her breath and tried - miserably - to conceal it as a cough. 

“I don’t know what you’re talking about,” Agatha said, jaw clenched. 

“It didn't take you long to find someone to keep my seat warm.” 

“It kept the heat off you, didn’t it?” 

“I didn’t ask you to do that for me,” Wanda said. “And you’re not overly known to be selfless, Agatha. So why pick the one journalist you hate?” 

Agatha spat out a laugh. “I can think of one other journalist I hate more and that’s exactly who she wanted to replace you with.” 

Wanda’s face turned from hard, to question, to a softened disbelief. “Oh.” 

“Yes, oh.” Agatha slapped both hands upon her knees before she got up from the couch. “Will you go on the record once we have enough evidence?” 

Wanda stood up with her, face blank as her eyes searched her surroundings for answers she would never find. Agatha stared at those eyes that looked like they belonged to a deer caught in headlights. 

“Evidence for what?” 

“This all goes a lot further than just an unfair dismal of an employee, Wanda. Like I said, my hands are tied; I can’t tell you anything more. You know this,” Agatha continued.“But I can assure you that I am working to clear your name, just as much as I am making sure that UBA has a future without my mother thinking she has a right to meddle with it.” 

She hadn’t wanted to leave the conversation at that, but it was the truth and the truth was what Wanda was owed. When Agatha had gotten back into her car, the first thing she did was pull out her phone and open up her text chain with Rio.
