Agatha Harkness: Wanda’s not at fault but I’m sure you can guess who is. 

She hadn’t been prepared to come into work the next day and face a new, totalitarian regime. When Lilia had handed her the copy, the women had scowled and tutted and told her that she didn’t understand why they were giving “that man” airtime. 

It was only when she read through the script that she realised how bad it was. 

“Have you read it?” 

Rio had curled her head around Agatha’s open dressing room door. It had become something Agatha had become used to; the constant check-ins, the woman’s spritely presence around every corner. Rio had tried to mention what had happened between them that night alone in the office when she had come to work the next day, but Agatha had swiftly clenched her jaw and told her never to bring it up again. So far, she hadn’t said a thing since. 

“Of course I have,” Agatha muttered, barely looking up at the reflection of the woman in her mirror. 

“And?” Rio’s brows were raised. 

“We do our jobs, like normal.” 

Rio’s tongue poked against her cheek as she stepped in, closing the door behind her. 

“Are you going to be ok with it?” Agatha asked nonchalantly. 

Rio sighed. “Agatha, I have had this exact conversation with Lilia, with Alice, and even the sound technician asked me if I was going to be ok this morning. I am going to be fine.” 

Rio’s eyes were just about imploring enough for Agatha to believe her. 

“Maybe it’s not me we need to worry about,” Rio murmured under her breath. 

Agatha’s gaze narrowed, her chin snapping up to Rio’s direction. “What is that supposed to mean?”

“Nothing,” Rio said, biting her tongue. “So, Maximoff will corroborate?” 

“She’s tentative,” Agatha mused. 

Rio looked over her shoulder to double check the door was still closed, lowering her voice. “It makes sense though, right? That your mother got rid of her, given what Stark has announced for his campaign manifesto.

Agatha’s expression was grim, her fingers clenched around her own copy of the script. “It does. Looks like I'm officially the daughter of an extremist.” 

Rio simply laughed in response, shaking her head as she began to retreat out of the door. “It suits you.” 

Agatha scowled at the woman who somehow always knew how to get under her skin. 

“I’ll see you out there,” Rio said before closing the door. 

When Agatha had unearthed herself from her dressing room, she had sixty-seconds until they were to be on-air. Rio sat in her chair, reading over her copy as she walked through the studio. The crew all looked at her with forlorn expressions that she chose to ignore.

The show went seamlessly, until they got to the political updates segment. 

“In the lead up to primaries, Tony Stark has today announced his intent to run for President, as a representative of the Republican Party,” Rio began. 

“Mr. Stark has issued the following statement: Our country used to have order. Our country used to be great. Now our children are left to question who they were born to be,” Agatha paused to take a deep breath. Her fingers shook the script in her hands. “Our borders should…” she took another breath, “... not be open.”

She could not actually be reading these words out on live television. She could not have members of the public thinking she believed the things she was saying. She could not have Nicky one day watching the clip back and thinking that his mother could support such atrocities. 

She took another breath, her head flinching slightly as she did. “They are your children’s jobs to take, not those of another nation that is incapable of looking after… after its people.”

She felt a hand brush her thigh under the table. She heard Jen in her earpiece asking if she was ok. All she could do was focus on the next sentence on the teleprompter. 

“Birth rates should not be experiencing the decline that they are. We want to change that, to ensure our countries’ longevity and future as the strongest nation in the world. Our children don’t need to become overwhelmed by the choice society allows them today. They need direction. They need order, and they need to learn that traditional values are traditional, because they-” 

Agatha paused; gulped. Bile rose in her throat. 

“...are what work,” Rio finished for her. Agatha caught her eye, lost for breath and lost for words. Rio just gave her a small nod before she continued to take over Agatha’s script. “Mr. Stark goes on to conclude his statement with a very telling belief of where his campaign intends to take him, should he be successful.”

Agatha felt her lips curl as she noticed Rio had gone entirely off-piece with that last sentence. The room watched them, eyes on the floor and faces solemn. No one batted an eyelid at Rio’s defiance; Agatha couldn’t blame them. They were all shocked at what they were hearing. 

Rio inhaled deeply before continuing. “It was always Adam and Eve, Mr Stark said,” Agatha could practically feel Rio fighting away the urge to roll her eyes. “Never Adam and Steve.” 

Agatha’s hands tightened her hold on the piece of paper; the corner of the white sheet trembled back and forth. 

“We’ll be keeping you updated on further announced campaigners in the coming weeks,” Agatha managed to get out. “Remember you can catch Rio and I hosting the Nevada Caucus in Las Vegas this February.” 

When they finally cut to advertisements, Agatha let out a breath that was so long, she could have been convinced she held it the entire segment. Rio flattened down her jacket before turning to her co-host. 

“You ok?” 

“I need five,” Agatha muttered as she pushed herself up from the desk. 

“Agatha-” 

She didn’t turn back around. When Lilia tried to break her strut from the studio, Agatha repeated the same words to her EP. 

“You don’t have five,” Lilia told her, but Agatha had already pushed past her, walking out of the studio and ignoring Jen’s calls after her. 

Agatha near-screamed at Lilia as she walked away. 

“Well, make five!” 

In her dressing room, she locked the door and began to pace the room, back and forth with her head in her hands. Her throat was tight, her vision blurred and head spinning. 

She couldn’t process what she had just read; what she had just heard with her own two ears. 

That her mother was cosying up beside an apparent dictator-in-the-making. That there once progressive, truth-telling media space was being infiltrated by oppressive scum. That she was compliant in it all. That she was compliant in the support of ideologies that went against who she was as a person. 

It was just another reminder that she would never, and could never, live her life authentically. 

Not whilst her mother was still around. 

A knock on the door stopped her pacing. Agatha hissed at the intrusion. 

“For god’s sake, Jen, I’m fine-”

“It’s not Jen,” a lower, softer voice sounded. “Open up.” 

And for reasons she could not fully explain yet, she did open up. 

Rio moved into the space like she owned it, like she was here to take control, and for once, Agatha was not mad about it. All she could focus on was the mess they found themselves right at the centre of. 

“We have ninety seconds.” 

“I can’t go back out there.” 

“Grow up, Agatha.” 

“Excuse me?” 

“Grow the fuck up,” Rio said, not even batting an eyelid at the expression of astonishment on Agatha’s face. “This is our job. We go out there and we do our jobs like normal. That’s what you told me earlier. So grow up and do your fucking job. Don’t leave me to pick up the pieces.” 

Agatha was lost for words to say the least. She had never had a colleague speak to her like that, let alone someone as junior in her experience as Rio Vidal was. 

What left her more speechless was the slight curl of excitement in her stomach that she couldn’t deny she felt from being on the receiving end of such a pointed, angry tone. From such a beautiful, angry woman, no less. 

She couldn’t let Rio feel like she had that power over her. 

“What do you think gives you the right to come into my dressing room and tell me to grow up?” Agatha asked, her mouth open with her bemusement. “You wouldn’t even be here without me. You grow up.” 

Rio’s laugh was bitter. “Alright, Agatha.” 

Agatha pressed her script into her face, her glasses in her hand scrunched up to her forehead as she growled. She gathered herself, took one more deep breath before turning back to Rio, her features softer than they had been all morning. 

“I need to put a stop to this, Rio.” 

Rio’s own face faltered. She wasn’t used to hearing Agatha sound uncertain, nor was she used to hearing her sound so genuine. 

“I know,” Rio sighed. “But acting out like that on-air is only going to make her suspicious.” 

“I don’t see YDL covering his manifesto without putting their opinion on it,” Agatha huffed. “We are as bad as Eagle News right now. And it will be you and me on the firing line when ratings drop tomorrow.” 

“Do you know what got me through my, very unjust, suspension?” 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “What?” 

“Knowing that at some point, the truth would come out,” she replied simply. “It took two weeks until someone posted a video of it. I’m sure you’ve seen-”

“The dykes-must-die guy? Everyone has seen it, Rio,” Agatha waved her hand with dismissal. “He deserved it, for what it's worth.” 

“Thanks.” Rio flashed her a small smile, her hazel eyes lighting up. “What I’m trying to say is, let the ratings drop. Let us be in the firing line. Because as soon as this comes out? Everyone will be eating their words. Everyone will be running to the two people they can trust. The two people who wanted to tell the truth from the start.” 

“Look at you,” Agatha smirked. “You missed out on a career in politics.” 

“Don’t do me that disservice,” Rio said with a frown. “But we’ll get her - Evanora, I mean - I promise.” 

Agatha offered her a small smile, nodding in agreement. 

“Come on,” Rio said, holding her arm out. “Calderu is going to kill us.” 

 

Chapter End Notes

"it was adam and eve, not adam and steve" was painful to write i can't lie

Chapter 5: Sweet Disposition

Chapter Notes

things are about to get a little hotter around here

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It was a Saturday when Agatha received the call. 

The weeks following Stark’s campaign announcement had brought with them an air at work that left the hairs on the back of her neck standing up. She could feel the uncertainty her colleagues had in what they were, and were not, putting out on-air. She had not been the only talent to force words out of their mouth that they did not wish to speak. 

When her mind wasn’t on the fact that her son was most likely to grow up with his human rights dictated to him, it was on another equally-frustrating subject: Rio Vidal. 

She hadn’t been able to rid the thoughts of the woman, or the close encounter they had shared in the desolation of the UBA building after-hours. Neither of them had spoken about it; they were too focused on their investigation to pause for feelings, but the tension would sit on their shoulders and mock them any time they were in the same room together. 

That Saturday was the first day in two weeks that she had not seen Rio, or stayed late at work, or had had anything to do with her mother’s impending ruin of their news station. 

Instead, it had been a day entirely for her son. She had taken him to the zoo, despite their visit count already well-into the hundreds, and took a detour through Little Italy for some food afterwards. 

The sun had set, and Nicky claimed he was not tired despite yawning into his mother’s side every few minutes. She let him put on an orca documentary for the second time that week because he had not been able to shut up about it since the first time they had watched it. She didn’t mind, as long as she had him in one arm and a glass of wine in the other. 

 “Nicky, pause it for a second, honey.” 

She fumbled around her seat for her phone, finding it vibrating down the side of the couch. 

When she saw the name on the screen, her stomach flipped. 

“What?” 

“Hey, sorry to call so late,” Rio sounded breathless; borderline maniacal. “I’ve got something you need to see.”

Agatha caught Nicky’s eye, the boy sitting up now and watching her intently. At the age of seven, there was nothing he enjoyed more than getting his nose involved in things that did not concern him and pretending to be just like his mother. 

“You’re interrupting a very important documentary about killer whales.” 

“Orcas, Mama!” 

“Orcas,” she corrected herself, smiling when she saw Nicky’s grin. “Can it wait?” 

Rio sighed down the phone; Agatha already knew what her answer would be.

It had been two weeks since their night shared at Agatha’s apartment. 

Two weeks of stolen glances, endless text messages late into the night and brief touches to distract the other whilst on-air. 

One morning, Rio had walked into Agatha’s dressing room, her voice a sing-song-esque tune as she asked if she had left her shirt at Agatha’s - the one with Snoopy, Rio was sure to remind her - with little consideration for the fact that someone was already occupying Agatha’s time, and that someone was their Executive Producer. 

Lilia had given Agatha a look of confusion, considering Agatha had been convincing the entire staff since Rio had started working at UBA that she still hated her co-host, and said no more on the matter. 

Agatha was quick to remind Rio that they had to avoid suspicion; that it would be wise for her to pretend she still hated Rio whilst at work. 

The pair of them fell into a rhythm of pointed glares and the odd, hidden wink. Agatha had noticed Rio going purposefully out of her way to get in Agatha’s way, or forget her script, or ask the least intellectual questions possible.

“Because it is-” Agatha paused. “Wait, why are you calling me on this?” 

“It’s pretty neat. I can call you from my room!” 

“Rio,” she sighed. “Darling, you could have just called my mobile.” 

“What happened to the excitement, Agatha?” 

“It withered on our seven-hour-long travel day.” 

There was silence on the line for several seconds. Agatha imagined Rio chewing at the tassel of her hoodie, or picking at the skin around her nails. “Have you spoken to Nicky?”

“No,” her heart hurt at the mention of her son. “It’s nearly ten there, he should be in bed.”

“Do you think he is?” 

“Considering he is not allowed a phone until he is at least in middle school then yes, I have high hopes that Sharon has locked his Switch away and read him to sleep,” Agatha said. “Sharon’s too good with him. She gets a generous tip and his sleep schedule is never disrupted.” 

“You’re a good mom.” 

“You keep saying that, but you’ve hardly seen me parenting.” 

“I’d like to see it,” Rio replied. “I imagine it is very, very hot.” 

Agatha tried not to think of the implications of what Rio was actually saying; that she was implying she wanted to see more of Agatha than just intimacy. She wanted to see a different kind of intimacy entirely. 

“Come to my room,” Agatha said quietly. 

Her ears were met with a crass laugh down the line. 

“You’re too easy.”

They had been waiting for weeks to have time with each other - just enough time without risking the hands of a small boy opening her bedroom door, or a colleague barging through to their dressing rooms. They didn’t go crazy, there would be time for that after the debate. For that night they just held one another, and Agatha got to experience the first night that she could remember being the comforted, rather than the comforter. 

The next morning’s wake-up-call was not until 5am - a reasonable lie-in for them, even if they had both been entangled in each other and very much awake for the last two hours. It was only when Agatha remembered that hair and make-up would be knocking for her in a matter of minutes that she insisted Rio return back to her own room. 

Rio had pouted and tried to hide under the covers until Agatha stripped them completely from her bare body, resulting in a squeal and quick movement to cover herself up. Rio would not leave without a kiss and Agatha obliged her after at least two-minutes of going back and forth in an argument about whether a kiss was actually necessary. 

Deep down, she had wanted it. 

What Agatha failed to notice was that Rio left in the same creased material of her clothes from the day before, and that Ralph Bonner happened to be leaving his own room on the very same floor, at the very same moment.

The day of the debate was arduous and demanded too many smiles for Agatha’s liking. She couldn’t think of anything worse than being in a room with die-hard Republicans all day, let alone the one who was trying to tear down her family birthright.

This caucus had more heat on it than any other; one of the first of the election cycle, and in a state where the primary debate was suspected to swing red for the first time in years. If Stark came out on top of this caucus, it meant he would be the front-running political candidate for the Republican Party; that he was one step closer to governing their entire country. 

Held at the Paris Theatre in the early afternoon, the production crew and talent had hours of rehearsals and editing ahead of them before they were even on-air.

Each time she did it, Agatha felt her cheeks redden and pulse raise.

Agatha was no stranger to broadcasting and moderating political debate. She had covered three election cycles already in her career but the stakes had never been as high as they were on this occasion. 

“We’ll have to change this,” Lilia pointed at a question on the script. “From the powers that be above. They don’t want us focused on Stark’s social values, they’d rather us focus on his economic protections. It is the son of the greatest governor that Nevada has ever seen… Execs words, not mine.” 

Agatha didn’t need to ask which executive gave the final order. 

“Greatest is debatable," Rio muttered under her breath. 

Lilia coughed. “This is a red debate, Vidal. To them, Howard Stark was the best they’ve had.” 

Agatha coughed. “I’m sorry,” her words trailed off into a laugh. “We’re now having our questions dictated to us so that Stark comes out looking the best? He still needs to be asked about it-”

Lilia’s frown flattened. “We can’t.” 

Agatha’s interest piqued. This was her chance to get confirmation that it was her mother’s own dirty work - and opinions - altering their ability to practice journalism with integrity. 

“Why not?” she asked with a patronisingly-sweet smile. “Is it not our job?” 

She was sure that if Lilia looked at her any harder, her eyes would fall from their sockets. 

“I’m following instructions-”

“From your CEO?” 

Lilia rolled her eyes at Agatha. “Don’t tell me how to do my job.” 

Agatha could see the slight hesitation in Lilia’s face; the slight hesitation that said somebody else had already told her how to do her job. It was the first, real piece of evidence before her to show that Evanora was manipulating this debate and how her staff presented it. 

It left Agatha’s skin red and her lips sore from the strength of her teeth biting into them. 

Evanora didn’t want them to be neutral; she wanted them to be compliant. 

But there was no room for remaining neutral - not with the evidence they had on UBA receiving excessive funding from Stark. 

The decision for UBA to be host to a Republican caucus alone was enough to raise question marks. Everyone knew it usually would have been Eagle News to present such a Republican-heavy event and Agatha only suspected that Evanora had promised her new ally she would give him the appropriate platform to spread his agenda.  

That meant two things. Firstly, she needed to speak to Rio, alone. Secondly, she knew Ralph would be sniffing around the debate like a wounded puppy, desperate for an inch of affection or moment in the spotlight. 

She just hoped he wouldn’t embarrass himself by showing up around her. 

Hope was a fickle thing; all it took was for her to leave her dressing room after hair and makeup had readied her tired eyes and paling complexion, for her to hear that drooling, deep voice that always left the hair on the back of her neck standing up. 

Every inch of her body stilled. Her throat closed up; her limbs locked each bone and joint in place without her permission. 

Agatha Harkness had always been a professional in fight or flight. 

But hearing the sound of that voice? 

Around that voice, she only knew how to freeze.

“Agathaaaa,” it mewled. 

Her eyes closed and lips pursed together as she took a deep breath and turned around. 

He was in a blue suit, a red tie, and dark eyes narrowed directly at her. His hair was perfectly tousled and slightly darker than she remembered, his chin slightly stubbled and eyes black. 

The annoying thing about Ralph Bohner was that he always looked charming, no matter how vulgar he was in every other manner. It was how he had half of the industry wrapped around his finger, despite his public divorce and the - truthful - rumours of him having an abusive past. 

Agatha had always regretted not fighting harder. She had always wondered what Nicky would think of her - that she couldn’t be strong enough to put him behind bars for good. That a man who had caused them both pain and hurt got to walk free, have a good career and good lifestyle to show for it. 

She took one look at him, curled her lips in disgust before beginning to walk away from him. 

Bile rose in her throat when she felt a hand wrap around the back of her shoulder, stunting her movement and instead pulling her closer into a familiar scent that sickened her. 

“Why are you running away from me?” 

Agatha’s movement froze, along with her heart and her throat. 

“I have a restraining order against you, Ralph. Fuck off,” she hissed, swiping his hand from her shoulder. “ You’re not even supposed to be in this building.” 

“That doesn’t really mean anything,” he said with a sickening grin. “Not when you’re me. You and I both know it. Besides, we’re here to cover the debate.”

“Don’t pretend like you wouldn’t have loved it, Harkness.” 

She glared at him, taking a step back. 

“Would have helped squash some more of those rumours for you, wouldn’t it?” His brows raised, his chest puffed out in a way that left Agatha sickened. “That’s what you always needed me for.”

“She is not shiny, she is-”

She had truly never seen anything like it; if anything, she was the only one that could succeed in fronting against Ralph Bohner in such a way. And she was tempted to kiss Rio Vidal in front of everyone for it.

“Later,” Agatha muttered. “I need to get through this debate.”

His dark eyes captured her own from behind the curtains before he made a bee-line for her and all she could do was hold her breath and pray that this day would be over quickly and she could be naked with her hotel robe on, glass of cabernet in hand whilst lounging in the bathtub of Rio’s hotel bathroom. 

She didn’t enjoy speaking to Stark, but she did unfortunately know him well enough to hold a conversation. Regardless of her mother’s suspected close dealings with him in recent months, the man had been at every industry event, charity gala and of course, any political convention held that Agatha was also expected to attend. 

She had never liked him, especially since the time she had been pregnant with Nicky and been subject to a comment regarding her “finally doing her duty” to her marriage that even Ralph had laughed at. 

Still, he walked over to her as sure as ever. 

“I hope we’re going to play nicely today,” the man uttered with a tight smile and curt nod. 

Agatha stifled her laugh. “Play?” she questioned. “I didn’t realise this was a game, Tony.” 

“Oh Agatha,” he laughed, shaking his head slightly. “Politics has always been a game. And one I need to stay on top of.” 

The thought alone left a shiver running across her spine. She was too closely involved in this for her liking. Too impartial to make a change, but too in the forefront to not be accused of bystanding. Her mind wandered to a simpler life, where she didn’t have family legacy and the future of her son to consider all at once. 

“Unfortunately, as a journalist, I can’t help you there,” she began. “You know that. The truth had always, kind of,” she couldn’t stop her hand gestures, nor her sarcasm, “been our thing. Otherwise, I’m sure they’d revoke my Pulitzer Prize.”

“I’m not insinuating anything,” she offered an easy smile. “I just question what it means to someone like you… the truth that is. She couldn’t control the snigger under her breath. “Oh not to worry,” she smiled. “I will be asking, on camera, just to ensure everyone gets to hear your answer. I’ll see you out there. Good luck.”

The crew had set up podiums on the stage with the candidate’s backdrops, and a clothed table to the side with two microphones where Agatha and Rio would be scrutinised by the nation as much as their political counterparts.

Together, they wore two suits that left them looking like they could star in the upcoming release of Mission Impossible. Agatha’s hair was lightly curled, her lips painted a deep red. Rio’s hair fell perfectly like it always did, her makeup minimal and confident smirk taking centre-stage. 

It started off easy. After the five candidates had individually gone on, and on, and on, and on about their manifestos and garnered the support of delegates and party-goers, only one politician was left with a standing ovation. 

Of course, it was Tony Stark.

She couldn’t get him on his blatant homphobia, nor his transphobia, nor his anti-immagrant policies. What could they get him on? Freedom to the press. It wouldn’t cause enough of a stir between the Nevada delegates and voters, but it would to any other blue state.

“I am of the belief that every American deserves respect,” Tony’s words were seamless, his smile composed. “But I also believe it is important that parents get a say in what their children are exposed to in schools and public institutions. Too much focus on individual identities takes us away from the bigger goal of becoming a unified group.”

Rio’s face was the picture of innocence. 

It was perfect. 

Perfect enough to leave Stark stuttering and attempting to smoothly move to the next question.

“What role do you believe the press should play in shaping political discourse during an election cycle?” Agatha had asked the candidates. 

She had felt Stark’s eyes on her the entire time his rivals responded. 

“The press has too much influence. They are here to inform, not to choose positions of power. Unfortunately, we have seen cases of just that in recent months,” Stark turned towards Agatha, offering her a wicked smile and quick wink. “I believe one of our moderators was a junior reporter only a few months prior…”

The audience began to laugh; a sea of cold, croaky laughter.

If she did see them, she feared she couldn’t be responsible for her actions against Stark and that would leave their investigation void and reputations ruined. 

“I propose that press organisations unite under one front to present our nation with a seamless, direct stream of news that is responsible in its approach and reflection of American values. Our people deserve journalism that supports its country, not that undermines it.”

“Can Americans trust a government funded and led by billionaires to regulate billionaire influence within the administration honestly?” 

When it got to Stark’s turn to answer, he laughed.

“Leaders invest in those they believe in,” he quipped. “There’s a reason they are where they are today; there is a reason I am where I am today. If the people of America choose to join me, I can promise that to them too.”

“Lilia’s booked dinner; Jen, Alice, You and I. Nice place across the road,” Rio said. “Are you going to behave?” 

“Don’t need to, I’m not going,” Agatha spat. “Have fun.” 

“Fine,” Rio murmured, her head turning back to face her mirror.

“You’re seriously going with…” Agatha turned around, eyeing up Alice who stood in the corner, arms crossed against her chest and foot tapping against the floor. 

“Oh,” Rio laughed. “I am.” 

“But you said we’d-”

“We can,” Rio murmured under her breath, her eyes glinting in that annoying way they always did. “After. If you’re good. If you’re nice.”

“Ignore her,” Rio whispered now, her smirk widening as her hands found the lapels of Agatha’s blazer and pulled her down, closer until their faces were near-touching. “If you listen to me, you will be rewarded after dinner. Ok?” 

Agatha’s gaze darkened, her mouth almost limp in her lust. “You brought me something?” 

Rio nodded. “Something that will help you to forget all about today.” 

“Fine,” Agatha hissed. “I’ll come.” 

Rio grinned. “Yes,” she said. “Yes, you will.”

The restaurant was private enough but anywhere in Las Vegas lacked the exclusive feel when it left a stench of stale beer and cigarette smoke wherever they went. At least Agatha could get away with several glasses of wine before the press caught onto their whereabouts. 

By her third glass, before their cheque was rolled out and no doubt all on their table would expect her to pay for them, Agatha was just tipsy enough to join in on the conversation in more than one-word sentences. 

“Do we need to be worried?” Jen asked after Lilia had spent five minutes belittling Stark’s manifesto presentation from the debate. 

“Of course we need to be worried,” Agatha drooled. “He’s going to drag us back at least a century.” 

Alice and Jen’s eyes widened the moment Agatha opened her mouth. No one had heard her willingly speak all dinner, let alone to criticise politics, of all things. 

“Slow down on that wine, Harkness,” Lilia chastised her. 

“Agatha is right,” Rio said from beside her. “He’s got a lot of support down here. You heard what he wants to do…” 

Lilia rolled her eyes. “He can censor journalism over my dead body.”  

“He’s going to do worse than that,” Agatha muttered under her breath. 

Agatha hadn’t planned to tell anyone else about their investigation, not unless it was absolutely necessary; her third glass of wine told her differently.

“Of course I have it in m-” she paused, her cheeks flushed “- wait, what did you expect it to be?” 

Lilia laughed softly under her breath before shaking her head. “Oh, nothing.” 

Jen coughed. “I’m sorry, are we just going to sweep under the rug the fact that we’re all going to get fired?” 

“You work with Harkness,” Alice retorted. “You’re safe. Me on the other hand…” 

Rio reached out, her hand finding Alice’s arm and squeezing gently in the hope that it would stop her from reaching across the table and strangling Agatha then and there.

“No one is getting fired,” Rio said. “Because we’re going to stop them.” 

“Alright Superman,” Alice rolled her eyes. “Are you forgetting that you’re a latino lesbian? Not really sure you’re what Stark is seeking in his job adverts.” 

Agatha bit down on her lip as she took a deep breath. She hated just how correct Alice was. 

“Your mother can drag me out of that studio once the rigor mortis has set in,” Lilia mentioned, turning to Agatha before taking a sip of her martini. 

“God, I shouldn’t have said anything,” Agatha said through a sigh. “You’re all so dramatic.” 

Whilst Alice and Jen bickered between themselves and Agatha chose to ignore them, Lilia turned to her and Rio, her face serious in a way Agatha always had dreaded to see on the woman. 

“Are you being safe?” 

Rio laughed nervously. “Define safe.” 

Agatha kicked her in the shin, flashing her brightest smile at Lilia. “Of course we are.” 

“And you’re definitely going to get her?” 

“Lilia,” Agatha sighed. “When have I ever disappointed you?” 

Lilia frowned. “I’m not going to answer that.” 

“Is that all?” 

Lilia stood up from her chair, the rest of the table watching her, before she looked down at Agatha and nodded. “You tell me if you need help,” Lilia said. “Anything. Ok?” 

Both Agatha and Rio nodded. 

“Good, then I believe we’re done here,” Lilia smiled with a straight jaw. “Oh, and Agatha, darling, get the bill for us.”

Chapter 7: I Put A Spell On You

Chapter Summary

TW - Implied/Referenced Sexual Assault

Chapter Notes

After, Agatha took Rio somewhere secluded; somewhere they could both just be without worrying who was watching. 

It looked like a speakeasy from back home; worlds apart from the slot machines and neon lights of Las Vegas. Rio had gawked when Agatha supplied her name and revealed that yes, she had to be a member to get into a place like this. 

That set the tone for the rest of their evening; Agatha flashing both her cash and exclusivity and Rio following her around like a lost puppy desperate to get adopted by her. If Rio were ever to ask, Agatha considered agreeing under several terms. 

Not five minutes into their first drink and the warm atmosphere of the bar had turned to something more sinister.

She would always sense him before she saw him. 

“I should have known you’d be here.” 

Agatha didn’t look up immediately. Not after years of perfecting her carefully practiced composure. Instead, she focused on Rio’s face; the way her eyes snapped up and a flare was set off within them; the way her shoulders straightened and her fist clenched a little tighter around her glass. 

“I was just leaving,” Ralph continued, his words purposefully aimed in her direction. “I thought it would be the dutiful thing to offer my congratulations, but I don’t want to intrude on this little…” his eyes swam between them both; Agatha didn’t miss the way he looked Rio up and down. “... This little get-together.” 

“Is it a crime to share a drink with a colleague after hours? That always used to be your thing… didn’t it?” 

Agatha offered the smallest, wry smile as she finally met his gaze. 

“True,” he said, fiddling with his cufflinks. “But it was never your thing, was it?” 

“I think we’re done here,” Rio spoke up. “Goodnight, Bohner.” 

Ralph laughed. He shook his head, clicking his tongue against his cheek in Agatha’s direction. “You’ve trained her well, haven’t you?” 

The moment Agatha stood up, Rio arose with her. 

She was closer to Ralph than she had endured nightmares about. The liquor on his breath and cruelness of his tongue threatened to transport her back to times she had spent years learning to hide from. 

Agatha’s voice showed no hint of her fears. 

“What is your problem with me?” 

Ralph continued his light chuckles, taking the opportunity to now look his ex-wife up and down with narrowing eyes. “You have everything because you pretend to be something you’re not,” he spat. “You think our son should have a mother like that?” 

Agatha wasn’t aware of what she was doing until Rio was reaching for her, hands wrapping around her torso and pulling her back. 

“That is enough,” Rio hissed into Ralph’s face as she separated the pair of them. “I swear to god, if you don’t leave this premises now, I will make sure every last soul on this planet knows exactly, exactly who you are. Seeing as you’re so occupied with authenticity.” 

“You are both going to regret that.” 

Ralph’s chest heaved, his musty breath panting erratically. He looked between them, his stare cold enough to give reason for Agatha to take heed of his threat. 

When he had left, Rio sat Agatha down and held her hand tightly in her own. Agatha hadn’t needed to tell Rio that she needed at least five minutes to catch her breath and process what had happened before she could form coherent sentences again. Rio just knew.

She assumed they were photographed together in Las Vegas; that rumours had sparked about their potential reunification - both professional and privately. 

“You can tell them I have nothing - and want nothing - to do with that man. Ok?” 

“Ok, of course. Sorry to bother-”

“Whatever,” Agatha hissed down the phone before hanging up. 

Her hand shook ever-so-slightly, in a way that you would only notice if you were looking for it. Rio, of course, was looking for it. 

A hand gripped around Agatha’s ankle, tentative but firm enough to cause her to look up. She found Rio and along with it, her face that held far too much concern to waste on someone like herself. 

“You good?” 

Agatha shrugged her shoulders, her jaw tightening. Anything to avoid telling - or showing - the truth behind her fears. “There’s a story coming out tomorrow. Apparently, about Ralph and I. I don’t know whether to be relieved, or to be even more worried.” 

“Ok, that’s ok. So they got a picture of the two of you talking together in Vegas?” 

Agatha nodded. “That or he’s decided to start some rumours about him and me,” she rolled her eyes. “Never could quite resist getting into my business, that one.” 

“Then it’s just baseless gossip. You know the truth. I know the truth, and so does he. That’s all that matters.” 

“Nicky doesn’t need to be seeing that,” Agatha said. “Kids have told him things about me before - things their own parents thought they believed to be true. Doesn’t matter how much I pay for exclusivity, gossiping low-lives seem to be lurking in every class of society.” 

“Does he know about…” Rio paused, her eyes searching Agatha’s as if questioning whether she should fully commit to her question or not. When Agatha’s stare hardened, Rio’s resolve weakened. “Ralph. Does he know who his father is?” 

“Took you long enough to enquire about that.” 

Rio shrugged. “Didn’t want to overstep." 

“Honey, you’re in my bed every night.” 

“Yes. You. Agatha Harkness. In Agatha Harkness’s bed. Of course I’m afraid to overstep.” 

Agatha kicked her legs off from Rio’s lap, her body curling into itself in a way Rio had recently learned to read as she prepared to talk about something she absolutely did not want to talk about. 

“He… He knows bits. He doesn’t know who Ralph is. He wouldn’t recognise him from a picture, or if he turned on the news, but he knows he has a father and he knows that we don’t spend time with him because he is not welcome in our lives.” 

“What did you tell him?” 

“Nicky?” 

Rio nodded. 

Agatha took a deep, shaking breath. Rio considered it to be the most vulnerable she had ever seen her before. When they locked eyes, Rio could feel the weight of what Agatha was about to say before she had even said it. 

“That he hurt Mama.” 

Agatha noticed the way her words hit Rio, just like she noticed the quick intake of breath and awkward hovering of her hand, not knowing where to place it, or where she was allowed to place it. 

“Agatha…” 

“I hate lying to him; I never lie to him,” she implored. “But I couldn’t tell him that his own father didn’t want anything to do with him so…” Agatha took a deep breath, “I went with the only other truth that there was.” 

And that was all the truth there was to it. 

Ralph had hurt Agatha; Ralph had threatened their son. Agatha, for the first time in her life, had chosen to leave. 

She packed up one bag for herself and one bag for her little boy, their entire lives shrunken down to a few books, toys, warm clothes and each other. 

Lilia had taken her in without asking a question - she had simply opened the door, held Agatha briefly, held Nicky for longer so that Agatha could catch her breath, and allowed them both into her home so that they could start to live their lives properly. 

She hadn’t been living it entirely then - she knew that - but she had made one step in the right direction and it was more than she had ever managed before. One step that got her to where she was today; a healthy son who smiled and squirmed at her tickles, a presence in the world as Agatha Harkness rather than just his wife, and a woman that she was beginning to give in to her heart's desire about keeping around. 

“Does he think that your…” Rio chewed on her words. “Does he expect you to have a boyfriend? Not now-” she paused, “just sometime, in the future.” 

Agatha shook her head. “He asked me one day if he would ever have a step-dad. It was last year, when he had a thing about asking questions for several months. Particularly about his own father. Anyway, he asked me that and I told him that, no, I probably would never find someone to be his step-dad.” 

“But you never said anything about a woman?” 

Agatha shook her head again. “And he didn’t ask,” she smiled. “Told you, I don’t lie to him.” 

Rio appeared to screw her hands against her head for a second before composing her stature, her teeth near-sinking into her fist. “Ok, so let me get this straight,” she inhaled. “You know what you want, but you don’t want anyone else to know about it, so you’re happy to essentially forgo the entire thing that you want?”

“You’re here now, aren’t you?” 

“Agatha,” Rio sighed. “Is this really how you want to live the rest of your life? Pretending to be someone you’re not in front of the camera, just to appease your bitch of a mother? I don’t understand it.” 

“I don’t do it for her,” Agatha said, her voice more raw than Rio had heard all evening. “I do it for him. For Nicky. So he doesn’t have to see me brought to my knees by a woman of my own blood- of his own blood. What kind of message is that telling him? His father already decided he wanted nothing to do with him, and then to find out you're the other family member that caused the downfall of his future?” 

“What do you mean ‘downfall’, Agatha? It really is a more widely-accepted thing nowadays… you’re allowed to be gay in this country.” 

“Not if you’re a Harkness,” she said quietly. “We’d lose everything.” 

“What? You have enough money to-” 

“It’s not about the money, Rio," Agatha hissed, catching herself at the last moment and breathing in deeply. “Do you know how much influence my mother holds? One email and she has defamed me to every single journalist in this country. Not to mention the hold she has over the West and Asia. Nicky wouldn’t be able to walk down the street without someone hollering at him. In any city, in any country. Then I would be the bad guy. I would be like her. I have spent the last seven years trying to be anything but like her.” 

“He’d still love you…” 

Agatha laughed, but there was no jest to it. Only a coldness that Rio had recently become used to only witnessing Agatha offer it to other people, not herself, not anymore. 

“He might,” she shrugged her shoulders. “But he might not. That's a risk I’m not willing to take.” 

Rio processed Agatha’s words, for longer than she usually did. Agatha could see the way she chewed on her tongue as the cogs in her mind turned at an alarmingly slow rate. 

 “Is it about people knowing you’re with me?” 

“No,” she said quickly. “God, no,” she shook her head, reaching for Rio’s hand and bringing it to her mouth. “It’s about everyone that thinks they know me. They know the Harkness off-spring who is destined to fill her mother’s shoes and not grow a size larger than the sole of them. It’s about the last seventeen years of my professional career being built on a lie, and that suddenly unravelling out of my control. If people are ever going to know, I want it to be on my terms.”  

And the way that Rio was looking at her - with eyes so open they were like looking into the middle of the earth, an endless hole that she would happily fall down. Agatha wanted to tell the world there and then; a press release did not seem so terrifying at that moment.  

“Would you ever be ready for them to know?” 

The voice that met Agatha’s ears didn’t sound like the Rio she had gotten to know over the last few months. It did not sound like the overzealous, spriteful specimen that had risen ratings on her first morning opposite Agatha in the studio. 

It sounded like hope waning. 

It sounded, she couldn’t help but liken the two, just like Nicky would sound when he was disappointed and was trying not to show it. 

Agatha, being Agatha, couldn’t help but deflect one last time.

She wished that resorting to such a measure was not so natural, but she had simply been a young girl in a house with doors that slammed and dinner that was taken from you if you so much as failed to come top of your class. 

“That I like women?” 

She watched Rio’s shoulders sink slightly, just as she predicted they would. 

“That you like me.” 

The pang within her stomach hurt more than she had anticipated. 

Truthfully, would she ever be ready? 

Would Agatha Harkness ever be prepared for the world to see straight through her?

Agatha exhaled, accompanied by a heavy sigh. “Rio, I more than like you,” she said, reaching once more for the woman’s hand. It wasn’t lost on her that there was a slight resistance in Rio’s arm, a slight strength preventing Agatha from getting to her so easily. 

“But-” 

“Ah,” Agatha was quick to interrupt. “Stop putting words in my mouth. Is this a dealbreaker for you?” 

Rio let the silence rush amongst them again as she considered her response. 

To Agatha, every second was more painstaking than the last.  

“Eventually.” 

Agatha couldn’t let herself think twice. There was a first time for everything, and that apparently included Agatha acting on the immediate reaction in her gut - or moreso, her heart - with the absolute refusal to let her head talk her out of it. 

“Then, yes. Eventually I will. Hell, it doesn’t have to be eventual. As soon as we have presented our case; as soon as the world knows about my slimy excuse for a mother and her ratty toy-boy, I’ll release a statement.” 

Agatha hadn’t expected Rio to laugh. 

“Querida, where is this coming from?” 

“I don’t know if I’m ready,” Agatha said. “I don’t know if I’ll ever be ready.” 

Watching the surprised glee fall from Rio’s face in turn with her shoulders falling from her neck hurt Agatha in a way she hadn’t been prepared for. 

She wanted Rio to believe her. 

She wanted Rio to be hers. 

“But if I ever was, it would be because of you.” 

But if I ever was, it would be because of you. 

She had been worried that they wouldn’t be good. 

She had convinced herself that Agatha Harkness didn’t deserve good. 

And somehow, from one moment of recklessness in the form of a promise, they became better than good. 

The rest of their evening spent together did not feel new or revolutionary; it just felt right. 

It felt like Rio had been given the permission she had needed to fully embrace the woman whose home she was in. It felt like Agatha had been given the clarification - even if, from herself - that she was allowed to choose what she wanted, and good things could come from them in return. 

If only they had gotten more than one night like that. 

Everything had been normal at work the next morning. Agatha had checked her phone the moment her alarm sounded at three-thirty, the threat of exposure that her publicist had alerted her of had been just scary enough to not fully allow Agatha to escape into her newfound commitment to Rio. Still, when she checked, there had been no indication that anything had been published overnight that involved her, or her ex-husband. 

So she kept it good. Rio left for work earlier than Agatha, just as she had been doing most days in the hope their secret could remain on their terms for just a while longer. 

She stood at Nicky’s door for more minutes than usual, questioning how she would speak to him. She knew she had to - that was never part of the question. Since her revelation to Rio the night before, she had considered just how to go about letting her little boy know that his Mama was someone he didn’t fully know yet, but she was now ready for him to learn her. 

Soon, she told herself. 

The rest of her morning arrived without fanfare and no breaking news that involved her name, apart from that in which she was presenting to the nation through a camera in Studio 2, with Rio, finally, back by her side. 

Just as Rio was rounding up their final segment, Agatha noticed members of the crew glued to their phones, showing each other what they were reading, whispering under their breaths. 

When she saw Jen stepping inside the studio, she knew it had happened. 

And she knew it was a lot worse than she had expected. 

“And we’re clear.” 

The words from their Assistant Producer barely registered. Everybody was staring at her, everything was quiet. Movement didn’t happen in real time, only broken, slow fragments. There was a ringing in her ear. All she could focus on was the heavy sound of her breath. 

Jen was shoulder-to-shoulder with Lilia as she held her clipboard up in front of her face. Agatha felt her fists clench as she watched their pathetic attempts to conceal their gossip. 

“What’s going on?” 

Rio’s knee tapped against Agatha’s, her brows furrowed as she looked around the room. 

Agatha’s laugh was bitter. 

“Something I’m going to hate.” 

She watched as Rio unearthed her phone from her back pocket. She watched as the woman’s brown eyes widened before quickly scanning the text back-and-forth. She watched their relationship begin to crack before it had chance to even begin. 

“Don’t-” Rio brushed Agatha’s hand away as she reached for her phone. “Let’s get out of here, come on.” 

Panic wasn’t part of her usual vocabulary, but it had begun to make a home for itself, deep in Agatha’s chest, there in Studio 2 on the 6th Avenue, in the midst of Manhattan. 

She could barely find the words. 

“Is Nicky ok?” 

They were broken more than formed. More broken than she had realised; Rio hadn’t so much as acknowledged her; instead she was wrapping her arms around Agatha - one around her waist, one over her shoulder - and guiding her from their podium on set and through the studio floor. 

“Rio,” Agatha hissed. “Is Nicky ok?” 

Rio was still moving, her pace quickening through the hoards of production crew gawking at them both. Her words were quick; rushed. “Yes, he’s fine. Keep moving.” 

But they weren’t moving. Agatha had stopped them, her foot in front of Rio’s, her chest angled in a way that prevented them from covering any more ground. She could feel the eyes on her; she could feel the judgement. She didn't care. 

“Show me,” Agatha demanded. “I swear to god, Rio,” she hissed, “if you don’t show me it right now, I will-” 

Before she could say or do anything else, Lilia was striding over to her, her expression tight and eyes hardened. 

She spoke with little room for argument. 

“You’re done for today.” 

Agatha’s foot slammed against the floor without her conscious mind being aware of such a decision. It moved on autopilot, just as her racing heart was beginning to do, beating further than she could keep up with. 

“We still have to plan for tomorrow-”

She tried, but it was a breathless, hopeless attempt. 

“Go to your dressing room, lock it and wait for me,” Lilia’s tone hardened, along with her gaze. She turned to Rio. The look she gave was harder than the one she had offered Agatha, which attested to the situation at hand; the situation that Agatha was still unaware of. “Take her and keep that door locked. Do not let her mother in. Do you hear me?”

Rio’s nod was astute and her shoulders rigid. She was in a state of order that Agatha had rarely seen from her before. She was used to Rio being spontaneous, and always disobeying any rule directed her way. She wasn’t used to this militant, instruction-obeying Rio who was offering a firm nod and carting her down the hallway without another word. 

“Rio, what the hell is going on?” 

There was no kindness behind Agatha’s words; there was no warmth. They only evoked a seriousness which - Agatha believed - Rio was not seeming to grasp. 

“If you don’t tell me what the fuck has been published, we are done.” 

It took so long to hear Rio’s reply. So long that they had gotten to her dressing room, the door shut behind them and Agatha manhandled onto the couch. 

“Agatha…” 

Rio sat down next to her, one hand reaching cautiously for her own. 

Agatha let her take it; only in the hope that she would receive the news quicker. 

“It’s not good.”
