UBA Lesbian Love Affair

Agatha Harkness and Rio Vidal are ‘dating’, source claims.


By Charming St. James


Senior Reporter


Known for their bright smiles and unconventional digs towards one another, these two faces of America’s biggest breakfast show, The Morning Show, are allegedly more close than sharing conversation over a cup of coffee. 

 

The two anchors hosted the Nevada Caucus recently, and were seen leaving an exclusive Las Vegas bar together. Rio Vidal is pictured [below] being far more intimate with her co-star than one could put down to being professional. 

 

An anonymous tip-off claimed that Harkness has “been with women all her life, [she] just knows how to hide it.” The source continued: “the nation's sweetheart is a liar.” 

 

Our source has provided evidence of Harkness’ flirting with her co-star over private communications.

 

In one message, Harkness can be seen saying: “Trying to sleep, but someone won’t stop texting me,” followed by a scantily-clad, revealing image.

 

This certainly gives fans a whole new perspective to consider Harkness’s divorce with ex-husband, Ralph Bohner, seven years ago. Is Bohner the golden boy in this story after all? 

 

Stay up-to-date with the latest gossip here at Page Six

Damn right, it wasn’t good. 

She had been foolish to think it ever could be. 

Thirty-nine years built around a lie she had only just decided the night before that she was ready to unravel. She hadn’t even had time to become accustomed to the idea of coming out on her own terms, but this? 

The only thing this unravelled was herself. 

She had read it all; every single world. She knew that someone had accessed her phone in order to get hold of those text messages, just like she knew that someone had tipped-off the press about their whereabouts in Las Vegas. Hell, she knew it could only be one of a handful of individuals who had known her long enough to off-hand that quote so willingly. 

But there was no place for logic.

Not whilst her ears rang and her vision had doubled to a degree that left her surroundings playing out in slow-motion. 

“No network is falling to the ground whilst I run it, but it also won’t have a lesbian leading it.”

Ironically, that was the only thought in her mind: the news was now out and that meant her mother would know immediately. She had probably just thrown whichever electronic device that had the misfortune of showing her the article in the first place, into a wall. Like mother, like daughter, neither had ever been good at controlling their anger. 

She had almost forgotten that Rio was still standing beside her, idly swaying from one foot to another as her teeth nearly drew blood from her lips. 

“Talk to me.” 

“I want to leave.” 

Agatha’s words didn’t sound like they belonged to her voice; a stranger that only unearthed itself during the far and few moments of complete loss of control over her life. 

“Lilia told me to-”

“I want to be with Nicky,” Agatha cut her off. “Where is Jen? Find her and tell her to call Sharon and pick Nicky up from school early.” 

“Agatha-” 

“I need to know he is ok, Rio. Jesus christ, someone make sure he is-” 

“Stop.” 

Agatha looked up to find Rio’s hand against her thigh and her dark, brown eyes imploring into her own. It was then that Agatha felt the wetness against her cheek, trailing down it too quickly and entirely without her say-so. 

“I need him here-” her voice was quieter now. “Is he ok? I need to know he is ok.” 

“I’ll get Jen, but you need to stay here. Lilia’s orders.” 

There wasn’t any part of her that could argue back; she could only register that headline on a loop within her mind, only re-read those lines over and over again until they jumped from the page and sank their teeth into her skin. 

She wanted to hurt her mother. She wanted to hurt her ex-husband. She wanted to scream in the face of that stupid, stupid Charming St. James, because please, what kind of name even was that. 

Whilst her mind was stuck within itself, Rio had phoned Jen and simultaneously let her into the dressing room in the span of thirty-seconds. 

“She wants Nicky,” Rio started to tell the woman with an earpiece still in and clipboard still attached to her chest. “Call Sharon now, and his school.” 

Jen nearly growled, clipboard slamming into her thighs. 

“I’m not her secretary!” 

Agatha got up from the couch in a movement more forceful than both her counterparts expected from her. She strided over to Jen, fists clenched. “Where is my phone?” she demanded. “You have it.” 

Jen grimaced, taking a step back towards the doorway. “I don't think that’s a good idea-” 

“Give me my phone, or you’re fired.” 

“You don’t get to decide that-” 

“Jen,” Rio hissed. “Just give her the damn phone.” 

“Vidal, could we have a-” Jen paused, her eyes glancing towards Rio then emphasising her head towards the door, “a word, please.” 

“Anything you say to her,” warned Agatha, “you say to me.” 

Rio shrugged her shoulders at Jen. “She’s the boss.” 

“So it’s true?” Jen looked between the pair of them, her mouth parted slightly. “You two are really a… You’re a… Jesus. Welcome to the team.” 

“Jen,” Rio rolled her eyes. “Now is not the time,” she said not before Agatha was already talking over her. 

“Oh give over, Jennifer,” Agatha hissed. “Don’t act like you’re surprised.” 

Jen seemed to shrink her neck into her shoulders, her smile tight. “Okay, okay,” she resigned. “Just so you know,” she held out Agatha’s phone, her grip still tight, “there’s lots of messages. Including from… well, her.” 

Rio snatched it from Jen before Agatha could get to it. “Noted, thank you. Now please go and call Sharon. Tell her we’ll meet them back at home.” 

It was that one, small word that took Agatha out from her panic and back into reality. Rio had called Agatha’s apartment home. 

Rio felt at home. 

Even in one of the scariest moments of Agatha’s life, her home still was Rio’s home. 

“Lilia gave strict instructions, Vidal. She’s not leaving here yet.” 

“Why in the hell not?” Agatha’s voice rose an octave. 

“Because I want to talk to you.” 

Three heads turned up towards the door as they each quietened. Amidst their bickering, no one had noticed the door open, as Lilia slipped in. Though she was a small woman, her tight jaw and foreboding gaze was enough to have anyone crumpling at her feet. 

“I’ll be back in twenty minutes,” their producer said. “You,” Lilia pointed towards Agatha, “and me are going to have a little chat. Ok?” 

Agatha didn’t think her heart could sink any lower but Lilia’s words only served to prove her wrong. 

As Lilia opened the door, she turned to face Rio and Jen. “No one lets her out of this room,” she said. “And no one lets Evanora Harkness inside. Am I clear?” 

Lilia continued, her features softening towards Agatha.  “It’s all going to be ok,” she said. 

Agatha couldn’t believe her. 

Once Lilia had left, Jen made her own excuses and was once again reminded to get in contact with Nicky’s Nanny before she could manage her own escape from the room that was now home to only melancholy and unadulterated fear. 

Correction; home to melancholy, unadulterated fear, a woman who had spent her entire life trying to keep control only for it to be shattered by one finger clicking ‘publish’ on an article, and another woman sharing this experience with her after priding themselves to the public as being an open book. 

She was - clearly - not an open book; neither was Agatha Harkness. 

“Someone has tapped my phone,” she spoke, setting her body back against the couch with a resigned exhale. “They’ve probably gotten to listen to this entire conversation.” 

“Which is why I wanted to get it back from Jennifer,” Rio held out her hand with expectation. “Phone, por favour?” 

Agatha sighed as her hand outstretched with her mobile encased in it. 

“Wait,” Agatha retrieved it back. “What has she said?” 

Rio looked at Agatha, her eyes fluttering shut as if gathering her courage to look at the screen. “Agatha, I don’t think that is a good idea.” 

Agatha’s eyes narrowed. “Show me.” 

Evanora Harkness: You are no daughter of mine. You will fix this, or you lose everything. 

It was a punch in the gut to read, to say the least. 

Agatha couldn’t quite comprehend what was going on around her, let alone focus on the threat from her mother  - she could only think about her son. Her sweet, little boy who was too kind for his own good. How did she deserve him? She would never know, especially after that day. 

Out of all the ‘bad’ things - ‘bad’ on Evanora’s terms -  she had done in her life, the one that counted as a sackable offense, where her mother was concerned, was her being attracted to her own gender. 

The highest crime of them all: homosexuality. 

It was the twenty-first century for crying out loud. 

“I can’t break now,” she whispered. “If I do, I’ll never be… I’ll-” 

“I know,” Rio murmured, her hand swiping softly against the brow of Agatha’s scalp. “I know. You don’t have to do that. Not now. Not yet. But you will be able to, ok? And when you do, I’ll be there.” 

The only agreement she could offer came in the form of a muffled noise against Rio’s shoulder along with the smallest nod of her head. 

And Agatha kept herself together through each pain-staking minute that she waited for Lilia to walk back through that door. But each minute longer she waited, the thought of her mother being the one to break down that door instead of Lilia became an evermore legitimate threat. 

She thought of what her mother would say to her, if she was standing in front of her now. 

She wondered whether the cold, ice of an eye that Evanora Harkness would no doubt show her, could be capable of thawing, even if just by a fraction.

Lilia Calderu had been in the life of Agatha Harkness ever since she was a young girl, and Lilia was a younger, then-assistant producer for TMS. Agatha had always liked Lilia, even if she also had always known to be wary of her. 

She could still remember the first time she had met Lilia; Agatha had been around Nicky’s age and she had snuck out from her mother’s receptionists’ beady eye and into the elevator. For a seven-year-old, she had navigated the forty-floor building with precision and found herself exactly where she had hoped to be: in front of the cameras. 

Lilia had been horrified at the sight of a child in her studio. The woman had stamped her foot on the floor and pointed at Agatha with such a strong jaw and depthless stare that Agatha had actually stopped what she was doing and listened. She had not been used to other people telling her off - only ever her mother. 

But whilst Lilia had been the only other adult to remind Agatha that she was, in fact, a child and children were supposed to listen to their elders, she also was worlds apart from Evanora Harkness. Lilia possessed a heart, just like she possessed warmth. She had recognised Agatha’s interest in the production of their show early on and she had learned, soon after, that the little girl’s mother - her own boss - was not much of a mother to her. 

Ever since then, Lilia had always been more of a mother to Agatha than her own ever had been. 

And when Lilia finally arrived at Agatha’s dressing room, and Rio had wordlessly agreed to leave them both alone, Agatha couldn’t look into her eyes. 

She knew the moment she did would be the moment that she broke. 

“You’re still in one piece,” Lilia’s voice was more a sigh than actual, coherent words. “That is relieving.” 

 “When are you going to let me out of this place?” 

"Darling,” Lilia began, taking it upon herself to sit on the couch across from Agatha. “I don’t want you anywhere on your own right now.” 

Agatha cursed under her breath. “If my mother finds me, she’ll stone me.” 

“I’ve got security locking down this whole floor. We have access to get you out a back entrance. I say we have ten to fifteen minutes before your mother works out how to override it.” 

“That’s generously short of you,” Agatha’s smile was flat.

“She may be an old hag but the people working for her, unfortunately, are not.” 

Agatha’s vision was hazy as she stared into the distance, silence passing between them both. Lilia got up from the couch and moved closer to Agatha, guiding her to sit down in the chair, taking both hands into her own. 

“Listen to me,” Lilia said. “It’s all going to be out in the open now,” she gripped Agatha’s fingers tighter, “ok?” 

Agatha nodded softly, taking a deep breath as she did. “I know.” 

“This is your life. Not hers.” 

“I know, but Nicky-” 

“That boy is yours and no one else's, Agatha.”  

“She has more control than you realise.” 

“And you have more people fighting in your corner than you realise. More than she could ever dream of. Trust me.” 

The tears came ugly and hot. Her heart beat so fast she could feel it in her ears. She thought of Nicky, and she thought of Rio, and she thought of the little girl who used to dream of being in front of the cameras, just as much as she had dreamed of, one day, being allowed to be who she knew she was at her core. 

Arms enveloped around her, firm and grounding in a way she hadn’t realised she needed more than anything else in that moment. 

“I don’t k-know,” she sniffed, her movements to rid her tears were as aggressive as the shock of feeling them roll down her cheeks. “... I don’t know what to do.” 

“You don’t have to know, honey,” Lilia rubbed her hand against Agatha’s back. “You just have to be kind to yourself, as awful as it sounds.” 

A muffled laugh came from the woman, fetal-positioned into Lilia’s chest. 

“Awful?” Agatha unearthed her head from Lilia’s chest, wiping at her eyes. “It’s not just awful. It is cringe-worthy.” 

Lilia shrugged. “You make me uncomfortable when you cry.” 

“How do you think I feel!” 

“Piccola, listen to me,” Lilia’s fingers found Agatha’s chin, holding up so their eyes met. “It’s done now, ok? This is your chance to live your truth. This is Nicky’s chance to know his Mama. This is your shot at true, true happiness.” 

Agatha spat out a laugh. “Hardly,” she murmured. “Evanora wants me to deny it, otherwise I’m out.” 

“Is this job - is this lie of a life that you have been living for the last fifteen years - really what you want, Agatha? Is it really worth losing Rio over? What you two have is good.” 

“Oh, please,” Agatha rolled her eyes before taking a deep breath. “You’ve known about us for one hour.” 

Lilia’s smile was smug. “Honey, I’ve known since before Vegas.” 

“Excuse me?” 

“It’s not often that you wink at the person after you’ve berated them in front of the entire studio, Agatha. Please, don’t insult me.” 

“I did not-”

“Don’t,” Lilia interrupted. “Enough of this now. Let’s get you home to your boy.”

Rio had gotten into Agatha’s car with her, just as Rio had carried Agatha’s bags and held each door open for her as they progressed down the levels of the network’s building, for what Agatha assumed would be the last time. 

She barely gave it a second glance upon getting in the car; seventeen years of her life given in more than just blood, sweat and tears and now she had nothing to show for it apart from becoming the hottest new piece of gossip in town. . 

Agatha knew that Rio had noticed her dark, red-rimmed eyelids and the stains etching into the foundation on her cheeks. She knew, but still, Rio said nothing. She just sat by her side, quiet, but always there. 

It unnerved Agatha how much it helped to calm her. 

During the car ride through the busy-Manhattan streets, Agatha had taken Rio’s hand and held it close to her lips. 

“I need some time, Rio,” she had muttered.

Rio’s eyes had widened, no matter how hard she had tried to stop them. Agatha had watched as Rio’s lips sucked in a deep breath, her ribs extruding as she did. “From what?” 

Why did she have to say it like that? So blunt and leaving so little room for Agatha’s answer to at least try and sound eloquently un-like a dismissal. 

“From you.” 

“Agatha…” 

“Not like that,” Agatha said quickly, her gaze meeting Rio’s as her hand gripped tighter. “I don’t mean… Well, not forever. I just need tonight. This weekend. I need to be with Nicky and he… he needs to know the truth before school on Monday morning.” 

“And where does that leave us?” 

“You still want to help me get to the bottom of ‘whatever fucked up situation’ I have just forced you to be a part of?” Agatha released Rio’s hand, her eyes finally finding the brown ones she had avoided looking into. “Your words, if I remember correctly.” 

Rio was quiet, her stare unforgiving. 

Agatha hated every second of their silence. 

“I want to be more than that, Agatha,” she sighed. “You know this.” 

“Jesus, Rio.” 

They both should have known she would snap eventually. 

“Are you seriously making this about yourself right now?” 

“Agatha… You need time on your own right now, one-hundred percent. I can’t be the reason Nicky faces instability nor do I want to cause you anymore hurt. But, quierda,” Rio inhaled. “I meant what I said last night and this is your chance. If you want me, pick me. And we’ll take her down together. Otherwise I’m out.” 

“I was the one that said I needed-” Agatha paused, her words becoming more a splutter than sense. “Are you leaving me?”

Agatha couldn’t believe what she was hearing. She couldn’t believe that she could be publicly outed against her will, and then lose the very person she had been outed over. 

“Agatha, you just told me you didn’t want to see me.” 

“For the weekend!” 

They had gone back and forth for several minutes, neither realising at which point of their argument that the driver had decided to close the visor that blocked their snide remarks from his ears. Agatha didn’t care; George was used to her ways. 

“I don’t want to add to this - this is something that no one should have to go through - but, Agatha, I’m just trying to tell you that if you go out there and deny this, which I am assuming is an option considering your removal from the company has not yet been announced… Well, if you do that, then I’m done wasting my time here.” 

“Wasting your time? That’s what you think I’ve been doing?” 

“No, Agatha-” 

“Get out.” 

“Excuse me?” 

“Get out!” 

“No,” Rio’s voice left no room for argument, no matter how hard they both knew Agatha would try to fight it. “Hear me out, here, ok? I want to be here for you - hell, I want nothing more than that right now but I need you to know where I stand because… because the things I feel…” 

“Jesus, spit it out already.” 

Rio’s expression faltered, her head shaking in disbelief. “You are impossible, you know that? I was trying to tell you that the things I feel for you are, plainly, terrifying. And clearly I should be terrified because look at how you’re handling all of this.” 

Agatha had stilled, her back slowly sinking further into her seat before her palm rested against her face and an odd, disgruntled noise escaped her throat. 

“What will it take?” Agatha asked, her voice suddenly sounding like it belonged to a stranger, her hand hesitantly hovering over Rio’s knee. “What do I need to do for you to know that I want you?” 

Rio placed the softest, saddest kiss on her cheek. “Don't hide from it.” 

“From what?” 

“What you feel for me.” 

Agatha searched into those brown eyes as if Rio hadn’t already given her the obvious answer. She didn’t understand those words: “Don’t hide from it.” It was like she had missed that lesson in school, or more so, from her own parents. 

So she released her hold on Rio, ignoring the lurch in her stomach as their contact ceased. 

“George,” she snapped open the visor that blocked them from her driver. “Stop here.” 

The car ground to an abrupt halt somewhere along West 23rd Street as tourists dawdled and men in tailored suits dodged them strategically. Agatha knew that Rio was looking at her. She didn’t have to avert her gaze from the street to rid that feeling of eyes trying to pierce through her walls. 

“Out,” Agatha muttered under her breath.

The sound of the car door slamming shut had been echoing in her mind for the rest of the journey home. It was only amplified as she was met with flashes and cameras shoved against her window as Geroge pulled up to her apartment building. 

She had forgotten about this part; had forgotten that she was now the hottest, shiniest source of gossip on the East Coast. 

All she could think about was the sound of that damn door. 

“Agatha, how does it feel to have your secret out?” 

Rio had barely uttered a word as she had gotten out. 

“Ms. Harkness - over here! Can you comment on the identity of these alleged sources?” 

The only word she had given was that hidden within the noise of the entire car reverberating from her force. 

“Trouble in paradise with Mr. Bohner, Agatha?” 

Rio had never looked back. 

Her doorman, Trevor, came to her rescue just as he had done several times before. A gentle arm around her own, another blocking her face as a path forward was cleared for her to a place she could finally - hopefully - breathe. 

“You good, kid?” 

Trevor’s words had threatened to break her. He was an older gentleman and he had manned those front doors for nearly thirty years of his life. 

She remembered the first time the paparazzi came after her on the morning after she had filed for divorce from Ralph. Trevor had done just as he had done now, protected her with grace and decorum and then, once alone, offered her a sure squeeze of the shoulder and words she always remembered: “I got you kid.” 

“I will be,” she replied with a flat smile and curt nod. 

As she turned away, those same words followed her back. 

“I got you, Ms Harkness.” 

She blamed Trevor for the tear that escaped down her cheek as she got into the elevator. 

There was no time for tears the moment the elevator reached the top floor of the building, doors opening onto Agatha’s private floor. She was met immediately by the sound of Nicky causing some form of chaos through the front door; it was a much more welcome sound than that of the car door slamming shut on her chance at happiness. 

Opening the door, she was met with the sight of Sharon unpacking Nicky’s school bag, and said Nicky sprinting around the kitchen island in circles, imitating noises of the toy car he held in hand. 

“Mama!” 

Nicky noticed her immediately, pausing mid-sprint and turning on his heel to instead, hurl himself at her legs. She was sure that boy had some Pavlovian-esque association with the front door opening. That sound, to him, meant food, cuddles and safety. It was one of her biggest parenting achievements considering that her own association to the front door in childhood had never included any such thing. 

“Hey baby,” Agatha smiled the moment his body slammed into her own. Her hands found the sides of his face and she felt her shoulders ease a little as she laid eyes on the chocolate curls and bright, brown eyes of her son. “How was school?” 

Nicky’s face lit-up as he squeezed his mother tighter before balancing his feet on top of her own, like he always liked to do, swaying back and forth with a giddy smile. “Good, we were learning about volcanoes today. Did you know we have over one hundred volcanoes here?” 

“I didn’t know that,” she smiled at him. “But that’s very cool.” 

“Uh-huh!” He jumped up and down on his little feet. “Is Rio coming over tonight? I want to tell her all about it. Oh, and also, Mama! There were loads of cameras outside when we got home! Do you think someone famous is coming to the building?”

Agatha closed her eyes, gathering her breath. When she looked up, she caught Sharon offering her a forlorn look and a silent comment that felt like: “I am so sorry this has happened Agatha.” She just smiled and brushed it away with a hand - there was still no opportunity for her to break. Not whilst Nicky was here. 

“Slow down, honey,” Agatha laughed, trying to pretend that his words weren’t a punch to her gut. “I think it’s just us two tonight. Mama’s got some calls she needs to make, but we could finish that lego set if you wanted?” 

Her heart hurt even more when she watched Nicky’s face fall, before he begrudgingly agreed to her request. She felt wicked; so bad, even her own son didn’t deserve her as a mother. How would she explain to him all of this? How would she protect him from the inevitable gossip and bullying in the playground at school? How would she look her son in the face knowing he might resent her for the rest of his life?  

She knew, the only thing she could do was tell him the truth. 

“Don’t hide from it,” Rio had told her. 

She wouldn’t hide from it. Not from her own son. 

Even if it did mean she spent the rest of the afternoon dodging Nicky’s questions about why he was home for school so early and enduring a mental battle as to what she would say, and when. 

Sharon left in the late afternoon after doing two loads of laundry and preparing Nicky’s favourite dinner for them that evening, already knowing without having to be told that Agatha needed that extra bit of help that day. 

She let Nicky eat dinner on the couch beside her under the pretense of them having a ‘movie night’. Agatha even endured her own portion of dino nuggets and mac and cheese that usually she wouldn’t dare let pass her lips, but that night it was more important to show her son that he meant more to her than how anyone could perceive outside of the walls they called home. 

Once she had entertained Nicky’s own version of the big bang story through beige, battered chicken pieces, she decided she could wait no longer. 

“Nicky, I got to talk to you about something. Is that ok?” 

“Am I in trouble?" 

“No,” she said quickly, brushing her hand through his hair. “Not at all, buddy. If anything, Mama is in trouble and she needs your help.” 

Nicky’s eyes widened. “You’ve been naughty, Mama?” 

It was her natural instinct to say yes. She had to force the words down from her throat before they could escape, thankfully catching herself at the last moment. 

What kind of mother would she be if she taught her own son that being gay was wrong? 

“I’m not in trouble, really. And I certainly haven’t been naughty," she offered a small smile. “Sorry baby, it has been a really long day and I don’t think Mama is making much sense.” 

“Silly Mama,” he giggled. 

“Indeed.” Agatha said. “But there is something I need to talk to you about. Something quite important that might be a lot for you to process, and if it is - if you feel confused at any point, you can ask me anything. Ok?”’ 

“Is this going to be one of those adult talks that I’m going to hate?” 

She couldn’t hide the small laugh he inspired in her. It helped her breath a little easier, and she found herself wondering, yet again, what she had done to deserve him. 

“Most likely, honey. But I promise, if you stick with me, we’ll put a movie on and finish that lego after. How does that sound?” 

Nicky’s face lifted, his body practically bouncing from his seat. 

“Ok,” Agatha gathered her thoughts, every inch of her body shaking with the anticipation of something she had never done before. “You know how you saw those cameras outside today? On the street?” 

“Yeah, Trevor had to help Sharon and I through them. There were so many.” 

“I know, and you did so well to get through them all without being scared.” She gathered her breath before continuing. “They weren’t here because someone famous was coming to the building. They were here because of me.” 

“Because of you?” He looked confused. “Mama, did you ask them to be there?” 

“No, I didn’t ask them to be there.” 

“Then why?” 

“You know how Mama’s work means she is on television a lot?” 

Nicky nodded astutely. 

It had taken months of back-and-forth within her own mind on whether her son should know that his mother was in the public eye. It was something she had grown up being thrust into without the opportunity to say no, and that was the last thing she wanted for him to endure without his consent first. 

But at the age of four, Nicky started asking questions about her work and why she had to leave so early and Agatha kept telling him that she “told people the news.” 

It wasn’t until Nicky turned five and spent the day at home with a stomach bug that she received a phone call from Sharon mid-morning telling her that her son was in tears because he had seen her on television; he was apparently confused first, and then scared that the television had “eaten Mama.” 

She had returned back from work earlier that day, and sat down with Nicky on the couch, just as she did now, and explained to him exactly why she was on the television. Ironically, she had to spend thirty minutes prior explaining to him that the television had, in fact, not eaten her. 

“Well, because I am on television a lot, that means that sometimes people who watch me on television become interested about my life, even if they don’t actually know me personally. It is just like how we report on our President. Our President is just a normal person, like you and me. You could be President if you wanted to be.”

“I could?” 

Nicky’s face lit-up like he had just promised her a week full of christmas mornings. 

She nodded. “You could. You’d make a very excellent president, all things considered.” 

Nicky seemed to take this as gospel, and started muttering about how he would one day become the leader of their country. 

“Anyway, honey, what I am trying to tell you…” she reached for his hand, causing him to look up at her with those big, brown eyes that now hurt a little more than usual to look at because she realised that those same big, brown eyes were the ones that she had let get out of a car and slam the door on her just a few hours earlier. 

“Today, somebody who does not know me, published a story about me that lots of other people who do not know me, have now read. In this story, they have found out some parts of my life that I choose to keep hidden. And I don’t choose to keep those things hidden because I am ashamed of them, or because they scare me. I keep them hidden to keep them safe.” 

“Like me?” 

It had been a conversation that mother and son had shared after Nicky had managed to grasp the concept of fame, and that his mother belonged into that category. He had asked if he, too, was famous and Agatha had explained that she chose to keep that part of her life private, because it deserved its chance to blossom without the scrutiny of the entire world. 

“Just like you.” 

“What have they found out? That you didn’t want them to find out?” 

"Well, that's exactly what I wanted to talk to you about. You know how adults sometimes choose to be with other adults? As girlfriends and boyfriends, husbands and wives?” 

“Yeah… like Aunt Wanda and Uncle Vis?”

“Exactly like them,” she smiled and took a deep breath. This was the moment. There was no going back from this. The first time ever in her life that she was doing this and she knew it would go one of two ways: her son would know who she was, truly and completely, or her son would never want anything to do with her ever again. 

“What I am trying to tell you, baby, and this is hard for Mama, because Mama hasn’t told anyone this before, ok? You’re the first person who gets to know. You’re the person who will always get to know first.” 

Nicky seemed excited by this news, like it was a special secret between them both. Agatha could only hope that he would keep seeing it that way after she had unveiled the truth fully. 

“I know,” Nicky told her like he had not spent only seven years on this earth. “So you don’t have an Uncle Vis?” 

She should have been thankful that her sweet boy was doing most of the work for her. 

“I don’t have one,” she said. “Or… I didn’t have one, but I have been becoming friends with someone who I think could be that someone for me.” 

She hadn’t seen before the face that Nicky had presented her with. It was too adult for such a small child to wear - a raising of his brows and a slight smirk on his lips. 

“Mama, do you have a boyfriend?” 

He asked with such simplicity that it hurt her more than she had expected. Because that was what he expected; that was what every small child expected. They had been brought up to know that girls had boyfriends and boys had girlfriends. That babies had both a mother and a father. 

“No, I don’t have a boyfriend,” were the only words she could get out of her mouth. 

“But they’re saying you do?” 

“No, they’re not.” 

“... Mama, I’m confused.” 

“I know, baby,” she reached for him, her arms encircling his waist and pulling him closer against her chest. “I don’t have a boyfriend," she said before taking one more breath. “And I don’t want a boyfriend.” 

Nicky looked up at her like she had hung every single star in the sky for over a millenia. 

“... I won’t ever want a boyfriend, because I don’t want to be with a man. Do you understand? I don’t want a boyfriend, but I would quite like, one day, to have a girlfriend.” 

Nicky’s eyes widened slightly, his little mouth forming a perfect ‘o’ that he often did when the part of his movie had gotten really good. 

“A girlfriend?” 

Agatha’s nod was tentative. “How do you feel about that, baby?” 

Nicky chewed on his words for a while before offering a sly smile. “I’m ok with you having a girlfriend. As long as it is Rio. It really should be Rio, actually. She basically lives with us anyway. And, she’s really cool and… I just want you to be happy, Mama. She makes you happy, right?” 

Her sweet, sweet boy. 

He would never know the extent at which his words threatened to split her in half. She hadn’t expected him to be so accepted, but to be so eloquent whilst he did it? To state the obvious as if it was just that: obvious. It left her eyes shaking and her lip trembling as her fist scratched at her neck to avoid any tears from spilling. 

“She does make me happy, buddy. Nearly as happy as you make me.” 

Agatha succeeded in keeping the tears at bay for the rest of the evening, whilst Nicky cuddled up beside her and they completed his lego set and they watched the orca documentary for at least the seventh time. 

When she was sure that her boy had escaped to the place where the real world could not hurt him, Agatha retreated to her own bedroom, drew the curtains, collapsed into her bed and finally, finally let herself cry. 

She cried for the little boy who had been produced from anything but love, and had succeeded in teaching her how to love, and offered her the permission she had needed to continue loving others in the way he had taught her. 

She cried for the woman who slammed the car door behind her earlier that day. That same woman who she had not been able to get out of her mind for months now, and who she would go through this entire ordeal several times over just to be able to say “she is mine.”  

Most of all, she cried for every version of herself that had spent their life's work pretending to be something they were not.

Chapter End Notes

NOT OUR WEE BABIES IN A FIGHT

Chapter 10: As The World Caves In

Chapter Notes

once again evanora is being a homophobic bitch and im sorry

See the end of the chapter for more notes

New York had turned grey, the air biting in a way it hadn’t been for weeks. It was fitting, given Agatha could think of nothing worse than leaving the confines of her apartment that weekend. Not after that article on her had dropped. 

She had avoided her phone just as she avoided live television, despite her son having an affinity to any pixelated screens in the sense that if he did not have at least one in his vicinity, he would start climbing the walls. 

Regardless of how hard she tried to avoid facing the reality of how the world now saw her, Agatha had seen a few of the text messages from friends and colleagues - some genuinely kind and others she knew were only looking to sink their teeth into some gossip. 

On Saturday, she had faltered slightly in her abstinence and ended up switching on her phone and searching up her name online. It had been a moment of weakness - one she was not proud of - but Rio had ignored three of her calls and she had consumed several G&T’s, so what was one more unhealthy habit added to the list? 

YDA: What is going on behind the doors of UBA and why is the CEO's daughter, Agatha Harkness, being targeted? 

TMZ: Did Agatha Harkness leak this story herself just because she was too scared to come out? 

Eagle News: Homo-Harkness - who would have ever guessed? 

Page Six: EVERYTHING we know on the Vidal and Harkness romance! Plus: Deep dive into who has it out for Harkness

She should have known she would regret reading what the world had to say. She wasn’t surprised that UBA had avoided coming out with their own version of the story, but she was surprised that Eagle News had even dared to put their own spin on the narrative. She could only imagine Ralph’s smug face as he signed off on the copy. When she had first read the headline, she had to put the mug she was holding back against the countertop for fear that she would throw it across the room and smash it into a wall. 

She most likely would have done so, if Nicky weren’t with her. 

On Sunday, after a heated game of charades post-dinner, Agatha and Nicky found themselves curled into one another under several blankets in the den. The den was a smaller playroom and quasi-cinema. It was also their calm place. 

The couch was a bed more than a couch and complete with the softest of blankets and more pillows than were actually necessary. The space maintained a serene feel with a glorious view of the Hudson that allowed her mind to breathe in tandem with the plants that surrounded her - plants that were only alive thanks to Sharon, and Agatha’s cleaner. 

That night the room didn’t feel so calm. 

Agatha couldn’t quite put her finger on it; she held Nicky tighter than usual, counting his breaths as dragons and vikings united as one on the screen. Work was on her mind, of course. How she would show her face in front of everybody tomorrow. How she would come to her decision about choosing her career or choosing her relationship. How she would cope with the inevitable stand-off with her mother. 

As luck had it, she didn’t have to wait long to find out. 

The doorbell sounded more violently than usual. 

She felt it in her ears; in the way Nicky’s body jolted in her arms. The remote slipped out of her hand twice as she tried to press the pause button. 

“Wait here, honey.” 

Nicky looked back at her with his eyes wide, looking so much younger than he was. 

It wasn’t often that she got an unannounced visitor. Trevor had a list of vetted guests he could allow through the building and Agatha was usually aware of any that were incoming. Truthfully, it was rare she got a visitor at all and it was certainly intentional on Agatha’s part. 

Thank god for the invention of peepholes. 

But being able to see who was standing outside her front door did not make it any easier to actually see who was standing outside her front door. 

At least she had a chance to press play on the audio recording app of her phone. 

As she opened the door, she considered if it would be like opening Pandora’s Box, letting in all that evil into her home. 

It certainly felt like being stood opposite evil when she came face to face with Evanora Harkness, complete with her tight chin, rigid shoulders and eyes cold enough to burn. 

Agatha couldn’t help but chuckle. “At this hour?” 

“You should be thankful I’m doing the decent thing of wasting my time on you at all.” 

She should have known that was coming. 

“I don’t typically invite people that I dislike into my home.” 

“Then you won’t have a job to come to tomorrow.” 

Begrudgingly, she opened the door a little wider. 

Evanora swooped past her, her eyes inspecting every inch of the apartment. Agatha could already sense her distaste for the lighter, mid-century look that was unafraid to show a bit of colour. Agatha’s interior designer had done an impeccable job, she had to say, but it couldn’t differ further from the moth-bitten curtains and excessive amount of mahogany in her mother’s brownstone on the Upper West Side. 

“Aren’t you going to offer your mother a drink, Agatha?” 

“You won’t be staying long enough to need one.” Agatha hissed. “Go on then, spit it out.” 

“I am here to discuss how we rectify this mess you have made.” 

“A mess that I have made?” Agatha’s laugh was cold. “I think you’re pointing the finger at the wrong person in this room.”

That was the match that lit Evanora’s fuse. 

“You have been a foolish, sorry excuse for a mother. Do you not see what you have done?” Evanora’s voice began to raise with each word that spat from her mouth. “Parading around with that woman to such an extremity that the world is alluding to such abhorrent rumours about you! You are polluting that boy’s mind and you are polluting our family name!” 

“This has nothing to do with how I parent my child.” 

“It has everything to do with it. Every one of your actions will be scrutinised by the media for the rest of your life - you signed up for this.” 

Agatha wanted to scream; she had never, ever signed up for this life.  

“There is no world in which these rumours can be true whilst you also represent my network, and my family name. Do you understand me?” 

“Let me get this right… you don’t give a shit about the fact that one of your senior talent had their phone hacked, you simply only care who I sleep with?” Agatha’s head shook in disbelief. “You’re not concerned by the apparent failing of those fancy security systems you had installed last quarter? Haven’t got a few skeletons in your closet that you want to remain hidden?” 

“What the hell are you suggesting?” 

“...Mama?”

Agatha turned around, finding Nicky stood in the shadows of the hall with a blanket wrapped over his shoulders and held up against his mouth in tight, shaking fists. 

She didn’t think her heart could drop anymore. 

“Baby I told you to stay there-”

Agatha caught herself on the term of endearment so brazenly used in front of her mother, something she had never done or ever been in a position of needing to do. It didn’t matter how quickly she stopped herself. She still caught the way Evanora’s nose turned up and her lips pursed together; it was as if she believed that could prevent any of the warmth from seeping into her cold, cracked skin. 

“Nicholas,” Evanora’s words were void of any emotion but Agatha did not miss the way her eyes singled him out from across the room. “My, my… Haven’t you grown?” 

Agatha snapped.

“Don’t you dare talk to him!” 

She turned away, straight towards her son and without a second thought lifted him into her arms until he rested against her hip. Yes, he was getting far too big to do this now and yes, Agatha mourned it everyday. She would be damned if she had to stop now. 

He clung to her like he knew this strange woman in his home meant trouble. 

“Is she hurting you?” Nicky’s voice was a whisper against her neck. A whisper so soft it hurt. 

“No, honey,” she said as she carried him to his bedroom, furthest away from the exposure of the front door. “We’re just having a grown up talk, ok? You get into bed for me and read some more of your book. I’ll be back before you can finish it.” 

She hated seeing the lack of conviction on his face as she retreated into the darkness that his dinosaur-shaped lamplight didn’t quite reach. 

His stuffed rabbit was clutched under his chin and Agatha didn’t know how she was going to leave her boy looking like that. 

“Promise?” 

His voice was uncharacteristically small, in a way that reminded Agatha of who she had been as a small child, never knowing when she was allowed to speak or not. She hadn’t seen that in her own son before. 

“I promise.” The smile she gave him hurt. “Always.” 

She returned to the foyer a different person than she had been when her mother had knocked at her door. This lady - this stranger to her in every way but blood - had scared her child, and she would never forgive Evanora for that. 

“You don’t ever get to speak to him again. Am I clear?” 

Evanora laughed the same way that Agatha had seen her laugh when she fired their housemaid back when she was a teenager. After her cackles had drowned out, her eyes narrowed and her heels clicked against the floor as she took a step closer. 

“Let me be very, very clear, Agatha. Tomorrow, you have a choice. You fix this or you leave. I want you to dispel these rumours on-air tomorrow, during your apology for allowing people to think they could have access into your private lives, or that they can create such vicious rumours that threaten the integrity of your family’s livelihoods. Do you understand?”

“You’ve made it very clear where you stand on this issue.” 

“Good,” Evanora offered a tight-lipped smile that looked unnatural on her face. “Now it's time for you to make that same decision. Goodnight.”  

So Sunday evening, she cried again.

Monday arrived entirely unwelcome. Her sleep had been broken, her mind a never-ending cycle that thought about Rio, that thought about Nicky, that thought about the career she had spent her entire professional life dedicated to only to now face losing it altogether. 

She slipped from her apartment before the sun had risen, her pointed kitten heels clicking against the marble floors and shades already resting at the top of her head despite the hour and obvious lack of light. 

Rio ended up ignoring her all morning. 

Not ignoring her, per se. More like actively staying out of Agatha’s way. 

Usually, Rio would bee-line to her dressing room, no doubt to make some crude joke that Agatha would end up rolling her eyes at but smiling at her nonetheless.

The last thing she wanted to do was sit beside the woman she had hurt and dragged into this mess whilst also having to go on camera before the nation that had the entire weekend to feast away at her own downfall. 

Her mother’s words played in the back of her mind like a broken record. She had one last opportunity to do the right thing. One last chance to ensure she didn’t lose everything.

“Agatha…” Lilia’s brows furrowed. “What are you up to?” 

“Please,” Agatha’s stare deepened. “Trust me… and don’t let her into the studio until I'm finished.”

“Harkness!” Lilia called. “What do you mean ‘finished’?”

“I hope you know what you’re doing,” Rio muttered under her breath.

“And we’re live,” their assistant producer began to call out. “In Six.”

“Trust me,” Agatha murmured. “Please, just trust me.” 

“Four.”

Agatha returned the pleasantries, even if the falsity hurt her teeth. 

She couldn’t quite find the words, no matter how hard she tried; only a returned smile could suffice. She forced a cough and gathered the stack of paper in her hands. 

“Yes, thank you, Rio.” 

Her eyes found the camera, her throat gulping one last time. 

“Last Friday, a news article was published about me,” her words started off with a shake that no one would associate with an esteemed anchor with over fifteen years experience. “This piece was not only defamatory, but it claims to have access to my private communications. “That article did access my private communications. It was a breach of personal and intimate parts of my life that I should be entitled to not have broadcast without my consent, especially at the hands of people who I should be able to trust. Unfortunately, there is someone in my inner circle that I can no longer trust, and I am still as unaware as you are about who that is.”

She exhaled a lifetime worth of secrets.

Fucking hell, Agatha, you just said you love her.

There are people - people with power, with influence - in this company who are biased, discriminatory and oppose human rights that they claim to support.”

Everybody who remained in the studio was watching them. 

I hope you’re happy with your decision, Agatha. I told you not to let this…” Evanora’s voice had quietened. She eyed up Rio with a scowl, “her… be the cause of your downfall.” 

“My only downfall was not doing this sooner,” Agatha snapped. 

Rio gently tugged at her arm. “Come on,” she whispered. “Let’s go, Agatha.” 

Agatha refused to break her stare from Evanora until Evanora did so herself, clenching her jaw and turning on her heel with a small huff. 

“Wait.” 

Evanora’s head snapped around, her brows arched. 

“I just have one more question,” Agatha’s voice was calm, her smile composed. She made sure it was loud enough for everybody to hear it. “Then you don’t have to hear from me ever again.” 

“Make it quick,” the woman hissed. 

“Was it my mother or my ex-husband that hacked into my phone?” 

Agatha didn’t miss the way Evanora’s icy eyes widened slightly, nor the tension that overcame her entire body. Rio stood beside her, trying to hide her smirk. 

“Tell Stark I said hello,” she called as security escorted them down the hall.

“One word from you about what I said back there and I retract it entirely.” 

Rio grinned, holding both her hands up in defence after they had escaped into Agatha’s waiting Mercedes - courtesy of George and his efficient response times. “I’m saying nothing.” 

It had only been two minutes and thirty-two seconds - yes, Agatha had counted - until Rio gave in and opened her mouth. 

“But we kinda…” Agatha sighed at Rio’s words. “We do need to talk about that. And everything else. Like, are you going to dump me on the street again? Because I’d really prefer somewhere a bit more… off the beaten track, so I don’t get my ass mauled by the paps.” 

“I thought you were saying nothing.” 

Rio hedged her bets and remained silent for the remainder of the journey, pleasantly surprised to discover that she had arrived outside Agatha’s building and not offloaded along a random street that left her dodging the finance bros and flashing cameras all at once. 

On this occasion, she hadn’t quite managed to avoid the flashing cameras. There was a sizable, and clearly growing, group of paparazzi to the side of the entrance, Trevor stood before them to prevent any further movement. 

Rio couldn’t help but chuckle under her breath. “They don’t wait around.”

It may have only been mid-morning but Agatha would have believed anyone who had told her it had been several months of grueling, penniless labour of both her mind and her heart. 

The drain didn’t just wash the day away, it took with it the last thirty nine years spent living to appease somebody else. She came out of that shower with a clarity she had never expected to feel after such a tumultuous re-arranging of her life. 

But Rio was waiting for her in an oversized baseball shirt and boxers, hair in a bun that Agatha couldn’t decipher was purposefully messy or not and Agatha did not care. She couldn’t care because Rio was there waiting for her and Nicky would be home in a few hours and Agatha would finally have everything that she needed. 

“Hi.”

Agatha’s words were a breathless exhale, her gaze on Rio who stood behind the kitchen counter, watching her every move. 

Rio’s lips curled. “Hi.” 

They seemed to gravitate towards one another like it was destined for them to do so, in that very moment, on that very day, after such an arduous journey to get there. They held each other and breathed each other in. It was the first time Agatha had properly breathed all day. 

“You’ve been surprisingly calm about this,” Rio murmured as Agatha lifted her head and found Rio’s stare. 

“I’ve had all weekend not to be,” she said. “Oh, and it felt really fucking good to see that look on my mother’s face earlier. God bless adrenaline.” 

Rio laughed softly, taking Agatha’s hand and leading her to the couch. “Sit,” she instructed with a finality that caught Agatha’s attention. “What are you drinking?” 

After Rio had made them both a coffee - or several coffees after realising her first attempt was not up to Agatha’s standard of frothiness - they both took stock of their morning curled up by one another on the couch. 

“Lilia called me,” Rio murmured between sips, like it wouldn’t blow Agatha’s eyes out of their socket. “Whilst you were in the shower.” 

“She what?” 

“Evanora gave her a lashing and sent her home too. Not suspended though… just on the receiving end of that old hag’s temper tantrum, I guess. Anyway, Lilia met with Alice and Jen after work - actually, they’re together now at the only open Irish bar.” 

“You wanted to tell me they’re getting drunk?” 

“No,” Rio’s smile widened. “Better. They’re discussing exactly how to help you. Or us.” 

“I don’t need their help.” 

“You’re just going to give up? We have so much that could bring her down-” 

Agatha sighed. “We’re not about to get into the mystery mobile, Rio. I don’t need a team.” 

“Mystery Machine, Agatha,” Rio tried to hold back her laughter. “Mystery Machine.” 

“Oh, whatever!” 

“You’re an idiot,” Rio muttered, before shaking her shoulders back. “Ok, answer me this. What evidence do you have? Against Evanora?” 

“... The finance spreadsheets. Knowing she was contacting Stark.” 

“And you have proof? That she was contacting Stark?” 

Agatha watched Rio, her lips trembling in a snarl she desperately tried to hold back. “You infuriate me.” 

“Lilia has access to the newsroom systems online; that includes executive edits of segments, coverage and copies. Combined together, Jen and Alice have the entire US in their contacts. Plus. My source, of course.” Rio was looking at her with hopeful brows arched. “Agatha, it would be stupid not to.” 

Agatha’s jaw was tight. 

“...Whatever.”

They both knew that was the only approval she would ever give. 

“Also, your phone. You’re not still using it, are you?” 

“I am,” Agatha said. “It’s not like I’ve been going around texting people the entire extent of our investigation. I haven’t texted anyone, for that fact… Apart from Sharon. And Jen.” 

Rio might as well have clawed her nails down her face with the eye roll she had just offered Agatha. “Will you please let my guy take a look at it? They’ll track how they infiltrated the device -”

“Do you ever shut up?”

“Agatha, this is important.” 

Agatha huffed, handing her phone over. “Who’s your ‘guy’?” 

“Natasha Romanoff. Background in cybersecurity, experience with organised crime networks. Helped me out on a few occasions in this line of work.”

Agatha’s eyes widened. “That’s not a guy!” 

“Mi amor, not this again.” 

“Excuse me?” Agatha watched Rio catch what had just come out of her own mouth, them both as shocked as each other. “Did you just-” 

Rio’s lips curled. “Apparently so,” and before Agatha could stop her, Rio was letting her torso collapse into Agatha’s side, worming her back against her chest. “Purely in response to your little declaration earlier.”

“Perhaps I need to get my ears tested. I was sure someone mentioned something about who you choose to love?” 

Agatha’s hands tightened across Rio’s chest, her chin resting on Rio’s shoulder. “It was all for the press, honey.” 

“Oh yeah?”

“Yeah,” Agatha raised her brows in defiance. “You’re not that important,” she whispered as her hand began to trail up the side of Rio’s face. 

Rio put all her weight into Agatha’s palm, as if she was releasing a sigh she had been holding in for days. Her eyes fluttered shut, her breath exhaling. 

“I am the one in your arms right now…” 

“Oh look, Miss. Observant over here.” 

“You make it impossible not to tune into every detail, mi amor.” 

“Mmh,” Agatha sighed. “Say that again.” 

“Mi amor,” Rio’s voice had lowered, her own hand taking Agatha’s cheeks into her hands before she leant in and placed the softest of kisses against the ridge of her nose. “Let me kiss you?” 

“Only if you promise to do much worse to me afterwards.” 

Rio smiled. “Deal.”

Chapter 11: All For Us

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

They say that all the mighty should fall; that power was a figment of a fool’s mind. 

Nobody could conquer it all. Not whilst hurting so many along the way. The martyr and the sinner cannot co-exist as one. It was the natural order that required balance and nature was not to be messed with. 

Agatha wondered if this counted - as messing with nature, that is. She wondered if she would be punished for becoming a martyr from stopping a sinner, even if she had sinned herself. Then again, could her sins count as sins when they were coined as sins by the sinner? 

It was all too confusing and much too philosophical to be debating alone in her head at nearly three-thirty in the morning. Sleep had been a thing of the past and in the last week, Agatha had experienced a new level of delirium that she thought impossible considering she had been doing early-morning television for fifteen years, and had one stint with a newborn for additional experience. 

It was impossible to close her eyes when all she saw was everything she had done wrong in the past, and everything she could have done to avoid being in this situation now. 

She had always loved control, courtesy of her precarious childhood and neglectful caregivers; to lose it so astronomically at the hands of one person clicking publish… 

She had never felt so exposed. 

Not even at the hands of her mother; not even when forced beneath Ralph. 

Everything had been taken from her. 

She could only trust that their plan was enough to take it all back. 

“Agatha,” a croaky murmur sounded from beside her, an arm fumbling across her dark waves until a hand found her face, patting lightly. “There you are. C’me ‘ear.” 

The sound of Rio’s voice was a brief reprieve from the worry. Agatha was still getting used to having someone in her bed with her, after years of waking up to it empty, or with a small child’s limb digging into her back. She had never experienced the act of someone being there to comfort her, she had only ever been there to comfort Nicky. 

For some reason that Agatha could not explain, Rio made it easier to learn these new routines like allowing her back to ease against Rio’s chest, or not letting her heart jump at the feel of fingers in her hair. Rio was never hard, or abrupt. Each movement was pronounced and delicate. Purposeful in a way that showed she cared. 

“Agatha,” Rio whispered again. Her arm loosely draped across Agatha’s chest, her hand tracing the outline of her jaw. “You’re allowed to sleep, don’t let her take that from you as well.” 

“I’ll sleep when she’s behind bars,” Agatha huffed. “Or, preferably, when she’s six-feet-under.”

Despite Rio being half-asleep and behind her, Agatha knew she would be smirking. 

That was Agatha’s every night after being outed to the world. Rio had offered to stay over each night and each night, Agatha would shrug her shoulders and offer a brief nod before asking what Rio wanted for dinner. Rio would typically not get what she initially asked for after Nicky got involved and demanded something more child-friendly and much more beige. 

Nicky hadn’t enquired too much into his mother’s reasons for having her colleague over to stay so much. He knew they were friends and he knew that Rio was cooler than his mother so he was typically ecstatic to see her. 

Nicky and Rio had just clicked like they had never been apart from one another. There were little other ways to put it; the pair were thick as thieves.

When Nicky had realised that Rio was waiting at home for him on Monday afternoon, he had bolted past his mother to give Rio a hug, a high-five and an in-depth explanation into the legitimate threat of active volcanoes in America. Agatha hadn’t even minded; she had been so concerned that his classmates would say something to him at school, despite ensuring that Sharon had discussed it with his teachers the morning she had dropped him off, that it was a relief to see him so happy upon returning. 

Her son hadn’t said anything further about Rio being in his home, but Agatha had to hold back her laughter when Nicky attempted to offer her a wink when Rio was not looking. 

Regardless of her position - of lack thereof - at UBA, having the only two people she needed by her side, both smiling and both there for her… it made it all worth it. 

Agatha had never seen her boy warm to someone so quick but any time Rio would walk through their apartment door, he would run towards her, reach for her hand and drag her into his playroom so he could show off his latest lego set. 

She had always raised Nicky alone. Sure, Sharon helped when Agatha had to work, but she had been certain that her son would know his mother, and be raised by his mother, unlike Agatha’s own experience in childhood. Having Rio around was a first for both Agatha and Nicky but to any outsider, they would assume the trio had been together for years. 

Deep down, through all the stress and humiliation, Agatha was able to enjoy her time with Rio, and their time with Nicky. She considered that she deserved at least one good thing amongst the shit-storm of the past week. And she hoped it could, somehow, continue. 

The next morning came with full offence. The budding warmth of the spring sun was too cheerful for Agatha’s sleep-weakened eyes, and caffeine only added to her anxieties. 

She had been less anxious with Rio around, that she could not deny, but that morning was the first day that would determine the outcome to this utter shit-show. 

With both Agatha and Rio suspended, Alice and Jen had been put on leave too, meaning Lilia was their only remaining tie to getting inside of UBA. The three producers had created a call to action behind Agatha’s back - much to her annoyance - and that day was the first day they would be convening on how to take Evanora Harkness down. 

Most annoyingly of all, they were doing it at Agatha’s apartment. 

Agatha was surprised Alice was willingly coming to her apartment, let alone wanting to help her reclaim the narrative over her life. Rio had claimed that Alice actually believed in Agatha, despite their hostility towards one another. Agatha didn’t believe Rio at all, having muttered something about Alice only bothering because her “shiny superstar” had been thrown into the firing line along with her. Nevertheless, the two producers reached out to Lilia and next thing Agatha knew, Rio was adding her to a heavily-encrypted text chain titled Lets Bring These Fuckers Down.

At 06.50, she started to get that same itch she had gotten for the last four days. It was an itch that left the television remote staring at her like a big, red button with a sign beside it saying Do Not Touch. She wanted to touch it; she wanted to know what was being broadcast on her show, even if it wasn’t technically her show anymore. 

Her finger must have slipped, as the television turned on and displayed the advertisements. Agatha couldn’t halt the snigger in her throat as she clocked that several brands had clearly dropped their deals with UBA in the wake of their public family-feud and dismissal. 

It was the least Evanora deserved. 

Each limb in Agatha’s body seized at the first note of the show’s familiar introductory music. She was supposed to be on that chair, listening to that music as she watched her AD count her in. She wasn’t supposed to be standing in a kitchen, watching with a coffee as every other viewer did. 

The only time she had ever tuned in to the breakfast show willingly was whilst on maternity leave from having Nicky, and that only lasted eight weeks until Evanora was forcing her back into the office because Ralph wasn’t seeing eye-to-eye with their temporary female host. 

Now, she watched another stranger take her seat like it was their own and this time she didn’t have the luxury of returning to reclaim it. 

Well, Darcy wasn’t a stranger but Agatha liked to pretend she was. 

Seeing Jimmy sat beside her, where Rio usually sat, with his square head, square spectacles and square-fucking grin. She loathed that man. He wasn’t as bad as Ralph - she doubted anyone could be as bad as Ralph - but Jimmy had a similar cockiness to him. A cockiness that Agatha found most men that she met possessed

It probably had a lot to do with why she hated most men.

“Hey,” Agatha hissed. “I was watching that.”

Instead of the peaceful and intentionally stress-free environment she liked to maintain in her home, it had turned to a make-shift war room. Then again, it was an accurate reflection of the shift from order to chaos that had transpired in her own life that past week.

Besides Agatha, Jen had seemingly given up on her portion of the work, instead she focused on the sushi she had brought for herself and no one else. 

Opposite Jen, Alice sat - if you could call it that. Agatha had been watching her, for the last five minutes, attempt to push her crossed legs and upper-body up from the seat with her palms balanced against the seat of her chair. 

With that, and the incessant chewing coming from Rio’s teeth against the lid of a pen, it was safe to say that Agatha was losing what little patience she had. 

“Alright,” Rio started. “Jen - could we park the lunch break for five more minutes?” 

“But I need to hit my protein intake before evening-” 

“Jen,” Agatha interrupted, her hand reaching to prise the chopsticks from Jen’s grasp. “The smell is offensive. If you would rather side with my homophobic, racist cunt of a mother, you and your protein can leave for all I care.”

“Yes. I have show copies before and after executive edits. Everything that was edited out has, of course, been redacted, but I have an email from the powers that be above regarding neutral political coverage. Was sent out to all senior producers.”
