“Anything we can actually get them on?” 

“I would say that this entire page of redacted segments is pretty pertinent,” Jen quipped, holding up a document with an excessive chunk of writing blackened out. 

“Jesus, have I taught you nothing?” Agatha swiped the document from Jen’s hands before glancing over it. “The only words not redacted are the show dates. We don’t know what they didn’t want to air, Jennifer. It’s useless. Catch up.” 

“It says, ‘executive override - do not air’ in block capitals,” Jen near-exclaimed. “That sounds like censorship to me.” 

Agatha’s face found the palms of her hands, her head lightly banging against the table as she groaned. “We’re fucked. Absolutley fucked,” her voice was muffled against her hands until she looked up, eyes finding Rio’s. “This - these people - you seriously thought we could do this?” 

“She was just trying to help…” 

Agatha’s head snapped towards Alice, her jaw tight and eyes locked onto her like prey. “She’s not trying hard enough,” she retorted. 

“Anyway,” Rio said quickly, forcing a smile. “What about this, here? Someone changed the words ‘anti-LGBTQ legislations’ to ‘controversial social policy’. It’s not much, but it shows that Evanora is shying away from criticism of Stark, whilst projecting her personal beliefs onto things. The versions are time-stamped, so we can use them.” 

“Oh brilliant, it has taken us all but two hours to conclude that we only have one piece of evidence,” Agatha murmured. 

“I mean, that as a piece of evidence coupled with your suspension for being gay doesn’t look great…” Alice’s words were tentative which only got under Agatha’s skin. What pissed her off even more was just how correct Alice was, accompanied by the unnecessary reminder that she had, in fact, been subject to having her privacy stolen from her.  

“What have we got on Wanda?” 

“Err-” Rio glanced at her laptop. “That one junior reporter on evening news who was reassigned to research after they published a piece criticising Stark. He’s still not been allowed back.” 

Agatha looked pensive, her fingers scratching at her chin. “They’re willing to corroborate?” 

Alice nodded. “Got a copy of an email he received from HR, citing his removal was due to ‘political views unaligned with the ethos of UBA’.” 

Agatha nearly laughed. “That’s not good enough!” 

Jen’s head turned around to face her. “Excuse me?” 

“Agatha is correct,” Lilia’s voice was, annoyingly, the voice of reason, though Agatha appreciated the support nonetheless. “We are trying to pinpoint this entirely on Evanora. An email from HR is not enough to do that.” 

Agatha glanced at the clock, desperate to see it was an appropriate time to have a shot of bourbon. Unfortunately, it hadn’t even reached past midday yet and she was already too-aware of the amount of days she had recently reached for that bottle. 

Instead, she settled on the idea of another coffee, even if it did run the risk of leaving her skin crawling from a caffeine overdose. Agatha ignored the group’s protests as she got up from her seat and walked into the kitchen. Her head had become clouded with the overwhelming reality that they were fighting a losing battle and any moment of reprieve she could steal would be welcomed. 

It was just as the beans were grinding that the doorbell sounded. She cursed under her breath, hoping to god that it was the kind face of her doorman with another hoard of parcels for her, and not an unsolicited caller that certainly shouldn’t have access to her private residence. In her line of work, unfortunately, it had become a common occurrence. 

The last thing she expected upon opening the door, was to be met with a boy. She didn’t quite know if he was a boy, or a man. He could have been cosplaying as either if she were to take a guess. His hair was dark and tightly curled, his skin pale and clothing far too oversized for his pencil-like frame. 

Agatha wondered if NYU had taught their sophomore journalists about vox-popping again. That had been an awful few weeks; any budding student jumped at the chance of an impromptu and unsolicited interview with anchor-guru, Agatha Harkness, even if it did mean hunting down her address. 

“Rio,” Agatha all-but screamed through the house. “Why is there a child at my front door?” 

Rio quickly rounded the corner as the boy stared up at Agatha with doe-eyes. “Oh, William,” she smiled. “You made it.’ 

Just as the boy - William, apparently - exhaled a sigh of relief, Agatha held her hand out in front of the doorway. “Stop,” she hissed. “You don’t get to take another step until you tell me why the hell you’re in my home.” 

Agatha felt a hand at the small of her back, Rio stepping closer. “Agatha,” she said through a deep breath. “Meet the man who has access to all of your mother’s encrypted files and communications.” 

“Oh,” Agatha’s eyes narrowed, her hands flicking strands of hair from the front of her shoulders as she remembered the shaking twig of a boy who happened to also be personal assistant to her mother. “It’s you.” 

“Agatha, William,” Rio continued. “Wiliam, Agatha,” she clapped her hands together. “Great! Let’s get started then shall-” 

“Man?” Agatha spat out a laugh. “Now that you mention it, I would recognise those hideous ankle-bashers anywhere. How’s life on the executive floor treating you, teenager?” 

William shifted nervously, his head bowed to the floor. 

Rio’s shoulder bumped into Agatha’s, perhaps with a little too much force. Agatha was too angry to notice. “William is going to help us, Agatha.” 

“Help us?” Agatha's laugh was bitter. “More like report back to her on everything we’re doing. How can you trust him?” 

“Oh, we’ve had some words together,” Rio’s eyes narrowed as she looked at William. “Haven’t we, Kaplan?” 

William looked up and nodded astutely, even as his cheeks began to rouge. “What you’re doing is admirable. What she has done to you… I’m gay. I get it.” 

“No way, really?” Agatha mocked. “Who would have known?” 

Rio’s hand found Agatha’s arm, squeezing it lightly. “Agatha-” 

“I have screenshots,” William said. “Of messages between your mother, and Tony Stark.” 

And holy-hell, the last thing Agatha had expected to be her saving grace was a pre-pubescent twink. 

Agatha tapped her foot against the floor, looking the boy up and down. "What else?”

“Emails between Stark and Ms. Harkness. Emails between Stark’s campaign team and Ms. Harkness. A HR report with redacted names set for termination.” 

“And you’ve gotten this information how, exactly? PA’s don’t get given access to everything.” 

“I slept with someone on executive communications,” William blurted out. “They’ve helped me out with it all.” 

“This is your source?” Agatha turned to Rio, astonished. “It’s a child. A literal child.” 

“Hey, he just told you he slept with someone for information that could put your mother behind bars. Give the guy some credit.”

“Sounds familiar,” Agatha scowled towards Rio. “You and I are having words later.” 

“Lucky me,” Rio muttered under her breath. 

Agatha turned back to William, her jaw tight. “You can stay,” William’s face broke into a smile, “but, shoes off, do not touch anything and keep those grubby fingers from my couch.” 

“Agatha, you have a seven year old-” 

“Who knows not to put his grubby fingers anywhere!” 

Much to Agatha’s dismay, since William had joined them, a plan to take Evanora Harkness down had begun to take shape. They now had evidence that Agatha could have only hoped to have gotten her hands on - if only her mother had loved her enough to use her name in her passwords. 

William didn’t just provide evidence, he gave them damning proof that Evanora and Stark were working together without any consultation by the board of UBA, and that their work consisted of some very controversial, unprofessional matters. 

There had been a memo from Stark, indicating that “Maximoff is becoming a liability. We need clear-cut talent moving forward into this election cycle.” Ironically, the memo had been sent prior to Wanda’s so-called ‘resignation’. 

There had been an email from Evanora to Stark that specified: “Once our acquisition phase is complete, we pivot editorial tone ahead of Q4 in preparation for full-alignment post-election.” 

There was even an internal finance spreadsheet that displayed an allocated amount of funding for a ‘special project’, and said allocated amount matched up perfectly with a figure on Stark’s public campaign finance filings that Agatha had cross-referenced. 

To top it all off - because Agatha hadn’t clearly been through enough - there had been an email from her mother that had left her teeth sinking into her lips and wishing that her house wasn’t so full of people that didn’t call it home. 

Stark, 

You know I will do what it takes. If that means she needs to go, then she needs to go. Blood doesn’t get in the way of my professionalism; that’s why you can trust me. 

She chose that girl out of spite for me and I will ensure they are both rectified for their abhorrent actions. No behaviour such as this deserves air-time on my network, nor does it have any business being related to me. 

I will confirm when it is done. 

E.H

Rio had seemed to notice the way Agatha had quietened and the way she fiddled with the pages in front of her. It was nearing two o’clock and they had been at this for hours now. With each minute that passed, she noticed that Agatha’s bite turned more to a resigned murmur, and even she was struggling to maintain her composure. 

“I think that's enough for today,” Rio said. “Nicky will need to be picked up from school soon, and you all deserve to put your feet up. We can have at it again tomorrow, ok?” 

Their encore of supporters had been all too glad to have permission to leave, especially William who looked like he was about an inch away from hyperventilating at still being alive and in the same room as Agatha Harkness. 

Lilia hung back, pulling Agatha into the kitchen once everyone had left. Rio had quietly noticed and taken herself out of the room, clearly pretending to clear away the dining room table whilst her ears were still pointed to attention. 

“What are you doing?” 

“Shush,” Lilia chastised. “It’s my turn to ask questions. How are you?” 

“Brillant.” Agatha spat out a laugh. “Never been better, actually.” 

“Agatha…” Lilia sighed. “We’re going to make sure the world knows the truth, ok? I wouldn’t be here if I didn’t believe that we - that you - could.” 

It took everything in Agatha’s power not to roll her eyes, and even more for her not to break down then and there. 

“I appreciate the sentiment,” she murmured. 

“I’ll go on record,” Lilia’s nod was astute. “I don’t want to work another day for that company unless you are there too. And if you dare call me soppy or a schmuck, I will clip your ear.”

Agatha hoped she would feel relieved when the team finally collected their belongings and left. Instead, there were no words for her to say and not one thing she could think of as a reasonable distraction. She just moved from the dining area to the couches, sitting down with a leg tucked underneath her as she stared into the distant skyline. 

Rio was still busying herself with tidying away the large accumulation of coffee mugs and glasses, the apartment now oddly silent compared to the life within it that morning. 

It was when there was a particularly large clink that left an involuntary jolt run through her body that she realised her cheek was wet. 

She didn’t know when she had started crying, but the moment she was aware of it, she realised that the tears would not stop falling. No matter how often she wiped at her cheeks with her sleeve and no matter how many deep breaths she took, it was as if her body was mocking her. 

She didn’t want to cry in front of Rio, just like she didn’t want to be crying about that woman. 

Just as Agatha had planned a stealthy escape to her bedroom, she was intercepted by a hand reaching for her sleeve and preventing her from moving any further. 

“Hey,” Rio murmured as she turned Agatha around. 

The moment she stared into those brown eyes, her own continued to blur. 

“I just need a second-”

“Mi amor,” Rio sighed, her arms enveloping around Agatha’s body, slack enough that Rio could still look into her face. “Talk to me?” 

Agatha shook her head, burying it briefly into her chin in the hope that her hair would work to cover some of her sadness. 

She should have known it would not work; Rio just kept wiping the strands away and lifting her chin up to get a better look at her. 

“I shouldn’t have brought WIliam in, should I…” Rio sighed, knowing Agatha would not bother to answer her. Instead, as she ignored Agatha’s protests and attempts to get away, Rio guided her back to the couch and sat beside her. “Talk, let’s go. You’re not getting out of this.” 

“Rio… Jesus, I’m fine.” 

She knew her clenched fists and heavy breaths said otherwise. 

“I just really, really want to hit something.” 

Rio looked at her with the most endearing of expressions. “Please don’t hit me.” 

“I won’t if you leave me alone.”

“I’m going to pretend you didn’t say that.” Rio said. “Look,” she reached for both of Agatha’s hands, unclenching her fists and replacing them with her own palms. “If you’re worried about us not actually achieving what we’re setting out to achieve… Well, I get it. I totally do, but that’s not going to happen, Agatha. We have everything we need. We will get her.” 

“I know, but-”

“I’m being serious. I know it’s easy for me to say not to worry, but you have nothing to worry about any of that anymore. It’s all there in black and white. You have done nothing wrong; she has done everything wrong.” 

“It’s not that,” Agatha whispered, her voice threatening to crack. “I just don’t understand how she can… knowing now what it feels like, to have a child, to be responsible for that child… I just don’t understand how she can say those things about me.”

Rio stilled. 

She frowned slightly at the realisation that she hadn’t even considered Agatha could have been affected by that email. She hadn’t even considered that Agatha’s skin was not robust enough to take it - not that Agatha’s skin was not robust. It was the most robust she had ever encountered, and that was why it was such a shock. 

“Oh, Quierida” 

“I knew we never had a relationship. I knew we could never be anything more than what we did have, but I never expected her to actually go this far… I could never, ever do that to Nicky. So, I just don’t understand why she can do it so easily to me.” 

“Hey,” Rio squeezed Agatha’s hand, pulling another loose lock of hair away from her face. “Look at me, mi amor… You are not your mother. You never will be your mother. Nicky is testament to that. You are testament to that.” 

Agatha looked at her, through wet eyes, unconvinced. 

“And no one should ever have to experience this, but I need you to know that you have more than what she has: you have Nicky, you have me, you will, eventually, have the entirety of UBA supporting you. Hell, hopefully the whole industry will be. I know it hurts, but soon you’ll see that there is so much more going for you than simply her ill-affections towards you.” 

Agatha looked up, sniffled slightly, and broke into a small smile. 

“You’re so self-righteous,” she laughed through her tears. 

“You’d prefer me as something different?” 

“I’d prefer you to not always be so correct.” 

“Wow, Agatha Harkness calling me correct. I need a minute.” 

Agatha laughed softly before rolling her shoulders back and taking a deep breath. She needed to shake the bad feelings away, especially when Rio was doing everything to aid her. 

“Can I say something crazy?” 

“I’m sure it will come as no surprise, whatever you want to say.” 

“I want to talk to her.” 

Rio coughed. “Excuse me?” 

“I want to talk to her; my mother. I want to give her one final chance to explain everything on her terms… then I’m done. I swear it.” 

“Agatha…” 

“What could go wrong?” 

“A lot could go wrong, mi amor.” 

“Not with you there.” Agatha quirked her brow. “Think we could make that happen?” 

Unfortunately, they did make it happen. 

It was the last thing that Rio had expected to find herself doing, but as she sat quietly beside Agatha in the back of her car, driven by George, Agatha had to admit, she was impressed. She hadn’t expected Rio to ever agree to her going to see Evanora, let alone accompanying her. 

It had been two days since she had suggested it; two days of back and forth between them both at the time they were ready to turn the lights off for bed, and immediately when they woke back up again. 

They had barely uttered a word to each other in the car. 

Or, Agatha had barely uttered a word. 

All Rio kept banging on about was escape plans, what she should say, what she should not say, and exactly how to contact her if the situation arose. 

Agatha didn’t care. Her mind was a tunnel-vision, focused purely on arriving at her mother’s front door. It was the only place she could guarantee that Evanora would be at this hour, and it also would be the first time she had stepped foot in that palace for at least a decade. 

Evanora Harkness lived in the Upper West Side of the city, in the same brownstone that Agatha had taken her first steps in. The house was older than the television network and had housed every generation of Harkness since their conception. 

It was like walking into a crypt, only the dead things weren’t so well contained. 

“You have some nerve showing up here,” 

Agatha felt sick at the sight of the scrawny, aging woman before her. She couldn’t believe she had ever hoped to feel anything more than hatred for her mother. 

“Oh shut up and let me in before we pay for all the paparazzi’s bonuses this year.” 

With that, Agatha swept past Evanora, her fists clenched and chin held high. She was met with the same overwhelming darkness she remembered from her childhood. Mahogany floors and mahogany walls; moth-bitten drapes and antiques more expensive than most people’s mortgages dotted around in every corner. 

“Let me get one thing clear,” Agatha began as Evanora begrudgingly followed after her into the drawing room. “I don’t want to be here.” 

“Agatha,” Evanora’s lips were pursed. “You are wasting my time.” 

“I am going to give you one chance,” Agatha said. “One chance. Do you understand?” 

“I don’t follow.” 

“I am going to give you one chance to tell me the truth behind your relationship with Stark. Explain to me why you are funneling his money into our company? Tell me why you are aligning with a man who believes in everything our family’s network has stood against for generations?” 

“These are baseless accusations that I know nothing about.” 

“Even if I could produce the documents proving that you are planning to liquidate the company? Documents with your signature on?” 

Evanora stilled. 

Agatha felt herself getting smaller under her mother’s stare. 

Those blue, ice-cold eyes were penetrating her very limbs until she fell to the floor. 

“Agatha, do you have any idea what you are suggesting?” 

No matter how hard Evanora wanted to treat her like she was still a young, naive child, Agatha would not let her. For the first time in her thirty-nine years, she had all the evidence she needed to know that she had never, ever been the problem. 

“Yes, I do,” Agatha stated, her smile tight. “Ironically, you were the one who forced me to go and study journalism. You were the one that forced me to become so well-versed in this lifestyle. So, will you tell me the truth? Are you really planning on throwing our family’s legacy to the Republicans?” 

“Agatha,” Evanora’s voice was unnaturally calm. She started to cross the room, collecting her phone from a nearby counter-top. “Do you see these numbers here? They are contacts of mine.” 

Agatha had no idea where the old bat was going with this. 

“If I wanted to get rid of you,” Evanora began as she took a step closer. “All I have to do is call one of these numbers. In fact, I should expect at least half-price from them now, with how easy you have made it for me to find you.” 

In all honesty, Agatha had truly never anticipated her mother to stoop so low. 

Public humiliation? She understood. 

Wrongful imprisonment? Hell, it wouldn’t involve ending her life. 

And maybe in another life, she would have fought. 

Maybe she would have felt so ready to give up everything, but she had her son waiting for her, and she had a woman waiting for her that she had never expected to want, but needed so damn desperately.

That was when she knew that her mother and herself were different. 

There was a line that Evanora Harkness was prepared to cross, that Agatha Harkness could never imagine even allowing to start to fray. 

“Your own flesh and blood?” 

“We are not flesh and blood,” Evanora hissed. “I should have known you would turn out like this. So weak… so disturbed. And that poor boy of yours… What did you bring him into?” 

“I told you not to speak of him.” 

Evanora’s brows quirked. “Too late,” her mouth formed a sarcastic ‘o’. “I am being serious now, Agatha,” she raised her phone, her finger hovering over one of the contacts displayed on her screen. “Do you really not care about him at all?” 

“You’re willing to kill your own daughter?” 

“I’d do whatever it takes.” 

There it was. 

She assumed it would be the closest she would ever get to an admission. 

Agatha’s lips curled as she slowly backed away towards the front door. “The difference between you and I, mother, is that I will always, always care about my child.” 

She didn’t look back after the words left her mouth. Her mind was on one route and one route alone: getting out of that house, into her car and back with Rio. 

“Drive,” she ordered George as she slammed the door behind her, ignoring Rio’s attempts to get her attention. “George, I swear to god, if you don’t put your back into it, our relationship will quickly run its course.” 

“Yes, ma’am.” 

“What the hell was that?” 

Agatha avoided Rio’s gaze, instead reaching for her phone and dialling Sharon immediately. 

“Sharon? Hi, yes… No, everything is fine. I know it’s so last minute but I wanted to ask if you could collect Nicky from school? Something has come up.” 

She waited for several minutes, batting Rio’s hand away from the phone when she again tried to get her attention. 

“You can?” Agatha’s voice lightened. “Perfect. Pick him up as normal, I’ll let the school know. We’ll be back at the apartment by the time you are… Oh, and don’t stop for anyone until you are standing outside my front door.” 

“Are you going to tell me what the hell is going on?” 

“Darling, stop saying that word. It doesn’t sound good coming from you.”

“Agatha,” Rio’s stare hardened. “What did she do?” 

Agatha’s lips spread thin, reaching for her phone. She held it out in front of her, her finger tapping the screen once before a crackling audio sounded. 

“If I wanted to get rid of you, all I have to do is call one of these numbers.” 

Rio’s eyes snapped up; brown turned to black. 

“You’re willing to kill your own daughter?” 

“I’d do whatever it takes.”



Chapter End Notes
