Chapter 12: Come Together

Chapter Notes

this entire chapter was never supposed to be part of the story but fun fact the mods put on a creators crunch event where we ended up being on call for fourteen hours and this chapter was subsequently born

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Most people remembered their childhood through laughter, fun and togetherness. For Agatha, those things had either been forced or alien to her. The fondest memories she had were when she had upset her mother enough to be locked in her room. No matter the isolation, it always promised a few hours of safety and peace. 

She remembered the sound of the key scratching against the lock of her bedroom door, usually after darkness had fallen and her stomach had long given up on its rumbling. She remembered the way the pace of her heart would quicken to an unnatural degree. 

It was nowhere near as unnatural as her heart felt now. 

She tried not to show it; she knew that remaining calm was paramount when she had a young child to protect, and a woman that she loved, who had never asked to be involved in this dire excuse of a situation. 

The entire way home, her mind flickered between Nicky, and how on earth her mother could do this. She knew that Evanora hated her - that had always been obvious. 

But, she had never expected the woman to want to get rid of her. 

Not when she knew the love of her own child. 

“What are we supposed to do now?” Rio’s face had paled since she had listened to the audio. “We just sit around, exactly where she knows we will be?” 

“She can’t get us there.” 

“Agatha, that is the one place she knows you would be.” 

Agatha shook her head softly, one of her hands briefly resting upon Rio’s knee. “She can’t do anything to us there. It would be too obvious, and the one thing my mother wants more than me dead?” 

Rio’s brows quirked. 

“Her freedom.” 

“I don’t like this.” 

“Rio,” Agatha’s smile was near-gleeful, despite the pit in her stomach pining to take her attention. “You’re missing what I’m trying to tell you. We have it. We have her admitting to wanting to remove me. That is blatant discrimination.” 

Rio scoffed. “It’s blatant homicide, is what that is.” 

“I apologise for my bloodline, darling.” 

“You can apologise after we survive this shit,” Rio murmured. “What… What are we supposed to do now?”

“We get home to Nicky, we stay at home. If you want anything from your place, you’ll have to call Alice to bring it over-” 

“I have an entire drawer of things at yours.” 

“You have one pair of pants and two unwashed shirts?” 

“Yes… they are clothes, aren’t they?” 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I suppose it will suffice for a day or two.”

You’re not leaving my sight until we confirm when, where and how we are announcing what we have found.”

“And how long is that going to take?” 

“Hopefully not long enough for us to both be dead.”

Three days into being hoarded away in Agatha’s apartment - a “luxury, four bedroom and three bathroom penthouse,” she had to keep reminding Rio each time she would complain - she was dealt another blow to the stomach. 

Rio had taken a call just after lunch. It hadn’t been how Agatha had seen Rio take calls before; there was no friendly nod of her head as she answered, nor did she answer it then and there. Instead, she had taken one look at the contact name, dropped her eyes to the floor and made a mumbled excuse before taking herself out onto the balcony. 

At this point, Agatha couldn’t be bothered to follow her out. 

If Rio wanted to run, she would have run by now. 

That was what she had started to learn in the days they had been pent up together. Rio hadn’t left, just like she said she wouldn’t. Agatha had chosen her, and Rio hadn’t left. 

Every day that Rio continued to stay, Agatha trusted herself and her decision a little more. 

And she trusted that whatever Rio was doing outside on her balcony, she would ensure that Agatha was not privy to it in her best interests. 

It didn’t stop the scratching need within her fingers to pull open the french windows and demand to know what was going on but she was able to ignore it just a little easier for now. 

She looked up as soon as she heard the doors reopen. 

Rio was biting at her lip, her shoulders slightly hunched. Her feet shifted awkwardly once she had walked across the room and leaned against the counter to face where Agatha had been making her third coffee of that day. 

“Are you going to tell me what that was about?” 

“Let me see your phone first.” 

“My phone? It’s brand new. Why the hell do you need it?” 

Rio gathered her breath, before holding out her hand with expectation. “Phone.” 

Agatha snarled as she handed the mobile over, watching as Rio tapped in her passcode - the same passcode she had demanded she set herself because it was ‘indestructable’ - and began to divert her attention to god knows what. 

“Rio,” Agatha’s voice was clipped. “I don’t like to be kept waiting.” 

She should have known that would only cause Rio to break into a smile; even she knew she had walked herself right into it. 

“Oh, mi amor,” Rio chuckled before continuing her scrolling. “Don’t remind me of your impatience. I clearly haven’t done well enough to curb that, have I?” 

“Cut the crap, Rio.” 

Rio rolled her eyes, her smiling deepening as her tongue poked against her cheek. “That was Romanoff. We need to delete your email and create a new one. Your old account has been compromised.” 

Agatha almost laughed. 

Almost. 

“Are you trying to tell me that I was a victim to phishing? I am not that stupid, Rio. And I swear to god, if you’re insinuating that I am old-” 

“Agatha, shut up.” 

“Don’t tell me to shut up.” 

“I just did,” Rio’s brow quirked. “And I suggest you listen to me because this is actually, believe it or not, quite serious.” 

“Yes, I know. It was my mother, blah, blah, blah. Tell me something I don’t know..” 

“Agatha, it wasn’t your mother that hacked into your phone.” 

And Agatha, uncharacteristically so, was caught off guard. 

Her hand hovered beneath her chin as she motioned it forward. “Continue.” 

“You received an email on the way back from Vegas, from Nicky’s school. Only it wasn’t from Nicky’s school. As soon as you clicked on that link, they had access to your phone.” 

Agatha stopped still, processing the words before her. Her eyes narrowed, searching the room as she recalled exactly the moment she received that stupid email whilst on the plane. 

“Who had access to my phone, Rio?” 

Agatha didn’t like the way Rio was looking at her, just like she didn’t like people offering her pity. It was a large part of why she kept her life so private. She didn’t need people realising just how many people would willingly take advantage of her, and she certainly didn’t need their damn pity either.

 “It was Ralph.” 

Agatha’s hands braced the edge of the countertop, elbows locked and shoulders enveloping her neck as she released a heavy breath. 

Ralph had gone out of his way to hurt her, again. Ralph had leaked those texts to the press; those photos too. Ralph had been the one to provide the anonymous comment. 

Ralph had known where Nicky went to school. 

Ralph knew where Nicky’s school was. 

“Nicky-” 

It was like a mother bear waking from a slumber only to find a predator circling her cubs. 

“Rio, he knows where Nicky’s school is.” 

“Shit, I’ll call them now.” 

“They know not to let him in - they know, they-” 

“I know. Just to be sure though, ok? I’ll call them, and then we’ll talk.” Rio began to dial the number on her own phone. “In the meantime, mi amor-” she reached out for Agatha’s hand. “Look at me. Good. Focus on me. Ok. If you can, delete that damn email account whilst I’m gone. I will be two minutes.” 

With Rio on the phone to Nicky’s school, Agatha managed to get her shaking fingers to cooperate with her whilst she moved to delete her account. It felt wrong to even touch it, like she was touching him. She couldn’t even understand why he would bother to do this after nearly seven years of minimal to no contact between them.  

“Ok, they’re aware-” 

“I want to bring him home.” 

“And we can, but first, will you let me explain everything that I know?” 

"Whatever you have to tell me, you can tell me in the car.” 

Agatha swept past Rio, or attempted to sweep past Rio, until a hand pulled her back. 

“What the hell are you doing? My son needs me.” 

“Yes, he does. He needs you alive, and the whole point of this staying cooped-up on the top of a skyscraper-”

“It’s not a skyscraper.” 

“Whatever,” Rio huffed. “The point is, you need to stay here. If we both go then what happens if they try something on you? You really want to put that much trust into Evanora?”

“Spit it out then.” 

“Ralph and Evanora have been working together. She connected him to hackers and let him sniff around us at the debate. It was part of her great plan all along to get Ralph back as her main man of UBA. And knowing it would never work between Ralph and you… well, she did what she thought she had to do.” 

Agatha began to consider all of the slow and painful ways she could watch that woman suffer at her hand. Anything to make her feel an inch of what she had thrust upon her own daughter, her daughter’s son, and her daughter’s chance at happiness. 

“How do you know all of this?” 

“William has access to their internal communications, plus evidence that she had been meeting with Ralph behind our backs. Nat couldn’t trace the hackers, but the evidence is all there if you have half a brain.” 

“... Nat?” Agatha almost shuddered. “Seriously Rio?” 

“I’m sorry, that is what you care about most?” 

“I didn’t realise this Natasha was a Nat to you.” 

“Oh give over, Agatha,” Rio rolled her eyes, moving to pick up her keys. “I’m going to get your son, by the way. And don’t you dare step foot outside of this apartment.” 

“Whatever.” 

When the door shut behind Rio, in such a similarly finite way to that day she had slammed the car door behind her, the uneasiness in Agatha’s stomach threatened to lurch into her throat. 

She didn’t know if it was the silence, or that Rio was gone, or that she wanted Nicky, or that she had just endured yet another reminder that there was a concerning amount of people who thought they could control her life. 

Whatever it was, it left her wanting to crawl out of her skin. 

She sat staring at the first draft of script that hopefully would hold enough power to bring her mother down from the godly pedestal she had placed herself upon. It had stared back at her for the last three days after Lilia had dropped off her own notes and copies of evidence in order for Agatha to actually start deciding what she was going to say. 

The only issue was, she had no idea what she was going to say. 

How could she focus on something as mundane as a public speech when her own life had been threatened?

Her concern started when she realised that Rio had been gone for nearly ninety minutes. 

It didn’t take longer than twenty-five minutes to reach Nicky’s school, thirty-five at a maximum in traffic and there shouldn’t have been any traffic; it was barely mid-afternoon.

Her first call to Rio didn’t go through. 

Neither did her second. 

She called Nicky’s school, only to find out that he had already been collected. 

Perhaps Rio had decided to stop off and get Nicky a donut, which Nicky had let slip to his mother that they had done several times already, regardless of how frequently Agatha had reminded her to avoid offering her son so much sugar. 

She paced back and forth through the kitchen, her phone on the counter as she checked it every two seconds before proceeding to slam it down onto the counter again, withholding her want to growl. 

After the fourth time of nearly smashing her phone, it began to vibrate and a withheld number appeared on the screen. 

She shouldn’t pick it up; not after already falling for phishing once. Rio had been the one to warn her herself, but Rio wasn’t here right now and she would be damned if she let anything, regardless of their experience in cybersecurity, from getting in between her and her son. 

She accepted the call, allowing her silence to draw thin and reed out the potential of a sales scam. 

She should have been thankful it never came, but how could she be thankful for that when what happened was worse than she could ever have imagined. 

“Ma’am, we’re looking for Agatha Harkness,” the voice on the line spoke, clipped and professional enough to leave a chill running down her spine. 

“No comment,” she snapped. 

Just as she was about to hang up, she heard those words. 

“I’m calling from the New York-Presbyterian Emergency Room.” 

Emergency Room. 

No, no, no. 

There was no sound after that, only a ringing in her ears that cut off the woman’s voice down the line. She wasn’t in her apartment anymore. The walls were nothingness and everything had a hazy quality to it. She couldn’t make sense of anything but Nicky; but Rio. 

Nicky. 

Rio. 

“Ma’am? Can you confirm that I am speaking to Ms. Agatha Harkness?” 

“What the hell has happened?” 

“Ma’am-” 

“Is Nicky ok? Nicholas. Nicholas Harkness. He’s seven years old. He… He-”

“Ma’am, I need you to confirm your name before I can give you any details.” 

“Yes, this is her,” she managed to breathe out. “Agatha Harkness, speaking. Now tell me what the hell has happened to my son.” 

“Your name was listed as an emergency contact in the phone of Miss Rio Vidal.” 

“Oh my god,” Agatha murmured under her breath. “... Is she ok?” 

“She was in a motor traffic collision and has suffered minor injuries but she was knocked unconscious for a period of time and we cannot release her without her next of kin coming to collect her.” 

Rio is ok, she kept repeating in her mind as she began to taste metal in her mouth. Only when she wiped at her lip and found her fist marred with red did she realise just how hard her teeth had been sinking into them. 

“My son was with her,” Agatha said quickly. “He’s seven. Just under four feet, brown hair, brown eyes. Please tell me he is ok. Please.” 

“Let me check for you ma’am. It’s been hectic here today.” 

Agatha didn’t give a damn how hectic New York had decided to get with its injuries that day. No one mattered more than her baby. 

The wait was agonising, even if it had only been for a few seconds. They might have been the longest few seconds of Agatha’s life as she held her phone under her chin and reached for her keys, insurance cards and anything else she could think of. 

The sight of Nicky’s stuffed rabbit stopped her dead in her tracks. 

“Ms. Harkness?” 

“It’s Agatha,” she snapped. 

“Apologies, Agatha.” 

Fuck you and your apologies. 

“Would your son have been wearing spider-man socks?” 

Of course, Rio had let him wear those stupid socks this morning. 

She decided, in that moment, that she would let Rio dress her son in whatever goddamn way Nicky wanted to be dressed. 

Fuck the uniform violations. 

Fuck her mother. 

Fuck any threat against her. 

Nothing was more threatening than being the two people she loved most who had been carted off to hospital. 

“Yes, that’s him. Is he ok? Is he conscious?” 

“Yes, he’s ok,” Agatha let out a breath so severe, she considered it may have been her last if the news had been anything different. “He told the doctors his name, but we had to get it verified from you. He’s hurt his arm, but nothing too severe.” 

“I’ll be there immediately,” she snapped. “Do not allow anyone else to enter his room unless it is me. Am I clear? Anyone claiming to be a family relation of his must be refused entry.” 

“Yes, Ms Harkness - Agatha - apologies. Please bring proof of identification with you.” 

She ended the call, realising quickly that she was still standing in front of Nicky’s stuffed rabbit. It was still in the same place on the sofa as he had left it discarded that morning, back when he had just been a child and not the hit and run target someone else had decided he should be. 

Her cheeks were hot and wet without even realising that she had started to cry. The corners of her eyesight were blurred as she reached for the rabbit - Scratchy, as Nicky had so affectionately named him after an unfortunate run-in with Lilia’s pet cat. 

She ignored Trevor in the lobby, knowing he would understand from the mania in her features, and hailed down a cab to the hospital. 

On her way, the only coherent thought she could act on was to text Lilia. 

Agatha Harkness: Nicky and Rio are in hospital. This has gone too far now. Book in the press conference date immediately. 

Lilia Calderu: Don’t tell me that it was because of who I think it was. 

Agatha Harkness: Law Enforcement are waiting for me to explain, but go figure.

It took three separate people that Agatha had to scream at before she was taken to the room that now housed her son. Her sweet, innocent little boy. He lay in a hospital bed that only emphasised just how small he really was, his hair a little more tousled than usual and darkening purple flecks of skin appearing against one of his cheeks. 

He was talking to a nurse when she appeared at the door; Agatha had overheard the words “tricerotops” and “extinction” mentioned with his usual giddyness as he giggled with the nurse. God, she hadn’t realised how beautiful the sound of his laughter was.  

“Nicky?” 

His head snapped up into his mother’s direction like it was a siren call, an indisputable bond between flesh and blood. His smile widened. 

“Mama!” 

“Baby,” she rushed over to the side of his bed as the nurse offered a small smile and stepped back. He held out one arm, the other resting by his side in a white cast. She enveloped his body within her arms immediately. “God, I was so worried about you.” 

“I get to pick the colour of my cast, Mama!”

“Nicky’s been really, really brave. Haven’t you, buddy?” 

Nicky nodded at the nurse before nestling his head back against Agatha’s chest. 

“He’s got a fractured wrist. Someone will be in soon to get it properly plastered, and a doctor will discuss his recovery going forward, but it should be nice and easy. Maybe a couple of days off school, huh?” 

Agatha didn’t think she could hold Nicky any tighter, but she tried nonetheless. “Thank you,” she said to the nurse. “And his head? He’s going to be ok?” 

“He’s been scanned, everything came back looking great. He just needs to rest for a while.” 

Once left alone, the tears started falling again. 

She didn’t care. 

She had her boy in her arms and that was all that mattered. 

She just hoped Rio would understand why she couldn’t be with her too. 

After thirty minutes of cuddling, a second check-up from the nurse, and one conversation with the doctor, Nicky’s breaths had evened out against her chest thanks to the pain medication she had consented for him to be given. 

She had pleaded with a nurse to stay with him and call her the moment Nicky was as much as stirring in his sleep, and found herself finally on her way to Rio’s room. 

Rio lay on the gurney looking slightly more out-of-it than her son had looked. Her eyes were half-lidded, her hair angled in all directions across the pillow. There was a nasty gash to the side of her forehead with stitches visible, and her neck was braced in a way that Agatha already knew she would not hear the end of Rio’s complaints about it. 

Agatha’s breath hitched the moment hazel met her eyes. It was the way Rio’s lips curled slightly, her eyebrows pinched as the movement ached more than she had anticipated. 

She didn’t wait a second longer. She was by Rio’s side, reaching for her hand and perching against the bed before she could take her next breath. 

“You put me as your emergency contact?”

“‘Hi Rio’,” she mumbled. “‘It’s so nice to know you’re ok, Rio’.” 

Agatha sighed, her free hand tentatively tracing the outline of her bruised jawline. “You put me as your emergency contact?” 

Rio’s cheeks reddened slightly, shrugging her shoulders and then hissing as she did. “Alice refused to be mine. Said she picked up enough of my shit, and that she didn’t want to deal with you when you found out that you weren’t it.” 

“You know, she’s growing on me.” 

“Is this how I get you to start liking my friends? Getting hit by moving vehicles?” 

“Something like that,” she smirked. “You fucking terrified me, Rio.” 

“Wasn’t my intention.” Rio released Agatha’s hand, instead, moving it to swipe a lock of hair behind her ear. “How is he doing? They wouldn’t tell me anything… I’ve been so worried.” 

Agatha’s smile was as genuine as an Agatha Harkness smile could be. 

“Asleep, for the moment. He’s getting a cast which seems to be the highlight of his day, so don’t think we’ll be worrying about any immediate trauma there. He was worried about you too. Wouldn’t stop going on about how you had passed out with him in your arms. Kept saying, “she protected me, Mama”.” 

“Wouldn’t have done anything else,” Rio’s smile was weak. “And George?" 

“He’s ok. Extremely apologetic, has some whiplash,” Agatha shrugged. “Remind me to double his bonus this year.” 

“I was worried about him,” she murmured. “Agatha… I’m so sorry.” 

“Honey…don’t,” Agatha’s response was immediate. “You don’t need to say that. It wasn’t your fault. You saved him.” 

“If that bastard had looked where they were going-”

“Rio,” Agatha reached to take her hand back, her tone dropping. “It was targeted. Whoever did it, she sent them. They fled the scene, of course, but they were in an unmarked, unregistered vehicle. She has her dirty prints all over this.” 

“She’d do that with a child in the car?”

“It was me that was supposed to be in it. That’s the first time it had left the building in three days. Nicky had been taken to school and back by Sharon each day… It was meant for me.” 

“I’m going to fucking kill her.” 

Agatha’s lips curled slightly. “Not before I do.”

She didn’t think anything was a wake up call like it was seeing the two people she loved most laying, injured, in hospital beds. She had known that she was the only one who could put a stop to her mother, but nothing had made it more clearer than being phoned up by an ER telling you that your son and girlfriend had their lives put at risk. 

Wait. 

Were they girlfriends? 

They had never discussed that. The past week since Agatha’s confession live on-air, and consequential suspension, had left her too busy to think of anything so mundane. 

But knowing that she could have lost Rio, and that Rio would have been, technically - on paper - nothing to her… the thought was nearly as horrifying as it had been to see her unable to move in her hospital bed. 

She made a mental note to revisit that thought at a later date, when her life hadn’t turned into playing personal assistant to one genuinely shaken up adult, and a small boy who was milking the fact that his arm was in a cast as much as he possibly could. 

Her two sick-notes had been discharged from hospital two days before under strict instructions to rest for one week and do little else. Lilia, Jen and Alice had been over at all times of the day and night, each bringing hoards of cooked meals, a new lego set for Nicky and another new lego set for Rio. 

Rio had done everything in her power not to sit still. She wasn’t being out-done by a hyperactive seven-year-old, which was something Agatha had not expected to learn about the woman. It was enough to confirm to her that she was absolutely never having a second child. She didn’t need one; she technically already had one, even if they were a thirty-four-year-old with a successful (and temporarily on pause) career. 

“Agatha!” 

That damn noise had been Agatha’s soundtrack of the last seventy-two hours. It was constant; if it wasn’t Rio, it was Nicky. She told herself each time that she would much rather be running at their beck and call instead of planning their obituaries. 

“You’re not having another pop-tart, Rio. Do you have any idea how much sugar-”

“Hey,” Rio held her hand up as Agatha walked into the room. She was flat against the couch with Nicky curled up on the adjoining side, his head bruised into Rio’s shoulder as they watched endless re-runs of nature documentaries. Agatha could swear she would be dreaming of David Attenborough’s voice at this rate. “You’re stressing me out. Doc said to avoid stress at all costs.” 

“Mama, don’t stress Rio out.” 

Rio smirked. “Yeah, what he said.” 

“Hey,” Agatha turned to Nicky, leaning over to poke her finger under his arm until he squirmed. “You’re not allowed to side with her. We’ve discussed this; I birthed you.” 

“Mama!” 

“I’m not trying to steal your son’s loyalty, I just want a fresh soda.” 

Agatha rolled her eyes as she swiped Rio’s cup into her hand. “You’re going to rot your teeth.” 

Nicky wiggled himself up from the couch, puffing out his chest and fluttering his lashes. “Can I have one?”

“Absolutely not,” Agatha shook her head. She looked at Rio as she walked towards the kitchen area behind the couches. “You,” she pointed with her finger, “need to stop rubbing your sugar addiction off on my son.” 

Whilst in the kitchen, Rio began shouting for her again. 

“For fucks sake,” she muttered under her breath. “What!” 

“Your phone, Mama!” 

Agatha reached them, fresh soda and equally as fresh a water for Nicky in her arms. 

“Yeah,” Rio smiled up at her, eyelashes fluttering against her cheeks as she held out Agatha’s ringing phone. “You’re phone, Mama.” 

Agatha scowled at the name, ignoring the god-awful heat pooling in her stomach. It vanished as soon as it had arrived, the moment she saw Lilia’s name on her screen. 

“Tell me something good, Calderu,” Agatha spoke through gritted teeth whilst half-heartedly trying to wipe at a squirming Nicky’s sticky cheek. 

“I have a date.” 

“As lovely as it is that you trust me with your love life, I have more pressing issues-” 

“No, would you just hear me-” Lilia paused, and then proceeded to take an evidently long breath that Agatha had the pleasure of listening to every heave and crackle. “I’ve got a date for the press conference. Next Monday; it’ll be two weeks since your suspension. I’ve got several confirmations of attendance already. Can you be ready by then?” 

Rio was looking at her, eyes asking too many questions for Agatha to compute. 

She nodded without remembering that Lilia couldn’t see her. “Absolutely.” 

“Good,” Lilia said. “Remember to read the deeds to the building. If you want it done outside UBA, you better make sure that Evanora won’t have people standing there pointing a barrel down my face. Oh, and how are they both doing?” 

Agatha looked between Nicky and Rio, both looking up at her with expectant grins. “They’ll be fine,” she said as she glared into both of their eyes. “I’ll talk soon. Servant duty calls.” 



Chapter End Notes

had you panicking for a second there, didn't i?

Chapter 13: Grounds For Divorce

Chapter Notes

if you follow me on twitter then you'll know i've been banging on about the song 'grounds for divorce' by elbow for months and it is the song that inspired this entire fic but i couldn't use it as the title because people would think this was a divorce fic lmao. but all of the huge 'gotcha' moments in this fic have this song playing in the background to them

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The end was nearly in sight, and it was a terrifying prospect. 

You could argue that every moment in Agatha’s life had built up to these very few days, she just had never known it. 

Each slap she had taken, each night she had been locked in her room without dinner. Her entire education and career laid out carefully in front of her before she could walk. The sham of a marriage that she hadn’t had the courage to say no to. The life she tried to build for her son, knowing it would always be impossible because of the family he had been born into. 

All she had to do was stand up in front of the world that she had been shunned from. 

No big deal. 

“How are you feeling?” 

Rio was up and walking now, brace off her neck and bruises faded to the smallest tonal differences against her skin. Nine days post-accident, and Rio had been reeling to get her revenge as soon as she had managed to walk to the toilet on her own. 

“Like I don’t know whether to vomit or laugh,” Agatha murmured as she busied herself with getting breakfast ready for Nicky. It was all she could do: pretend the world wasn’t about to set ablaze around her. “I just can’t believe the end could be tomorrow.” 

Two weeks on from her suspension; two weeks since she was threatened to have a hit placed on her; two weeks of silence between her and her mother. 

Within that time, Evanora Harkness hadn’t just threatened her daughter. She had threatened the little boy that Agatha breathed for, and the woman that she was starting to learn she needed just as much. 

Thankfully, enough time has passed to lull Evanora into a false sense of security; it was just enough time for her to see that Agatha hadn’t bothered to try and one-up her mother for a final time. 

In return, Evanora had kept up her promise of complete radio silence, even if her threats still loomed over all three of their heads each day. 

She only hoped that this would be the last of those days. 

It had taken their team long enough to decide how they would even go about the grand-finale of their investigation: releasing it to the public. 

There had been discussions about hijacking another broadcast, until Agatha and Lilia both reminded everyone that Evanora wouldn’t think twice about cutting them off on-air as soon as she caught wind of them being in the building. 

They had considered just publishing the documents with an accompanying video, but Rio had quickly put the idea down after seeing disappointment behind Agatha’s eyes. 

Agatha needed something she could truly sink her teeth into. She needed a statement that said: you are not getting rid of me that easily, and whilst I’m at it, don’t you dare come for my family again. 

Family was the only inevitable outcome Agatha saw in this situation. Or more so, the only one she clung to in order to keep her getting out of bed each day. 

That was why, in under twenty-four hours, Agatha and Rio would be taking to the street, outside UBA’s building just off Sixth Avenue. 

Lilia, Jen and Alice had each spread the word of their press conference to all their media contacts apart from Eagle News. 

Agatha had wanted to ensure their message to their rival news station where her ex-husband happened to be the face of, was clear enough to know they were not welcome. 

If they were lucky enough, they may even get a surprise cameo from Evanora herself. 

Agatha didn’t mind; she had sifted through hundreds of pages of deeds and documents just to confirm that her mother did not, in fact, own the street as well. 

There was only one thing standing in her way: UBA’s board members. 

A committee of billionaire philanthropists, esteemed journalists who had retired, and savage business men nearing their sell-by date. A committee that - up until that day - were none the wiser of the company’s CEO’s plans to restructure the work they had put their entire pensions into. 

The only issue was that Agatha, despite having known most board members since she was learning to speak, had been suspended and subsequently shunned from having anything to do with UBA. Given that each member of the board was at least double her age, she had little faith in any of them feeling overjoyed to return her call. 

Nevertheless, she tried. 

Two of them had gotten back to her. One, a woman who Agatha was aware of, had a history of submitting tips to TMZ and Page Six. She promptly decided there was no need to bother her with this illustrious news unless she ran out of other options. The second was a man that went by the name of Gaz, despite his formal title being Sir Gerald Huntingoton, III. 

He was one of the last people she had expected to want to engage with her. 

Gerald - or Gaz, however Agatha couldn’t face allowing that combination of letters to leave her mouth - had agreed to meet her at the bar in The Langham. He was a tall, round man with rosy cheeks and a softness to his features. Agatha noted that he wore a tie of several shades of orange; an accessory she wouldn’t expect from such an esteemed socialite. 

The second thing to surprise her were the two glasses of whiskey on the rocks, in crystalline glasses upon the small circular table between their armchairs. She had expected a glass of wine, perhaps a gin and tonic. She hadn’t anticipated that he would think she was capable of drinking such strong alcohol but it gave her a good indication of the man she was about to meet, and she considered that maybe this wouldn’t go as badly as she initially feared. 

With the knowledge that her new companion didn’t take her entirely for a fool, she allowed her shoulders to ease back into the leather whilst she crossed her navy, pinstripe-suit-covered legs. 

“Sir Gerald,” she nodded curtly as she placed her handbag down beside her chair and reached for the glass. “A pleasure.” 

“Agatha, please,” his chin found his neck as he raised his glass to meet her own. “It’s Gaz. You’re not in pigtails anymore.” 

“Unfortunately not,” she murmured. “I appreciate your time. It seems most board members… well, let’s say they’ve made their decision on who they think I am.” 

Sir Gerald chuckled to himself, his head shaking as his cheeks turned pink. “No, no,” he had profused. “Not me. What you have done is admirable. If I had the courage to do so myself at your age… Well,” he sipped his drink, “I would be in a much better place today.” 

That had been the general consensus with most that had interacted with Agatha post-outing. Anyone who had bothered to give her the time of day, did so because they also understood what it felt like to have some part of yourself on show for others to judge. 

He allowed Agatha to explain everything that she had been investigating into, about her mother, about Tony Stark, even about the alleged-hacking from her ex-husband which she wished she did not have to call ‘alleged’ because she knew damn well that it was true. 

After one more drink together, Gerald clapped his hands together before holding out an arm for her to shake. 

“You have my full blessing. I will go to the board - I will share these documents with them, and I will alert them of the press conference. What you are doing…” He took a deep breath, his fingers ringing together in a way that Agatha would not expect from somebody of his calibre. “... Well, I am behind you the entire way. And I will make sure the board is too, otherwise they are not a board I want to be a part of.” 

She could only hope that the rest of the board would align their views with his own.

Fat lot of luck she had whilst she was portrayed as the lying dyke she absolutely - maybe - was not.

Agatha never wanted to live the night before the press conference again. She would be amazed if she came out on the other side unscathed, let alone still breathing. 

She had done everything in her power to curb the itching in her fingers and restlessness in her legs.  

She had explained the logistics behind times-tables to Nicky three times already, but he could not grasp his little head around what happened when you wanted to multiply something more than ten. 

She had spent forty-seven minutes in her dressing room, eyeing up the endless racks of clothing and questioning what the hell she could wear that following morning. It needed to be professional, classy not but not too in your face, and it had to be heterosexual enough that she didn’t look like she was trying to make a statement, whilst also alluding to an air of liberalism that didn’t leave her looking like a raging member of the far-right. Plus, it had to leave her looking fucking fantastic. 

She had ended up nearly falling asleep as she held Nicky, his breaths even against her chest whilst they laid in his bed post-bedtime story. She had been in there so long that Rio had knocked on the door softly to check she was ok, before managing to convince her to come to her own bed. 

Eventually, she had followed Rio down the hall and into her bedroom. What was once a carefully-curated set of oaks and beiges had turned into what she could only describe as what she expected Nicky’s room to look like when he started walking around the house with headphones and deciding that it was too awkward to call her ‘mom’. 

Since the crash, she hadn’t given a damn about Rio’s mess. Mess? What mess. She had Rio sleeping in her bed each night, alive and breathing. Her son across the hall, alive and breathing. She truly did not give a damn anymore. 

Being there, enveloped in a darkness that eased her mind and the warmth of Rio’s arms around her waist that reminded her she had nowhere else to be, was honestly all she wanted. She was able to catch her breath a little easier each night before bed, no matter how hard it was for her to actually sleep. Unfortunately, she still hadn’t worked out the magic remedy for quelling the constant whir in her mind. 

“Agatha,” Rio’s sleepy tone met her ear. “I can hear you thinking.” 

“That’s physically impossible,” Agatha had muttered back.

And when she thought sleep had finally overcome Rio, she was proven wrong not thirty-minutes later. 

“Baby,” Rio whispered into her ear, in exactly the softness that they both knew had Agatha squirming beneath her.

She hadn’t had anyone call her that before. The first time Rio had said it, she had pretended not to hear it. The second time - the time that she knew it wasn’t a mistake - Agatha had demanded she repeat it again, and again, and again, until it was nearly the only term of endearment that Rio would use with her. 

“You’re just going to look tired for the cameras tomorrow,” she murmured. “You’ve already won. Come on, we both know that.” 

“We don’t know it until she has no access to that place, there is no threat on Nicky’s life and you and I are both back in our chairs.” 

“Soon, mi amor.” Rio wrapped her leg around Agatha’s hip, fully enveloping her back against her chest. She began to trail her fingers gently across Agatha’s arm with just the perfect amount of softness that she had learned was one of the only things that would send Agatha off to sleep. “Can I tell you something?” 

Agatha groaned softly against Rio’s arm that her head lay above. “If I’m not going to like it, then no.” 

“I mean, you’ll probably want to hit me, but it’s not a bad thing for me to say.” 

“Will it get you to shut up?”

Rio chuckled from behind her; her breath warmed Agatha’s neck. “Yes.” 

“Fine,” she grumbled. 

Rio moved gently, her neck still slightly tender, as she pushed herself up to place a kiss against Agatha’s arm, then to the side of her cheek, and then on top of her head. “I love you,” she spoke in the softest whisper, the words threatening to get lost in the darkness. 

Agatha’s breath hitched. They hadn’t said that to each other yet. Not explicitly. Not if you didn’t count Agatha’s dramatic confession on live television in front of the entire nation. 

“... Rio,” Agatha’s voice was quieter now, a breathless laugh escaping her throat.  “How the hell am I supposed to sleep after you say that to me?” 

“You just told me to shut up, I’m not saying anything else.” 

Agatha groaned again, laughing as she gripped onto Rio’s arm even tighter. “Fine.”

“Fine.” 

Before she allowed her eyes to close for what she hoped would be the final time that evening, she considered whether she truly loved Rio too. She had been thinking about it in her head long enough. The woman’s dirty clothes were in her laundry basket, just like her pantry had been stocked full of snacks she wouldn’t let Nicky be caught dead with. She had taken it all in her stride, because despite how much she may seem to kick up a fuss about it, she knew it would leave the biggest void in her heart if it were to disappear. 

So she whispered back to Rio in the dark before placing a ghost of a kiss against her wrist. 

“I love you too.” 

Agatha managed to get four hours of sleep which was more than she had gotten in one stretch over the last fortnight. She woke, still in Rio’s arms and realised that this was the day. 

The day. 

No turning back after this. 

The outcome of that day would determine the future of her family’s legacy. The future of her own legacy. Most importantly, it would determine how many people wanted to trust her over her own mother. 

She had little hope in regaining the peoples’ support, but she hoped what she had to say would deter them from siding alongside Evanora even so. 

It was odd. It may have been the first thing on her mind upon waking, but it wasn’t the thing that kept returning to plague her thoughts. No, instead her mind wandered to what Rio had told her the night before; what she had in-turn, told her back. 

She wondered if Rio had meant it. Perhaps she had been dreaming? Perhaps Agatha had been so delusional from lack of sleep herself that she had made it up entirely. 

Her movements were precise as she unearthed herself from Rio’s arms and turned over to face the sleeping woman beside her. Each time Rio exhaled, her breath would cause a loose strand of hair to float back and forth against her nose. She looked so serene. 

It wasn’t fair that she looked so at peace when Agatha was experiencing the current crusade fighting inside her head. 

“Wake up,” she poked at Rio’s cheek repeatedly until, at least sixty seconds in, a groan finally sounded in-between what had been very intermittent breaths. “Oh, good. You finally decided to grace me with your presence.” 

“Agatha, what are you-” Rio squinted from the light poking through the curtains, pulling the pillow over her face. “It’s too early.” 

“We need to get up. Don’t you dare go back to sleep.” 

“I’m going back to sleep,” Rio mumbled, her voice muffled. 

Agatha swiped the pillow clean off Rio’s face, resulting in a high-pitched whine as Rio realised what had happened. Before Rio could protest, Agatha was diving - as gently as she could manage, given her body had taken a rather large hit only just over a week before - on top of Rio until her body completely covered her. 

“Agatha!” Rio hissed as she received an elbow to her neck. “What the hell-” 

“Shush,” Agatha whispered, her face so close to Rio’s that their breath tickled each other’s skin. “Can I ask you something?” 

She looked down, her eyes glancing over the freckles that peppered Rio’s nose. They were barely visible to the eye which meant that Agatha was one of the few people to know they existed and that thought left her feeling very satisfied indeed, and even more aware that she intended it to stay that way. 

Rio opened one eye, looking entirely unconvinced with her decision to do so. “What?” 

“You could sound a bit happier.” 

“You just woke me up when I clearly said-”

“Whatever,” Agatha rolled her eyes before a smirk appeared. Her hand clasped at Rio’s jaw, ensuring she could look in no other direction. “You know what I said last night?” 

“What did I say last night?” 

“You know what I said last night.” 

Rio’s lip curled. “I do,” she teased. “But I want to hear you say it.” 

Agatha couldn’t help it. The moment she felt heat in her cheeks, she buried her face into Rio’s neck and groaned. “Don’t make me say it!” 

“Fine,” Rio huffed, her hand reaching to bring Agatha’s face back up into her direction. “What did you want to ask me?” 

“Well, when you said what you said to me last night…” 

“That I love you?” 

Agatha nodded, closing her eyes when she felt her cheeks burn again. “Yes,” she sighed. “Does that mean I’m your girlfriend?” 

And Rio laughed. 

Actually laughed. 

Laughed to the point that spit was flying onto Agatha’s skin. 

“Jesus Christ, you can ask me to be your girlfriend, but you can’t say you love me?” 

“I’m not asking you to be my girlfriend!” Agatha clambered off Rio, crossing her legs to sit right beside her. “I’m asking if you are my girlfriend.” 

“Where has this all come from?” 

Agatha shrugged her shoulders, her head bowed slightly. She didn’t need Rio seeing the woman she had woken up next to looking like a strawberry for the third time that morning. 

“Just was thinking about what there is…” she looked up into Rio’s eyes, her own expression more sincere than it had been since she had woken. “... What there is for us after all of this. Everything we worked for, all of that brought us together. And now we’re just… I don’t know. We’re going to lose that.” 

Rio sat up quickly, reaching for Agatha’s hand and holding it against her chest. “Mi amor, we’re not losing anything. You are most certainly not losing me, if that is what you’re worried about. I got hit by a vehicle for you.” 

Agatha’s face broke into a laugh. 

“You can’t get rid of me now,” Rio continued. 

And Agatha tried to believe her, just like she tried to believe Rio every time she would tell her that “everything is going to be fine today”, even if she had ended up saying it over ten times before they had even gotten dressed. 

Agatha wore a dress - not for appearances sake, but because she actually wanted to. She wasn’t going to be fit into a box that predetermined how many piercings and tattoos she had, whether she only wore pantsuits and if she was going to get a buzzcut or not. 

She was still Agatha Harkness. 

Nothing would change that. 

It was a dress with an open collar down to her mid-section, tight at her waist and gently flowing against her legs in a deep navy. She allowed her hair to curl down past her shoulders, one front piece pulled back across her ear. The usual gold of her earrings were on show, complimenting the necklace her son had bought her last mother’s day - courtesy, of course, by Sharon’s prompting. 

Rio was, of course, unapologetically herself. If she wasn’t allowed to be on this occasion, then she wouldn't be allowed to be anywhere else. So today, apparently, would be the day that she debuted some small-spectacled sunglasses, her side bangs framing her face in a way that meant, annoyingly, she pulled the look off. Complete with a molten amber biker jacket and black pants that were made to look like they refused to touch the skin of her legs, the pair of them together looked quite the show. 

At least, Nicky had told them as much. 

“Wow,” he had said, looking them both up and down as he waltzed into the living area with several action figures balanced in his arms. 

Rio’s tongue poked against her cheek. “Too much, kid?”

Nicky shook his head. “You two look like the bad guys in a movie.” 

Rio looked at Agatha, trying to hold back her laughter. “I guess that’s what we were trying to go for?”

“Absolutely,” Agatha said. She bent down to Nicky’s level, her finger prodding against his nose until he squirmed away and she settled for a kiss against the top of his head. “But, we’re the good guys today, honey.”

Sharon arrived to look after Nicky and both women said their goodbyes before venturing downstairs to meet with their new - temporary - driver, and security detail that Agatha had insisted on employing, even if Rio had rolled her eyes every time she laid eyes on the burly men.

“If you wanted a bodyguard, mi amor, you could have just asked me,” she had told Agatha the first morning that they had arrived after the car collision. 

Agatha had quickly told her that she could play bodyguard when she didn’t need help walking to the bathroom anymore. 

She had been able to relieve herself independently for four days now; Agatha was secretly disappointed that there had been no talk of roleplay from the woman as of yet. 

Then again, there were more pressing issues to consider than their next venture in the bedroom, but she promised herself she would fly Rio and herself to the tropics and indulge in an entire week of it with her afterwards. 

They hadn’t spoken much in the car; Agatha didn’t think she was capable of it as she was sure she had swallowed sawdust. Their hands clasped one another at their laps and that was enough. 

Agatha had already demanded to the driver that they be dropped off down a quieter street around the block. Everyone would be waiting for them, including the security she refused to do this without. 

Besides, if they had parked up outside UBA, they would have made it too easy for Evanora and that was the last thing that woman deserved. 

“Wait a moment,” Rio said as they pulled up at the side of the street, Agatha already gathering her belongings. “I just wanted to say, no matter what happens-” 

“Whatever it is, can it not wait thirty minutes?” Agatha sighed, but sat back in her seat when she saw the look on Rio’s face, even if her leg was tapping erratically against the floor.  “Seriously, Rio?” 

“Oh shut up and let me talk for once,” Rio shook her head in disbelief, but she was smiling nonetheless. She reached for Agatha’s hand, her thumb brushing over the skin of her knuckles. Their eyes locked, staring into each other knowing that these were the last few moments of quiet before everything might change. “I just wanted to say, before we go out there-” 

“I really don’t need a pep talk, thank you very much.” 

“Shut up, Agatha!” Rio laughed again. “What I’m trying to say is, regardless of the outcome today, I wanted you to know that nothing changes how I see you, or how badly I want you. And, I really would like you to be my girlfriend… If that was still an option?” 

“Oh…” Agatha exhaled deeply before a smile crept up on her lips in tandem with the rouging of her cheeks. “That could be arranged.” 

They stared at each other; they both laughed; they both leaned in at the same moment until their lips found each other’s warmth. 

Agatha found herself hoping that Rio’s lips would only ever be touched by her. 

“So that’s a yes?” 

“Of course it is, you idiot.” 

And finally, when Rio got out of the car, there was no slamming of her door. Only an outstretched hand and gentle kiss to Agatha’s temple as she helped her out onto the street.

She had expected perhaps five to ten journalists if they were lucky. 

She hadn’t expected for the entire corner of the street, and path down the block, to be filled with crowds of cameras and microphones. 

There was an anticipation in the air that she had only become too acquainted with over the last fortnight. An anticipation that was impossible to decipher if it meant danger or not. 

They had to move quickly. It wouldn’t take long for some loyal UBA minion to clock the hoards of crowds outside their building. In the space of five minutes, Agatha had been getting out of the car and now found herself being walked up to a makeshift podium, on an equally-makeshift podium. 

Agatha was a proficient public speaker. It had been part of her life and career for nearly two decades, and there had never been a fear associated with it. But stood there now, hundreds of familiar faces looking up at her with something unreadable in their expression… 

She just knew that she had to do this right and that they had to believe her words. 

She just had to be a damn good journalist. 

And how couldn’t she be? 

She already had one of the very best, right at her side, and she was ready to take down every fucking person who had tried to hurt her, and the people she loved. 

Rio’s hand rested at the small of her back. It grounded her enough to cough, check the microphone was working and finally speak the truth. 

“I know I am not the world’s most popular person in light of recent situations I have found myself involved in. I know you may doubt my integrity, just like I know you are here today in the hope of discovering something new and shiny about my life,” she gathered herself, briefly looking towards Rio who just nodded her head sincerely. “But I ask you, today, not to be here for the next tabloid headline. Instead, I ask you to be here as a coalition, a group, a team of journalists, to protect our profession, and to protect our integrity.”

“I ask this of you because I have uncovered, along with my team, a host of concerning evidence to suggest that if Tony Stark - the current front-running Republican presidential candidate - is successful, he plans to reshape the news industry as we know it today.” 

There were some gasps, some obnoxious sniggers and several dropped jaws staring up at her now. 

“Not only this, but my mother, the CEO of UBA, is working in allegiance with Stark and has committed to liquidating UBA of its assets and becoming the prime news station that Stark will use to censor news across the United States of America.” 

The dropped jaws gradually got lower. 

“Our investigation has spanned over several months. We will be publishing a full and in-depth presentation of the accusations and evidence currently present in this case. Take your time to dissect this information at your own accord,” Agatha continued. “But first, I want to take a moment to share my side of the story. As you will know, I was publicly outed against my will just over two weeks ago now. Following that, I was given a choice directly by my mother. That choice included either going on-air and denouncing that I could ever be…” she took a deep breath, realising that she had never actually said the word out loud before. “That I could ever be gay, or losing my job and having my life defamed against my will.”

She looked at Rio again, who pressed against her back a little harder. 

“I was suspended due to my sexuality and refusal to comply with pretending to be somebody I am not. And the truth is, I had already lived that life for thirty-nine years and I was ready to live it for longer, until I realised that I was part of a corporation that was leaning towards targeting people exactly like me, and exactly like my girlfriend.” 

More gasps sounded in the crowd. There were several news stations with a full on field production crew, taping their recording live to their station. Every single person had eyes on Agatha and every person was listening with full intention. 

Rio was her girlfriend. 

Everyone knew Rio was her girlfriend. 

It wasn’t as scary as she thought it would have been. 

“Yes, I am a Harkness, and yes, I was in line to take over the company. Whether that stands true is up to you, and what you do with the information we are about to give you.” Agatha took one more deep breath. “Evanora Harkness, after corroborating with Stark, laid out the plan for the infrastructure of their far-right news dictatorship and included in those plans, was the liaison with journalist Ralph Bohner, who they believed to be the ‘perfect’ host for the demographic they intended to appeal to. The same Ralph Bohner that is my ex-husband. The same man that I was forced into a marriage with. The same man that threatened the life of myself, and my newborn child. That man - put up to the task by my own mother - sent me an email that downloaded software onto my phone that enabled my private, internal communications to be hacked. That man, and my mother, and a future presidential candidate, all agreed that the best course of action to take any heat away from themselves, was to publish my secrets.” 

Rio’s entire arm was across her waist now, her fingers flexing against the material of Agatha’s dress. It helped her to breathe a little easier. 

She couldn’t believe she had just told the world that. 

She assumed Ralph’s abusive past would get more heat than the threat to their entire industry, but it was a step in the right direction nonetheless. 

Agatha looked to Rio, signifying her turn to take over. 

“We are here to present the basic facts. And let it be known,” Rio’s eyes darkened along with the tone of her voice. “These facts are a damning display in dictatorship, censorship and discrimination that our network usually prides itself on standing firmly against. We’re going to start from the beginning, back in December of last year, when Wanda Maximoff’s abrupt resignation from the company was announced.” 

Agatha noticed Lilia at the corner of their make-shift stage, Jen and Alice at her side. She could have sworn that Lilia’s eyes were glistening, but the woman quickly swatted her hand in front of her face when she noticed Agatha’s stare. 

“Wanda Maximoff did not resign,” Rio continued. “Her contract was terminated with immediate effect by Evanora Harkness. This was after the CEO had made a private agreement with Stark, back in October last year. In exchange for funds and security in Stark’s pending-presidency, UBA would become politically-aligned with Stark in every way Evanora could manage. In light of this decision, Maximoff’s Russian heritage - a nation Stark has publicly declared his distrust for - meant that she was simply removed from the company. This is a blatant act of discrimination against an honest journalist who has since had all allegations dropped by officials.” 

Agatha watched Rio, and could not help but think of how fucking lucky she was to have that woman by her side. She had half-expected her, at some point, to reveal she had been working for YDA this entire time; that she was just another industry plant to add to her game, but no, she had stuck by Agatha’s side at every moment. 

“We have since uncovered documents that suggest many other employees are set to be unlawfully terminated from the company. Myself and Agatha, as you both know, have already been suspended. In our published evidence, you will find an audio recording of her threats and indisputable acts of continued discrimination regarding this suspension. You will also find the redacted list of employees set for termination.” 

“That is not the only evidence we have. You will find, once uploaded, evidence of private internal communications between Evanora and Stark discussing their agreements and plan to infiltrate the news industry, Evanora and Ralph Bohner discussing how they can publicly shame Agatha and get her removed from the company, and Evanora and her senior executives and producers, discussing exactly which news segments they will cut from airing on the show because they did not align with Stark’s political views.” 

Agatha’s hand reached for her microphone again, her eyes locking into Rio’s as she received a tight nod. You got this, Rio was saying to her. 

“Dating back to last year, you will find evidence of Stark funneling undisclosed funds into UBA subsidiaries through shell companies, among public donations that match up with a list named ‘undisclosed special project’ that Evanora was preparing for the network. You will find documents with redacted segments that were supposed to be aired on our show that could not be because they were directly opposing what Tony Stark’s manifesto outlined.” Agatha’s lips were pursed, her eyes hardest on the crowd before her. She was getting into a groove now; everyone was attuned perfectly to what she was saying, and there wasn’t room for her to make a mistake. “You will realise that all of these push towards Evanora’s end goal: to create a new television network under Stark’s censorship. This is a direct violation of the First Amendment." 

Rio took hold of her own microphone, coughing slightly before continuing. “And let us be clear on one thing,” she said. “Tony Stark has shown that he will so readily control our right to present news exactly as it should be: transparent and objective.” 

Agatha stepped forward herself. “He has displayed the tenacity he possesses in order to defy the very Amendments that make our country into what it is today - an institution that, yes, has a long way to go, but still, will always be fairer and kinder to all than any institution led by him.”

That was when the commotion started. 

It began in a far corner of the crowd. Agatha only noticed from the sudden shouts, jeers and faces turning around to inspect the disruption. She turned towards Rio, who looked equally confused. Beyond her, Alice and Jen were moving towards the security guards to enquire further. Lilia simply looked at them both on the podium and nodded for them to continue. 

“Wrap it up, ladies,” Lilia hissed.

But before they could continue, a cry shouted out in the audience, followed by what could only be described as a raucous moment of miscalculation. 

Agatha may have joked about it, but the last thing she had expected to see in front of her was the face of her own mother. It was a face that she hadn’t seen on Evanora in many, many years. It reminded her of when she had snuck out at the age of fifteen for an evening with her friends from high school, only to be picked up by her family’s driver and transported right back in front of the very face she was staring at now. 

And once Evanora had reached the front of the crowd, her own security detail around her, and all the surrounding journalists giving her their dirtiest looks possible, Agatha could only laugh. 

“You have some nerve showing up here,” Agatha said, a smile creeping up into her features. “Especially after you tried to kill my son, and my girlfriend.” 

“What?” Agatha smirked. “You don’t have anything to say to that? I thought not.” 

Rio had stepped closer to Agatha, blocking the path that Evanora had straight towards her, even if there were at least five body guards swarming them concurrently too. 

“If I still have all of your attention,” Agatha looked to the crowd, still obediently keeping their gaze with her. “Then I would like to let you know of the recent occasion that my own mother thought it was acceptable to commit homicide, just to get what she wanted for her company. Evanora Harkness paid-off an organised crime group to put a hit on my life. In doing so, she had unknown, professional individuals watching my every move post-suspension two weeks ago. The one day that my partner, Rio, agreed to collect my seven-year-old son to school after we discovered that his father - who we still hold a restraining order against - had discovered the location of my child’s whereabouts, Evanora Harkness allowed for her men to instigate a road traffic accident. My girlfriend, and my son were both in the car at the time of the collision. Thankfully, they are both still here to tell the tale.” 

Perhaps she should have led with that fact, because the moment it had left her mouth, the crowd was shouting and jeering in Evanora’s direction as her security detail tried to ward them off. It happened too quickly for Agatha to work out exactly what had gone on, but one moment her mother had stood in front of her, and the next she had vanished. 

“We cannot allow this coercion to occur at UBA, or any other television network for that matter. That is why I stand before you today, denouncing my own family legacy. That is why I ask for your help in spreading our message so far and wide that Stark is not allowed to ever reach the White House, and Evanora Harkness can never set foot inside UBA again.” 

And quickly, Rio was stepping forward. Her movement was gentle as she prised the microphone back into her direction, giving Agatha a look that she already knew meant trust me. And she did; she trusted Rio implicitly. 

“And whilst we’re on the matter,” she stated. “I want you all to ensure that Ralph Bohner is known to the world as the abusive cunt that he is,” there were several more gasps from the crowd at Rio’s profanities, but Agatha only nodded for her to continue. “And that he is never allowed to work professionally again, let alone believe that he has the right to access my partner, and her child.” 

Jen had reached to gently grasp the back of Agatha’s dress, just enough for Agatha to turn around and realise she was telling them that they were running out of time now. 

“Thank you for your time today,” Agatha’s smile was composed. “Our evidence and investigation will be online immediately following this press conference. Please, share it. Talk about it. Allow this to never die down. It is only your profession at risk if you decide not to.”

Their press conference had been breaking news on every channel in the US, and several internationally. Agatha had expected a few people to pick it up but she had never anticipated the entire world being interested in what she had to say. 

Between leaving the press conference and arriving back at her apartment, everything had been a near-blur. She faintly remembered congratulations from UBA staff, from her direct team, from Rio herself, but the first time she began to think coherently was the moment she walked through her front door and heard Nicky’s excited squeals at her arrival. 

“I watched you, Mama!” 

Nicky had sprinted through the hallway, his socks sliding against the hardwood floor as he slammed into her hip and clutched her tightly. 

She hadn’t anticipated the tears to start falling. 

But with Nicky clinging to her, and Rio wrapping an arm around them both, she couldn’t stop them, no matter how much she wanted to. 

“Mama was so good, wasn’t she bud?” 

Agatha looked up at Rio, mid-embrace, and laughed between her tears as Rio reached to wipe them away. 

When Nicky looked up, between them both, Agatha cupped his cheek with her hand before placing a kiss to the top of his head. “You watched us, hm?”

“Mama, you sad?” 

“No baby, of course not,” she said quickly. “Happy tears, I promise. I think I need a vacation after al this. What do you say? Fancy getting away to a beach?”

Nicky’s face brightened, jumping up and down on his toes. “The beach? Yes, yes, yes!” 

And so it was settled. 

Rio clenched her arms around both of them, tightly. Agatha breathed them in, realising that she had finally done it. 

In the hours after she had stood up against her mother, they had nearly broken the internet. 

Every media outlet, every social media page, every person that was anybody, was discussing what had been broadcast live to the world that morning. They had trended on X for hours. They had both gained hundreds of thousands of followers. Each of their publicists had been calling them non-stop with engagement updates and press and media opportunities. 

Most importantly of all, the SJIP - Society For Professional Journalists - and the Department of Justice had been in direct contact with Agatha, not one hour after the conference. 

They wanted to set up a meeting for the following week. 

Agatha agreed without a second thought. 

And after that? 

After that she received an email, signed by every single member of the board committee at UBA. 

Dear Ms Harkness, 

What you achieved today was profound. 

You have our backing and support, entirely. 

We would love to discuss this further with you, immediately. 

With our trust,

The UBA Board Committee 

She couldn’t fucking believe it.

Chapter 14: Farewell To The Fairground

Chapter Summary

Six months later... what are Agatha and Rio up to?

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

If anyone had told her how arduous it would be to run a broadcasting empire, Agatha would have ensured she actually carried out her endless threats to her mother about calling up the national children’s helpline to take her away when she had still been a minor. 

It was exhaustive, to say the least. 

To think her mother was going to force this life upon her. 

It would have been just another one of Evanora Harkness’ cruelties added to a list. She would have always claimed she was just toughening her daughter up for the job, and Agatha could clearly see why now, not that she could ever imagine she would endorse doing it to her own children. 

Hypothetical, pluralled children, that was. 

“Ms Harkness, your 2.30 has arrived.” 

She looked up from her desk to find William shuffling his feet in the doorway to her office. 

He had opted for neon green nail polish that week, and it was all Agatha had been able to focus on. It was infuriating but the least she could have done was let him keep his job after he had decided to get his dick rubbed by an old executive who happened to have access to every piece of evidence they had needed to take Evanora and Stark down. 

“It’s already a quarter too, Teen.” Agatha hissed before slamming her notebook down onto the mahogany wood of her desk. “And you were sure to tell them that I have to leave by 3.15, yes?” 

He nodded quickly, his eyes bowed to the floor. 

“Useless, incompetent…” she sighed. “Assholes. Ok, let them in.” 

Agatha had quickly learned that her days in the job meant mind-numbing meetings with balding, male pensioners who believed they could get away with sweet-talking her, whilst single-handedly ensuring the satisfaction of over one thousand employees, and hundreds of clients that paid said employees salaries through their advertisement deals. 

There had been days where she understood that Evanora may have been driven to insanity by the endless demands and conflicting opinions, but there had not been one single day in her six months on the job, that Agatha Harkness felt like she had the right to impose on an entire nation’s rights to their freedom. 

There had never been a day where she considered disowning her own son for who he chose to be, just like there had never been a time in his entire life that she had restricted what he could, or wanted, to do just to suit her own desires. 

The meeting had just been yet another nothing-y meeting. She could have been home by now, back to where her life truly mattered. 

“Ms Harkness!” 

Once her clients had left, and she was packing up her briefcase, William had proceeded to scream her name three times in the space of five minutes. 

“What?” 

“You’re being called,” William called back, his words in a sing-song tune. “Again.” 

Agatha appeared behind the boy, heels clacking against the executive level floor. “I’m off now, they can wait. Make sure that the flowers I sent out have been delivered in the next hour. Are we clear?” 

“Yes ma’am.” 

“Oh William,” Agatha chastised. “Never, ever call me that again.” 

His cheeks turned an obtrusive shade of red. “Yes, Ms Harkness.” 

Her face cracked into a softer, simpler smile. Her eyes truly met his, holding his stare for several seconds. “I’ll see you later, ok?” 

William’s exhale was obvious, even if he tried to hide it through a returning smile. “Of course,” he nodded. “I’ll be out of here in an hour, and then… yeah. See you.” 

“Good,” Agatha said. She started to walk down the hallway, pausing just before the elevator. 

“Oh, and William?” 

The boy - man - child - boy? She still hadn’t worked it out. Whatever he was, William turned to look at her again, nodding. 

“There should be something for you waiting back at your apartment.” 

She didn’t stay to wait for his reaction, she had better places to be. 

By 3.45pm, she was pulling up outside her building back in the West Village. She thanked George for the journey home, bidding him a good break in his shift before she saw him again that evening. 

Trevor was waiting at the door, smiling as wild as anything. He bowed his cap towards her as she offered her pleasantries and kept her walk brisk until she was in the elevator towards her apartment. 

The moment she opened the door, just as she now received everyday, a small, four-foot-two, rabid wolf in the form of a child bowled into her legs. 

“Baby, let Mama get through the door first,” Agatha sighed, laughing under her breath nonetheless. Her boy and his bright eyes looked up into her eyes as his arms clutched around her waist. Her face softened, a hand wiping the hair from his eyes. “Hey, honey.” 

“Hi,” he grinned, bouncing on the tips of his toes. “I missed you. Do you still have to go out tonight?” 

Her heart dropped. She hoped he hadn’t been thinking about it all day. 

Ever since the collusion Nicky had been involved in, he had been more clingy with his mother than Agatha could have imagined, or hoped for. Especially for a boy who had just turned eight. She had expected him to be cooped up in his room on video games at this point, but there wasn’t one moment that she had complained about him doing the opposite. 

“I do, honey.” Agatha held him close, crouching to place a kiss to the top of his curling locks of hair. “But Sharon will be here, and I’ll be here when you wake up in the morning.” 

His smile faltered briefly, before he nodded and let go of his mother. 

She watched him, standing in front of her as if remembering where he had misplaced something. It made her longer days worth it just to come back to that tiny face with his tiny cogs working in his not-so-tiny brain. 

“Oh, I forgot,” Nicky’s smile widened. “I’m supposed to show you something.” 

Agatha’s breath hitched before she spluttered out a laugh. “Are you?” 

Nicky nodded astutely. “Come on.” 

He held out his hand and Agatha didn’t think twice before taking it. 

When Nicky led her to his playroom, she hadn’t expected to come face to face with a dungaree clad, sweating and extremely exasperated version of her girlfriend. 

She sat on the floor, cross-legged, boxes stacked high around her and books, games and toys surrounding her in a mess that hurt Agatha’s eyes to look at. 

Agatha didn’t know what was worse: the state of the room, or the state of Rio. 

“Why the hell have you not been answering your phone?” 

Agatha’s hands wrapped around Nicky’s ears. “Language,” she hissed. “And why the hell are you not getting ready?” 

“I will be ready before you and we both know that.” 

“No you will not.” 

“Yes, mi amor, I will be. And anyway, we’re supposed to be moving out in less than a week… I think we need to have a conversation about our priorities again.”

“Darling, that’s what the movers are for,” the corners of Agatha’s lips curved into a smile as she looked down to find Nicky giggling too. “They’re coming on Tuesday.” 

Rio’s mouth was left agape. “You can’t be serious.” 

“You were with me when I booked them!” 

“If you’re talking about the other night when you forced me to watch that housewives crap with you, I was clearly asleep.” 

“You grumbled each time I asked you a question.” 

“Agatha!” 

“Rio’s been working hard, Mama,” Nicky said with conviction. “You should give her a kiss at least.” 

“Oh?” Agatha quirked her brow, bending down to Nicky’s height. “You really think she deserves that?” 

Nicky nodded. “Definitley.” 

“Fine,” Agatha smirked. “Only because you said so.”

She would do anything to have that woman over every inch of her body right now, but she had to remember: small, small child in their vicinity, and a prior engagement to attend tonight. 

Later that evening, however, she was sure there would be no holding her back. 

“Hi,” Rio breathed out heavily as Agatha pulled her into her embrace, blue meeting hazel, just like they did when everything was right. 

Agatha couldn’t wait. Her eyelashes beat against her cheeks once before she was leaning in, her lips finding purchase against Rio’s. She could taste her saltiness that only left her mouth dry for more. It was sweet yet possessive in one. Tongues gentle and the skin of their chins scratched by fingernails. 

Agatha exhaled once they had pulled apart, her already-swollen lips curving into a smile. “Hi,” she whispered. “I think now that you know you don’t need to keep packing boxes, you should get into packing something else.”

“Mama, can I help Rio pack?” 

The two women broke apart, both momentarily forgetting the little ears and eyes at their attention. They immediately shook their heads at the boy. 

“No honey,” Agatha bit into her teeth to hold her laughter back. “I think it’s movie time, huh? Whilst Mama and Rio get ready.” 

Of course, Nicky was overjoyed at the perspective of watching a movie so early into the afternoon. He didn’t mention a single other thing, apart from several questions about whether he should opt for Ratatouille or The Incredibles, leaving Agatha and Rio to escape to their bedroom and get at least thirty minutes together before they actually, definitely needed to begin getting ready for the evening.
