She wore a dress of two halves. Its top was a black, off-the-shoulder and asymmetric against one hip, whilst the skirt was a pleated white chiffon. The gold badge of her belt complimented that of her necklace and rings, and her hair was loose in light, bouncy curls. 

Rio didn’t need to tell her she looked good for her to know she did. 

She had made sure that her outfit for that evening served to remind everybody in attendance exactly who she was, as a journalist, as a mother, and as a woman. 

There may also have been the briefest consideration that she should, naturally, remind Rio exactly who the woman was that chose to stand on the end of her arm.

“Shame,” Agatha smirked as she clipped her earrings in. She watched Rio in the mirror, smirking. “You may have gotten a kiss for it if you did.” 

Rio pouted before making nonsensical noises of protest, until eventually she frowned, dropped her shoulders and appreciated the vision of the women before her some more. 

“I genuinely don’t know what I did to deserve to be in your company.” 

Agatha shrugged. “I mean, that vibrating strap helped your cause. Maybe if you use it again when we get back, I’ll consider keeping you around.” 

“Querida, we’re moving into our own home next week. You cannot get rid of me.” 

Agatha turned around, facing Rio with a pointed chin. “It has five bedrooms. Don’t think I’m above forcing you into your own.”

She’d be lying if she said it didn’t annoy her to see Rio laughing in disbelief. 

“Come here,” Rio held out her hand, crossing the room until she was close enough to smell that signature lemon, rose and patchouli scent that was only brought out for “rooms that deserve it” as Agatha had put it. 

“You wouldn’t last a night without me,” murmured Rio as she gently traced her nail against Agatha’s shoulder, knowing it was the only place acceptable for her to touch anytime after Agatha’s hair and makeup was complete. “Especially if I was only down the hall.” 

“You sure you don’t want to find that out first?” 

Rio’s tongue poked against her cheek. “Shut up and kiss me already.” 

So Agatha kissed her; Rio kissed her back and Agatha proceeded to prise herself away the moment Rio’s hands began to wander. 

“You’re still in a towel,” Agatha’s eyes were stone. “Get dressed. Now.” 

It had been Rio that they ended up waiting for, just as Agatha had concluded. 

Agatha waited by the front door, reapplying her lipstick after covering her boy in goodnight kisses and passing him off to Sharon, as she thought of all the insults and means of getting Rio back for her extensive time-wasting habits. 

But she was forced to eat her words the moment she heard the sound of heels clicking against her marble floors. She could feel Rio before she saw her, or perhaps it was her smell that hit her first. It was the same smell that she recognised from the first night they had shared together - hints of cedar and sandalwood, an odd note of coriander that drove Agatha insane the moment it hit her nose. 

When she turned and saw what her girlfriend was wearing, she contemplated giving up on them leaving the house altogether. It wasn’t an outfit worthy of other people’s eyes, so perhaps she should rip it off the women whilst she still had the chance. 

She had never seen this outfit before, and it was different to what she was used to seeing in her girlfriend’s wardrobe, and it may have been causing her to feel slightly feral over it. 

Rio's outfit was all-black, but far from the usual suit she tended to choose. Her black pants fell loosely over pointed heels instead of the typical boots or brogues she wore. Her top had Agatha salivating; a satin collar around her neck with billowing black mesh that flowed until it cinched in at her belt. The sleeves were shoulderless, showing off the tanned, silk skin of her arms that Agatha needed her tongue over every inch of. 

And her hair? Agatha had never seen Rio’s hair like that. She looked like a different person. No, she still looked like Rio; a different version of Rio. 

She had slicked it back into a ponytail which showed off her dark features and annoyingly-glowy skin that Agatha envied each day. Sure, there were a few flyaways; she had quickly learned that the woman’s hair was hard to control no matter how fine it looked. 

Rio didn’t often wear much makeup, and she wasn’t wearing much now, but her eyeliner offset the deep amber of her eyes, and her cheeks were just slightly blushed enough to highlight her freckles. 

Agatha was snapped out of whatever spell she had been put under by the sound of a cough, then a laugh, and then: “like what you’re looking at?” 

And goddamn this woman, she was doing the stupid tongue-poking-against-cheek thing that she knew drove Agatha crazy. 

“I was going to shout at you,” was all Agatha could say. “I was going to shout at you and now I can’t do that because you look like that,” she threw her hands out, flustered. “You’re late and you look fucking hot.” 

“Thank you,” Rio smirked, stepping closer until there was no space between them. She turned them both to face the mirror in the hallway. “We look like we’re off to a funeral.” 

“If only,” Agatha sighed, continuing to look at their reflections. “I mean, I guess you could say that we are, actually.” 

“Oh? Planning to do something you haven’t disclosed to me tonight, Harkness?” 

Agatha scoffed. “Please, you really think I’d risk doing something that caused me to end up in a cell besides my mother? I just meant… Well, this is the last of this stupid, draining, but quite incredible chapter. After tonight, we never have to think of what we almost lost ever again.” 

Any sadness over those thoughts quickly vanished the moment Rio’s lips found the side of her neck. Agatha arched into it; Rio’s touch was muscle memory now and her skin practically craved it when she had gone too long away from her girlfriend’s presence. 

“I’ll miss it because it gave me you,” Rio murmured after her lips had departed. “But we’ve got so much good to focus on. Like that Space Invaders arcade machine you said I could buy as a moving-in gift?” 

At that point, Agatha was rolling her eyes and shoving Rio out of the door before she could add anymore to her already-too-long list for what would be going into hers and Nicky’s game room in their new home. 

If anyone had told Agatha Harkness last year when she stood in the ballroom of the Plaza Hotel that she would be attending the following year with Rio Vidal by her side, she would have most likely tried to spit in their drink. 

It had been one year since the night that had kick-started the downfall and reclamation of her truth. It had been the beginning of the end, and she only wished that she could go back and tell herself that the end would never be the end; it would just lead to something better. 

This year, it was her name at the head of UBA’s table. The CEO of the company and co-leading anchor of The Morning Show, sat beside her girlfriend, with the people she trusted most sat amongst them. Lilia had peppered them both in kisses at their arrival, Jen gushing over Agatha’s outfit whilst Alice had offered a curt nod and Agatha had returned it because, unfortunately for Rio, she doubted that her relationship with Alice would ever go further. Even William had been invited - a gesture of goodwill, Rio had reminded Agatha when she had begun to organise the RSVPs earlier that month. 

Her industry colleagues greeted Agatha with warmth and respect now, with little attention to the fact that Agatha had attended with Rio at her side, to which she greatly appreciated. It wasn’t that she wanted to hide Rio - no, that was never the case - but with the last thirty-nine years lived in the shadows, she wasn’t exactly ready to walk around in rainbow coloured tights and a badge that said raging dyke. 

“And to present our next award,” the announcer said from the stage, “please welcome Wanda Maximoff!” 

Nearly every head in the room towards their table. 

Nearly every face on their table turned towards Agatha. 

And rightly so, because what the fuck? 

Wanda was supposed to be on the West Coast. Wanda was supposed to be living out her newfound peace in San Francisco, anchoring for a local, sleepy news station whilst getting to spend most of her time with her infant twins. 

Wanda Maximoff was not supposed to be in New fucking York. 

“Um,” Rio’s confusion sounded to her left. “Did you know she was going to be here?” 

“Not a fucking clue,” Agatha murmured back. 

Despite the shock, it was incredible to see her friend again in the flesh. They had kept in touch over the phone, but to see Wanda here, knowing how much had changed in the past year for both of them… It was nice. Really nice. 

“Hello,” her bubbly, nervous tone spoke through the microphone, adorning a simple, green dress and low heels. “Now if any of you are shocked to see me here tonight, just know, it was an even bigger shock to me that I was allowed back into the city. 

She received a host of laughter from the audience. 

“I’m glad I was allowed back, because my job tonight is quite important,” she continued. “This last year, journalism and its longevity has been under threat. It has reminded us all just how important truth is to our profession, both internally and externally. And I would say that no one knows that better than I do, but it wouldn’t be true.”

Rio’s hand found Agatha’s upon the table, a finger gently caressing against her knuckles until her palm spread and Rio’s fingers interlocked into each of her own. 

“Because there are two individuals in this room that do know its importance better than I.” 

For fucks sake. 

Agatha did not like where this was going. 

“Already having received a Pulitzer Prize earlier in the year, our recipients of this next award have demonstrated, down to the very fibres of our profession, what it means to be a journalist.” Wanda paused, taking a breath. As she did, murmurs began to surface across the room. “Not only did their investigation shake the industry to its core, but it struck the hearts and understanding of people from every corner of the world. Even when matters of their personal lives were used against them, they continued to stand for what is right. Even when their lives were threatened, they bent over backwards to let the truth be known.” 

Lilia, Jen, Alice and William had their eyes locked on Agatha and Rio, each of them displaying a knowing smile that only served to piss Agatha off even more. 

This could not be happening. 

The Pulitzer had been enough; she had been ready to call it a day after that. 

“They didn’t just stand up for journalism, they stood up for the welfare of our nation,” Wanda continued. “Which is why, on behalf of the National Journalism Awards, I am proud to present the Excellence in Investigative Journalism award to Agatha Harkness, and Rio Vidal.” 

The applause was raucous, complete with shouts, jeers and even several wolf-whistles. Agatha didn’t quite know what was happening, she just knew that this could not be happening to her. 

But it was happening to her, and both of Rio’s hands were reaching for her cheeks, turning her head and pressing her lips against Agatha’s own, slightly pursed, extremely confused lips. Even their kiss was close to a blur and next thing she knew, she was being hauled through the audience and up onto the stage. 

Thankfully, being reunited with Wanda was enough to snap her out of her daze. She hugged the redhead in a way that would likely leave the crowd dumbfounded because they had actually just witnessed Agatha Harkness hug somebody. 

“You kept that quiet,” Agatha murmured into her ear as they parted their embrace. 

Wanda laughed, then winked, then shrugged her shoulders. “I’m so fucking proud of you,” she turned to Rio. “And you. Thank you for keeping this one in check for me.” 

Rio smirked. “It's tough but I’m happy to oblige.” 

Wanda placed kisses to both of their cheeks. “Now go up there and say thank you.” 

Rio did the first part of the talk. She had always been good in situations she was unprepared for. It was as if the noise of the audience could leach into her mind and force words out. 

“Wow,” she laughed into the microphone. “This was unexpected, but then again, this past year has been unexpected. Actually, fun fact for you all, this time last year was the first time I properly met my now-girlfriend. I’m still debating if that makes it the best or worst night of my life.” The audience cackled. Agatha rolled her eyes. “But it is safe to say that I would not be standing up here right now, if it weren’t for who she is down to her very bones.” 

Agatha felt the warmth creeping up on her cheeks and found herself regretting not consuming the remainder of her negroni before leaving the table. 

“This woman,” Rio turned to Agatha, her eyes glinting and smile wide. “Well this woman cares more than any person I have ever met before. I have never met a more tenacious, vigorous and thoughtful human being than I have in Agatha Harkness-” 

Agatha’s heel kicked against Rio’s ankle. 

“... And I’m going to let my lady do the rest now before I am in the dog house tonight.” 

The audience laughed once more as Rio pulled Agatha in closer to the microphone on top of the podium. “We don’t have a dog, but we sure do have a spare bedroom,” she spoke as she eyed Rio out of the corner of her eye. 

“Look,” she exhaled. “This was a surprise, a really, really nice surprise but it wasn’t all down to the two of us. There is a team of incredible human beings, and dear friends of ours that put their own careers on the line to ensure this investigation could ever even see the light of day. Without you Lilia, Jen, Alice and William, Tony Stark would likely be set to win the election in just a few months. Without your help, Evanora Harkness would still be building a professional environment built on lies and corruption. And without your help, I would struggle to sleep at night knowing that Ralph Bohner was still walking the streets of this city as a free man. So for that, I am forever indebted to you.” 

She felt Rio’s hand at the small of her back and found herself leaning further against it, and Rio supported her weight, like she always would. 

“And to every one of you in this room that believed in our story,” she took a deep breath. “I just want to thank you for accepting me for who I am, and allowing yourself to choose the truth.” She nodded once, looking beyond the stage. “Thank you.” 

The response was profound. 

Every person in the room stood to their feet, clapping and cheering. 

The applause continued as Wanda led them both off stage, Rio’s arm wrapped securely around their award, and Agatha’s waist. 

It took at least an hour to get through all of the congratulations from strangers, colleagues and friends at the ceremony. Everyone had something to say; everyone re-offering their support once more to them both. 

Back at their table, four very smug grins were waiting for them. 

Agatha glared at Lilia. “You knew?” 

“Darling, who do you think managed to convince Maximoff to make her great return?” 

She opened her arms and stole Agatha into an embrace, and Agatha let herself melt into it, just this once. 

“I’m so proud of you,” Lilia murmured against her shoulder. “Of you both.” 

And they laughed some more, celebrated some more until the awards had all been given out and the crowd turned to the bar and dancefloor. 

“Mi amor,” Rio leaned in, her words warm against Agatha’s neck as they sat at their table and took it all in together. “I can’t believe it has been a year since I first fucked you.” 

Agatha couldn’t help but scoff. “Honey, I was the one that fucked you if I recall correctly.” 

“Hey, at least you got an award out of it this time.” Rio smirked before beginning to hum with ignorance. “And, I’ll be sure to change that narrative of yours once we’re out of here.” 

“You can’t say that and expect me to wait.” Agatha reached for her phone and quickly typed something before slamming it back against their table. “George is arriving in fifteen.”

Next week, their alarm would sound at 3.30am. They would wake, no doubt with Agatha forcing Rio out of bed. They would drink their coffee and watch the skyline awaken before sharing a kiss and leaving the building to share truth with their nation. 

Next week, they will move into their own home. A space shared and built on love, and nature documentaries, and too many pop-tarts for Agatha’s liking. 

Next week, they would say goodbye to the chapter that had brought them together and instead, walk into a new one, with a giggling eight-year-old and an entire television network under their name - or Agatha’s name, but she planned to change that. 

Speaking of that… 

“Oh, I forgot to show you this…” 

The room was sticky with sweat and the aftermath of their ravaging of each other’s skin post-awards-cereony. Agatha’s hair fanned out against Rio’s torso as she scrolled on her phone and Rio’s fingernails grazed against the skin of her bare chest. 

“Jesus fucking Christ.” Rio had stolen Agatha’s phone, looking at the screen with wide eyes, re-reading it over and over again. “Baby, are you sure I’m not hallucinating?” 

Agatha laughed softly, her head shaking back and forth against Rio’s naked skin. “The settlement went through today,” she said. “It’s all done. Every last penny is mine. Or Nicky's. Or ours. Whatever you want to call it.” 

The press conference had been the catalyst that spurred multiple federal investigations into UBA. The network narrowly avoided liquidation, with the board and shareholders agreeing to a civil settlement that covered Agatha’s wrongful suspension, reputational damages and her family ownership stake in the company. 

Evanora? Done for conspiracy, fraud, obstruction of justice and a whole host of things that Agatha, simply, could not be bothered with. 

Stark? His campaign had collapsed under federal scrutiny, along with his support and hope of ever setting foot inside The White House. 

Ralph? Like the coward he was, he had accepted a plea deal. He lost his job, lost his reputation and lost any remaining access to Agatha and Nicky that, at one point, he believed he still had. 

It wasn’t the money that Agatha had blown up her entire life - as she had known it - for. It was the confirmation and knowledge that the apple had fallen far from the tree. 

Agatha was not her mother, and she never would be. 

It was vindication at its finest.

“I’m like your sugar baby,” Rio smirked, her eyebrows wiggling suggestively. 

Agatha hummed. “You’d like that, wouldn’t you?” 

Rio’s hands began to trial through Agatha’s hair, in the exact way they both knew would have Agatha submitting to anything Rio wanted. “I should at least get a cut. I’m the reason you had the balls to go up against her anyway.” 

Agatha couldn’t help but roll her eyes in response. 

“You can take all my money if you let me take your name.” 

Rio spluttered. “What did you just say?” 

Agatha shrugged her shoulders. “Harkness has… well, bad connotations.” 

“You’re being serious?”

In fact, Agatha considered that she may have gone insane. Then again, her and Nicky were currently the only two Harkness’s to not be dead or in prison. 

She nodded, her smile warm nonetheless. “I think Nicky would quite like to become a Vidal.”

“Nicky would also like a husky, which I’ve had to remind him that you will not allow, every morning for the last week.” 

“What can I say?” Agatha’s face was smug. “He has my tenacity. Plus, I can practically hear my mother screaming from her cell at just the thought of her precious name being tainted by another.” 

Rio sat up, pushing Agatha up along with her until they both were sat, cross-legged with the flimsiest of sheets between their laps. “... So you want to marry me?” 

Agatha pretended to think about it, and offered one final shrug before her lips curled into a wry smile. 

“If it stops you from walking around telling people that you’re my sugar baby, I’ll walk down that aisle towards you tomorrow morning.” 

Rio’s face broke into a grin. “I am so holding you to that.”

“If it stops you from walking around telling people that you’re my sugar baby, I’ll walk down that aisle towards you tomorrow morning,” Agatha quirked her brow. “Are you interested?” 

Rio’s face broke into a grin. “Interested in you? Always.”
